- NABH preparation calendar

- Date  19th Jan -102  Pest control, painting exterior of building , Core Objective elements -Word by Word list of all the  Core Objective elements as a list to be extracted from 3 rd edition aug 2022 Guidebook to NABH accreditation standards for small healthcare organisations (Documentation) [102 core OEs](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1-gQ2as0km94pykyB0u-PrkfV4Z-kWDDWnqNB5a2wAxE/edit?tab%3Dt.0%23heading%3Dh.5maz4pkqu61z&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180816867&usg=AOvVaw0CzSwJ1UUgWB7mRWQ5EiV8)
- Date  20th Jan \- SOP, registers, Files. Labelling signages, Formulary,NOT IN USE Room / Labelling of crash cart - Savita, Emergency Contact , Patient dress, bedsheets, patient wrist ID band, Oxygen cylinder tag Diagram: Cylinders (Empty / Part / Full) status indication.\- triage tag in caulaty, Numbers:Lift and each staff - Diksha
- Date  21st Jan \- Patient files  -On bed IPD files And 5 patient IPD files in each speciality in last 3 months
- Date  22nd Jan \- DIscharge summaries in Last 3 months - Implant and Instructions when to immediately contact hospital
- 23rd Jan Previous NCs  work on atleast 50 of them
- 24th to 29th  \- staff training including code training -Training:Code: 1 day Training

Department wise training -Department Heads:

- Casualty - GNM, MBBS Doctor  Komal Nurse, - check Defibrillator, ecg and monitors Dr Sachin will organise the casualty
- Front office - Diksha will answer all auditor’s questions
- Pharmacy – Vishaka & Ruchika will answer all auditor’s questions
- Laboratory – Diggesh will answer all auditor’s questions
- Radiology – Nitin will answer all auditor’s questions
- ICU, Ward  - Nursing – ICN Aman brother will answer all auditor’s questions, Sonali
- OT & Cathlab Aarti and Kunal will answer all auditor’s questions
- Nephroplus – Rakesh will organise- GNM nurse to be posted in Nephroplus
- Code Blue - training Shiraz will answer all auditor’s questions
- HIC (Hospital Infection Control) – Aman Brother will answer all auditor’s questions
- HR  - Gaurav Jagruti will answer all auditor’s questions
- MRD  -  Dr Sharad will answer all auditor’s questions,  Kashish
- BME Atul and Aman Rajak will answer all auditor’s questions

- Savia and Ruchika :Label  - crash cart

- No Expiry drugs should be seen in the hospital
- High Risk Medication list has to be put up in Pharmacy, OT and ICU
- LA SA (Look-Alike, Sound-Alike medicines) list has to be put up in Pharmacy, OT and ICU
- Narcotic drugs locker
- Emergency drugs and equipment check list

### Part 1: The Patient's Journey (Chapters 1-5)

Imagine a patient named Alex entering a hospital...

1. AAC (Access, Assessment and Continuity of Care)

- Story: Alex Arrives at the Counter.
- Memory Hook: The first step is always access and assessment.

2. COP (Care Of Patients)

- Story: He is greeted not by a doctor, but by a COP (policeman) who tucks him into bed.
- Memory Hook: The Cop provides the Care.

3. MOM (Management Of Medication)

- Story: The Cop realizes Alex needs pills, so he calls Alex's MOM.
- Memory Hook: Mom always manages the medication.

4. PRE (Patient Rights and Education)

- Story: Mom arrives and starts PREaching to the staff about how they should treat her son.
- Memory Hook: Preaching represents Rights and Education.

5. HIC (Hospital Infection Control)

- Story: Alex gets nervous from the yelling and develops violent HICcups that spread to everyone in the room.
- Memory Hook: Hiccups represent Infection Control.

* * *

### Part 2: The Hospital's Management (Chapters 6-10)

Now we leave Alex's room and go to the Hospital Administration office to fix the mess...

6. PSQ (Patient Safety and Quality Improvement)

- Story: To stop the spreading hiccups, the Director calls the Public Safety Queen.
- Memory Hook: She ensures Safety and Quality.

7. ROM (Responsibilities Of Management)

- Story: The Queen walks into the ROM (Room) where the Boss sits.
- Memory Hook: The "Room" is where the Management's Responsibility lies.

8. FMS (Facility Management and Safety)

- Story: The Boss is busy tuning an FM Station on the radio to check the building's alarms.
- Memory Hook: The FM Station controls the Facility.

9. HRM (Human Resource Management)

- Story: The radio music makes the HR Manager start dancing with the staff.
- Memory Hook: HRM is literal—managing the humans (staff).

10. IMS (Information Management Systems)

- Story: The IT guy takes an IMage (photo) of the dance and saves it to the System.
- Memory Hook: The Image/System represents Information Management.

* * *

what is the best way to prepare for nabh audit in 10 days

* * *

Preparing for an NABH audit in just 10 days is intense, but manageable if you switch from "System Building" mode to "Audit Readiness" mode. You don't have time to rewrite manuals; you only have time to verify evidence and train staff to answer correctly.

Here is a Battle-Tested 10-Day Crash Course to survive and succeed.

Gaurav to arrange for pest control esp for rats in the hospital 2 days before the NABH auditor’s visit!

### Phase 1: The "Paperwork & Evidence" Blitz (Days 1-3)

Goal: Ensure the documents the auditors ask for first are perfect. If these are messy, the audit starts on a bad note.

- Day 1: The "Legal & HR" Shield

- Licenses: Check your Statutory Compliance file. Ensure Fire NOC, PCB (Biomedical Waste), Pharmacy License, and AERB (X-ray) are valid. If expired, have the "Application for Renewal" receipt ready. - Gaurav to report
- HR Files (High Risk): Auditors always pick random staff files. Ensure every file has
- :[Check list personal file of employee](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1tS4dGy1YczWTaep6tcMQANnH8nNjIlNBGO7A_Zd-zqc/edit?tab%3Dt.0&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180845045&usg=AOvVaw05_4-RGefRLct5BnXQAOiy)
- Need Aman Brother’s training certificate

- Job Description (signed by staff).
- Joining Report & Appoint Letter.
- Vaccination Record (Hep B).
- Training hours log.

- Day 2: Committee Meetings & Minutes

- Verify that you have minutes for the mandatory committees (Infection Control, Pharm & Therapeutics, Safety, Quality).
- Hack: If a meeting was missed, hold an emergency review meeting today and document it as a "Pre-Audit Compliance Review."

- Day 3: The "Consent & Medical Record" Audit[Consent Lists](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/11ZVmRaRFORuITk99ifjDrK5yoUXhNV4JizFM2gD-0jw/edit?gid%3D0%23gid%3D0&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180846750&usg=AOvVaw0AqSnC754jKKm-QN0f0pCM)

- Pull 20 random active files and 20 discharge files.
- Check for:

- Initial Assessment completed within defined time (e.g., 15 mins for ER).
- Informed Consent: Are they signed? Is the doctor’s name legible? Is the date/time recorded?
- Discharge Summary: Is it complete with advice on medication and follow-up?

* * *

### Phase 2: The "People & Training" Blitz (Days 4-6)

Goal: Staff interviews are where most NCs (Non-Conformances) happen. Train them to answer, not to memorize.

- Day 4: "Code" Training (The Life Savers)- Dr Sachin, Aman

- Drill every single employee (guards, housekeeping, nurses) on: - want name s of staff who will do the mock!

- Code Red: Fire (R.A.C.E. – Rescue, Alarm, Contain, Extinguish).
- Code Blue: Cardiac Arrest (Who to call, number to dial).
- Spill Management: Show them the Spill Kit. Ask: "What do you do if blood falls here?"
- Code Pink

- Tip: Do this as a "Walking Drill" – go to their desk and ask.

- Day 5: Biomedical Waste (BMW) & Hand Hygiene -  Suraj Sonam

- This is the most common failure point.
- Check: Segregation (Red, Yellow, Blue, White bins).
- Quiz Housekeeping: "Which bag does this needle go in?" (Answer: White puncture-proof container). Where is the register where we have the weight of each waste?training os housekeeping? segregation?
- Quiz Nurses: "Show me the 6 steps of Hand Washing."

- Day 6: Departmental "Cheat Sheets" [NABH questions cheat sheet  for nurses.pdf](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://drive.google.com/file/d/1Y7K8oXuXpDjNoblEYIhrycmBrFE4cxbF/view?usp%3Dsharing&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180851200&usg=AOvVaw2jkwHX6zEFrG0uCazsi7As)

- Give every department a 1-page "Audit Cheat Sheet" containing:

- The department's Quality Indicators (e.g., "What is your needle stick injury rate?").
- The Scope of Services (What we do vs. What we don't do).
- Patient Rights (Staff should know at least 3-4).
- Mission vision
- Spill kit

* * *

### Phase 3: The "Facility & Mock Tracer" (Days 7-9)

Goal: See what the auditor will see.

- Day 7: The Facility Round (The "Broken Window" Fix) aman rajak 3 months record -

- Walk the hospital with maintenance. Fix:

- Flickering lights.
- Dampness/Seepage on walls (Paint over it if needed).
- Signage: Ensure "Exit," "Fire Extinguisher," and "Biohazard" signs are visible.
- Crash Carts: Ensure no drug is expired. Lock/Seal the cart after checking.

- Day 8: The "Patient Tracer" (The Auditor's Favorite Tool)

- Select a real patient currently admitted. Trace their journey from Entry → ER → Ward → OT → ICU.
- Check every document generated in this journey.
- Interview the staff caring for this specific patient. Do they know the care plan?

- Day 9: KPIs ? Quality Indicators (The Data Check) [HAI Surveillance (Hospital Acquired Infections)](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1JAjuLudTcBcFDHrZIjCRQGKp6eODOhA7dsasdpjV7p8/edit?usp%3Dsharing&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180855883&usg=AOvVaw1zgLzZVrc7Jvbq-1Uod6F7) Aman Brother

- Ensure your graphs for the last 3 months are printed and 7: If the auditor asks "What is your infection rate?", the ICN (Infection Control Nurse) must give the exact number, not a guess.

* * *

### Day 10: The "War Room" & Morale

- Morning: Final "Clean Sweep" of the facility (dust on top of cupboards, clear corridors).
- Afternoon: Pep talk. Tell staff: "If you don't know the answer, do not guess. Say: 'I will refer to the manual/policy and get back to you.' That is a correct answer."
- Evening: Assign "Escorts" for the auditors. Their job is to guide the auditor and discreetly signal staff to be ready.

### The "Red Flag" Checklist (Do NOT miss these)

1. Narcotic Cabinet: Must be double-locked. Key with the doctor/charge nurse only.
2. Fridge Temperature: Temp logs for medication fridges must be filled up to today.
3. Fire Exits: Must be unblocked.1 No stretchers or boxes in front of them.
4. Ambulance: Check the blinkers, siren, and emergency drugs inside.

* * *

* * *

Would you like a sample "Staff Interview Questionnaire" (Top 20 Questions) to distribute to your nurses and housekeeping today?

names of committees in nabh

To pass an NABH audit, you need to show evidence that specific committees are active, meeting regularly, and documenting their minutes.

Here are the Mandatory Committees required by NABH (5th Edition), grouped by their function.

### 1. The "Big 4" Core Committees (Non-Negotiable)

These committees drive the hospital's quality and safety. If these are missing, it is a major non-conformance.

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Committee Name | Purpose (The Mission) | Key Members |
| Quality & Safety Committee (Apex Committee) | Oversees the entire accreditation program. They review data from all other committees and make final decisions. | Chair: Medical Director / CEO<br>Members: All HODs, Quality Manager. |
| HIC Committee (Hospital Infection Control) | Monitors infection rates (HAI), needle stick injuries, and hand hygiene compliance. | Chair: Senior Consultant / Microbiologist<br>Members: ICN, Nursing Supt, Housekeeping In-charge. |
| PTC (Pharmaco-Therapeutic Committee) | Decides which medicines the hospital buys (Formulary). Monitors medication errors and adverse drug reactions (ADR). | Chair: Sr. Clinician / Intensivist<br>Members: Chief Pharmacist, Nursing Supt. |
| Medical Records Committee | Checks if files are complete (audits), legibility of doctor's notes, and timely discharge summary generation. | Chair: Medical Supt.<br>Members: MRD Officer, Clinicians. |

* * *

### 2\. The "Safety & Legal" Committees

These are often required by law as well as NABH.

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Committee Name | Purpose (The Mission) | Important Note |
| Safety & Disaster Management Committee | Inspects the facility for fire risks, hazardous materials, and conducts mock drills (Code Red). | Often combined in smaller hospitals. Must meet twice a year min. |
| Internal Complaints Committee (ICC) | Mandatory by Indian Law (Vishakha Guidelines). Deals with sexual harassment complaints. | Must be headed by a Senior Woman. Must have an external NGO member. |
| Grievance Redressal Committee | Reviews complaints from patients and staff. | Often split into two: Patient Grievance & Employee Grievance. |

* * *

### 3\. Clinical Audit Committees

These focus on specific clinical outcomes.

- Code Blue / CPR Committee: Reviews every cardiac arrest that happens in the hospital. (Did the team arrive on time? Was the CPR effective?)
- Death Review / Mortality Committee: Analyzes all hospital deaths to see if they were preventable.
- Blood Transfusion Committee: (Mandatory if you have a Blood Bank) Monitors blood wastage and transfusion reactions.
- Ethics Committee: Mandatory if you conduct research or clinical trials on patients.

### 💡 Pro-Tip for the Audit

- Minutes of Meeting (MOM): You must have a "MOM Register" for each committee.
- Frequency: Most committees must meet at least once every 3 months (Quarterly). The Infection Control Committee often meets monthly.
- Attendance: Ensure the attendance sheet in the register is signed. If the Chairman didn't sign, the meeting "didn't happen."

... [Hospital Committees as per your NABH standards](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v%3DJgLbEonmtHo&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180879186&usg=AOvVaw0r0rfo-368FD8y0MdsONm2)

This video provides a visual breakdown of the roles and responsibilities for each committee, which can be useful for training your staff.

ESIC billing and other corporate billing issues

![](<Base64-Image-Removed>)

* * *

These email addresses belong to high-ranking officials and departments within the Ministry of Labour & Employment and the Employees' State Insurance Corporation (ESIC), specifically focusing on the Maharashtra region.

The collection suggests a context of filing a serious grievance or complaint related to labour issues or ESIC benefits (particularly medical or super-specialty treatment) in Maharashtra.

### 1\. Ministry of Labour & Employment (Highest Level)

These emails go directly to the central ministry in New Delhi.

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Email ID | Owner / Designation | Role & Context |
| minoffice-mole@nic.in | Office of the Minister | The official office email for the Union Minister of Labour & Employment (currently Dr. Mansukh Mandaviya). Used for high-level escalation. |
| Ashutosh.pednekar@gov.in | Ashutosh A.T. Pednekar (IAS) | Chief Labour Commissioner (Central) and Joint Secretary. He acts as the head of the labour department's regulatory body. |
| pgcell-labour@nic.in | Public Grievance Cell | The dedicated department within the Ministry of Labour handling public complaints and grievances. |

* * *

### 2\. ESIC Headquarters (New Delhi)

These emails connect to the top management of ESIC.

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Email ID | Owner / Designation | Role & Context |
| dir-gen@esic.nic.in | Director General (DG) | The highest administrative authority of ESIC (currently Ashok Kumar Singh, IAS). |
| dmc-sst.hq@esic.nic.in | Deputy Medical Commissioner (SST) | Handles Super Specialty Treatment. This is the key contact if a patient is facing issues getting referrals for advanced medical care (heart, cancer, kidney, etc.) outside of standard ESI dispensaries. |

* * *

### 3\. ESIC Maharashtra (Regional Level)

These emails are for the officials responsible for executing ESIC rules specifically in Maharashtra.

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Email ID | Owner / Designation | Role & Context |
| rd-maharashtra@esic.nic.in | Regional Director | The head of ESIC for the state of Maharashtra. Responsible for all administrative and operational issues in the state. |
| smo-mh@esic.nic.in | State Medical Officer (SMO) | The top medical authority for ESIC in Maharashtra. Handles approvals for medical reimbursement, hospital tie-ups, and treatment complaints. |
| nk.singh@esic.nic.in | Niraj Kumar Singh | Assistant Director / Public Grievance Officer. He is an officer likely handling public grievances. (Note: While previously listed in Tamil Nadu, these officers transfer frequently; he is included here as a grievance contact). |

### Summary of Hierarchy

If you are sending an email to this list, you are effectively cc'ing everyone from the Union Minister down to the Regional Officer.

- For Medical Emergencies: The most critical emails here are dmc-sst.hq@esic.nic.in (Headquarters SST) and smo-mh@esic.nic.in (Maharashtra Medical Officer).
- For Administrative Complaints:rd-maharashtra@esic.nic.in and Ashutosh.pednekar@gov.in are the key authorities.

Proceedings and outcomes of the official visit to Mumbai undertaken on 24December 2025 for follow-up with ESIC and MPKAY authorities.

Summary of Actions Taken

ESIC – Parel & Colaba

Visited the office of the Regional Director, ESIC (Parel), (Abhilasha Jha); was informed by PA Chetan Patil that the Commissioner’s mail has been forwarded to ESIC Colaba for further action.

At ESIC Colaba office 5th Floor (Billing Section), met Mr. Harshpal Singh, Billing Head.

All files submitted by Hope Hospital were retrieved and reviewed on the ESIC portal.

Required covering letters were attached to the respective files.

Assurance received that files will be sent for doctor’s scrutiny within two working days.

ESIC officials were extremely cooperative and responsive.

MPKAY – Colaba & Worli

Met Dr. Sugat Wagh at MPKAY Colaba office and received the following status of pending bills:

₹13 Lakhs – Forwarded to DG Office (ready for payment)

₹18 Lakhs – Under processing

₹7 Lakhs – Under audit query

Total Pending Amount: ₹38 Lakhs

A fresh statement of pending bills will be issued by MPKAY.

Met Dr. Anjali Sawant, Operations Head, MPKAY at Jeevandayee Bhavan, Worli.

She assured that:

All pending MPKAY bills will be processed within 15 days.

Files will be sent to the DGP Office.

Payments are expected to be released by mid-January 2026.

Dr. Sawant also oversees MJPJAY operations, making her a key liaison for MPKAY, PMJAY, and MJPJAY cases of Hope Hospital.

Overall Assessment

The visit was highly fruitful and outcome-oriented.

Complete clarity was obtained on file status, payment stages, and timelines.

Officials at both ESIC and MPKAY offices were professional, cooperative, and proactive.

Clear follow-up channels have been established for faster realizations.

Conclusion

All objectives of the visit were successfully achieved. ESIC files are progressing towards medical scrutiny, and MPKAY payments are expected within the committed timeline. Continuous follow-up is expected to result in improved billing realizations and cash flow for Hope Hospital.

Report on Visit to ESIC Office, Colaba on 7th & 8th Jan , – Follow-up for Bills Processing & Payment Release

1\. Purpose of Visit

Visited ESIC Office, Colaba to follow up on processing of bills for patients admitted to Hope Hospital and for early release of payments.

2\. Meeting at Medical Benefit Branch

Met Mr. Harsh Pal, Superintendent, MBB Branch, 3rd Floor. He instructed his staff Chiranjit to check all Hope Hospital files on the portal and to send eligible files for L1 & L2 SMO scrutiny.

3\. Portal Verification

All files were checked by ESIC staff in front of us on the portal.

• Total bills submitted files of Hope Hospital: 115

• Files already forwarded for doctor scrutiny: 85 (sent to L1/L2)

4\. Pending Status

• 20 files pending on portal.

• 7 files have NMs.

• Balance awaiting BPA approval.

Superintendent assured that these 20 files will be sent for doctors scrutiny immediately after BPA approval.

5\. Deficient Document – 1 File

One file was not having referral and e-Pehchan. We are carrying the document with us for re-submission.

6\. SMO Interaction .

Met Dr. Shivkumar on 8th Jan @ 10am, he checked the portal and confirmed that 95 files of Hope Hospital had been received. He assured that all the files will be approved by 10th Feb, and then the bill will be processed by accounts deptt.

7\. Process Explained

After SMO scrutiny, files are sent to RD Office with payment statement and thereafter forwarded to Accounts for payments release.

8\. Next Follow-up

Dr Shivkumar told to call up in 15days and has assured that he will forward all the files for payment processing by 10th Feb..

### Technical Correction & Action Plan

- Do Not Rely on Inverter Readings: Inverter display readings can be misleading or inaccurate. Do not use them as the sole source of truth for system performance.
- Mandatory Clamp Meter Testing: To verify actual generation, a Clamp Meter must be used. This provides the only reliable measurement of the current (Amps) flowing through each specific string.
- Missing String Diagram: A detailed string layout diagram is missing and urgently required. Without it, we cannot determine the specific distribution of the 108 panels across the inputs (PV1, PV2, PV3).
- String Configuration Discrepancy (3 vs. 6): The inspection report notes the system is "connected in 3 strings", but for a 60kW system with this panel count, there are likely 6 strings (physically connected in parallel at the MPPTs). We need to verify how these are divided (e.g., 2 strings per MPPT) to identify exactly which subsets of panels are underperforming.
- Fault Isolation: Once the string diagram is available and clamp meter readings are taken, we can pinpoint exactly which specific panels or strings are "dead" versus those that are simply shaded.

Subject: Request for Technical Data - Hope Hospital Solar Review (Dec 9, 2025)

Dear GreenSky Solar Team,

Thank you for your visit and the review letter dated December 9, 2025. We have reviewed your observations regarding the 60 KW system's underperformance.

Before we proceed with the proposed technical survey or any civil work, please share the specific data logs and evidence collected during your inspection that support the following points:

- Generation Logs: You mentioned the total output is around "55 to 60% of current capacity". Please provide the calculation or meter reading logs used to arrive at this specific figure.
- Dead String Evidence: You noted that "one of the three strings is not giving any output". Please share the electrical voltage/current readings or photos of the inverter display that confirm this specific string failure.
- Shadow Visuals: Regarding the "shadow from existing panels and hospital signage", please share any photos taken during the site visit showing the exact time and extent of the shading on the panels.

We need this documentation to validate the extent of the damage before approving further steps.

Regards,

Dr. Murali Hope Hospital

![DABUN Dexter Series – 8 kW / 48V 1PH Offgrid with ...](<Base64-Image-Removed>)

Dabun Inverter apps are mobile applications for monitoring and controlling Dabun's solar inverters (on-grid, off-grid, hybrid) and solar systems, allowing users to track energy production, usage, battery status, and sometimes remotely switch the system on/off via Wi-Fi/GSM, with apps like [SolarEdge's](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.google.com/search?q%3DSolarEdge%2527s%26oq%3Ddabun%2Binverter%2Ba%26gs_lcrp%3DEgZjaHJvbWUqBwgBECEYoAEyBggAEEUYOTIHCAEQIRigATIHCAIQIRigATIHCAMQIRigATIHCAQQIRiPAjIHCAUQIRiPAjIHCAYQIRiPAtIBCDgxMzFqMGo3qAIAsAIA%26sourceid%3Dchrome%26ie%3DUTF-8%26mstk%3DAUtExfCna05_kHivYf7mRHK_AbTTgoKqDLCGOOEBi9K5DPVfKySvbqx8Rmz6PFbo3Y4Wqb_S-2lZIGHvZ3RQsoVzCriM6Whx_UVnRHDPfSZEjCQoFdlXnvakwpp8_Jkb144tWRPXUwfdM6jYbxibyhpo8l6LetwVt3KtltMBXWAMT3XwCFI%26csui%3D3%26ved%3D2ahUKEwig0ePZg7CRAxUcUGcHHdk4AugQgK4QegQIARAE&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180930396&usg=AOvVaw3Mcaw8aItYtG-tXehZU7Mg) or custom ones for their hybrid models, providing real-time data and smart energy management. To find the specific app, check your Dabun inverter model's manual or the Dabun website (dabun.in), as they offer various monitoring solutions for different setups.

What Dabun Inverter Apps Do:

- Remote Monitoring: Check power generation, battery levels (for off-grid/hybrid), and grid interaction from your phone.
- Control: Switch inverters or modes (like battery priority) remotely.
- Energy Insights: View real-time energy flow, savings, and system performance.
- System Management: Manage solar, battery, and grid usage for optimized savings.

How to Find Your Dabun App:

1. Check Dabun's Website: Visit dabun.in and look for "Monitoring" or "Apps" sections under their inverter products.
2. Inverter Model Specific: Dabun has different inverters (Dexter series, Solarizer) that might use specific apps or modules.
3. Wi-Fi/GSM Module: Ensure your inverter has the necessary connectivity module for app integration.

Examples of Monitoring (Generic & Dabun-Related):

- [mySolarEdge App](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v%3D8M481XRu7ZE&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180934614&usg=AOvVaw2NoQQRGWouqGLxL3jCNm6l) (for SolarEdge, illustrates app functionality).
- Dabun's own systems often integrate apps for their hybrid inverters, enabling "batteryless" operation and grid export control.

In short, if you have a Dabun system, you'll likely use a specific app (or a module with app access) to unlock its smart features.

CONTROL OF THE MANUAL

The holder of the copy of this manual is responsible for maintaining it in good and safe condition and in a readily identifiable and retrievable manner.

The holder of the copy of this Manual shall maintain it in current status by inserting latest amendments as and when the amended versions are received.

HR Manager – Human Resources Department is responsible for issuing the amended copies to the copyholders, the copyholder should acknowledge the same and he /she should return the obsolete copies to the HR Manager.

The amendment sheet, to be updated (as and when amendments received) and referred for details of amendments issued.

The manual is reviewed once a year and is updated as relevant to the hospital policies and procedures. Review and amendment can happen also as corrective actions to the non-conformities raised during the self-assessment or assessment audits by NABH.

The authority over control of this manual is as follows:

|     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Preparation | Approval | Issue |
| HR Manager, Human Resources Department. | Chairman, Hope Group of Hospitals. | Accreditation coordinator |

The procedure manual with original signatures of the above on the title page is considered as ‘Master Copy’, and the photocopies of the master copy for the distribution are considered as ‘Controlled Copy’.

Distribution List of the Manual:

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| S.No. | Designation |
| 1 | Chairman |
| 2 | Human Resources and Development Department |
| 3 | Accreditation Coordinator |

To organize the topics from the operational manual of Hope Hospital for the leadership team into five major title sections, we will categorize them based on the core areas of hospital operations they relate to. Here's a suggested division and names of conveners of the group discussion of LT:

1\. Administration and Management - Gaurav( Day 2 ) Sat - 13th April

2\. Marketing and Front Office Operations - Suraj ( Day 3 ) Mon 15 April - Mon

3\. Financial and Billing Operations --Gaurav and  Gaaurav( Day 4 ) Mon 16th Tues

4\. Human Resources & Staff Management - Gaurav ( Day 5 ) Mon 17th Wed

5\. Security and Facility Management - Suraj ( Day 6 ) Mon 18th Thurs

[Leadership Team training session Hope group on 16th April 2024, from 11 AM to 8 PM -Schedule and topics for a](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/19CTpnHLi4543USTXtdngu0jQ7L5t3ZQf8zEZEQ6YtYM/edit&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089180997978&usg=AOvVaw1AiOhHC7SHzQyU0I929ArD) Yearly training started in 2024.

This structure organises the manual into clear sections, making it easier for members of the leadership team to find relevant information quickly. Each section groups related topics, enhancing the overall usability and navigation of the manual.

## 🏥 Daily Accounting SOP for Hope & Ayushman Hospitals

### 1️⃣ Payment Protocol

- No payments should be made in cash.

- All transactions must be processed through UPI, bank transfer or cheque.

- Maintain cashbook and daybook entries daily for petty cash tracking.


* * *

### 2️⃣ Approval System for Payments

- Every payment requires three approvals:


- Gaurav Agrawal
- Accountant who is paying
- Receiving person


- Ensure voucher approval trail is documented and stored digitally. - send all vouchers in 1 pdf by mail


* * *

### 3️⃣ Daily Bank Reconciliation – ⏰ Deadline: 5 PM

- Perform daily reconciliation of all bank accounts.

- Cross-verify:


- Bank ledger vs Tally Ledger in one mail

- Tally closing balance vs bank statement


- Send daily bank reconciliation report by email to CMD and Auditor before 5 PM.


* * *

### 4️⃣ Cash Balance Verification

- Physical cash balance must match Tally closing cash ledger.

- Verify denominations and prepare a closing summary daily.

- Send confirmation - cash and day book by 5 PM via email.


* * *

### 5️⃣ Patient Ledger & Admission Records

- Maintain patient ledger for every admission and submission.

- Responsible Person: Madhuri


- Ensure payment receipts from corporates - Patient wise are recorded and tallied daily.

- Submit daily ledger summary by email.


* * *

### 6️⃣ Journal Vouchers (JV)

- Ensure JV entries are made for:


- Radiology

- Lab

- Consultant fees (OPD, IPD, procedures)

- Anaesthetists and Technicians


- JV entries must be verified and updated in Tally by EOD.


* * *

### 7️⃣ Reporting & Expertise

- Excel Export:Adamrit (Over Supervision)


- Responsible for data verification and error-free compilation.


- Tally Admin:


- Ensure all ledgers are up to date.

- Oversee JV posting, cash ledger, and reconciliation uploads.


* * *

### 8️⃣ Communication & Documentation

- All financial summaries (Bank Reconciliation, Cash Ledger, and JV status) must be emailed by 5 PM daily to Gaurav, Ruby, Viji and Murali

- Subject Line Format:

  \[Date\] – Hope/Ayushman – Daily Accounts Summary

- Copy to: CMD, Accounts Head, Auditor.


* * *

Here are the points for improvement in the functioning of Hope Hospital, as noted by the leadership team appointed today, based on handwritten notes:

* * *

Clinical leader - Aman Brother and Neesha -  Key Observations & Action Points

First thing to do every morning at 9.30 am is -

Find which RMO (esp Sachin and shiraz) , Nurse and leadership team member is absent and select a replacement for the day and inform him what his tasks are for the day!

As a duty doctor or nurse or admin staff, it should be observed that their behavior towards patients and their relatives is pleasant.They are expected to conduct with greater respect, patience, and cooperation in all interactions. Report immediately if they don't behave.

\- Discharge summary and bill should be available by 6 PM if ordered before 3 PM . No elective discharges after 3 PM and holidays

\- Address issues related to nurses and ward boys, who are presently focusing specifically on internal “politics and gossips”.

\- Surgery patients need interventions within 24 hours; admissions should not exceed 7 days.

\- Inform and counsel patient’s relatives in the doctor's chamber by RMOs as per advance statements sequence and keep billing transparent.

Nursing & Rounds

\- OPD nurses should be available at the counter. Not leave the OPD counter

\- Rounds will be taken between 11 AM–1 PM by Sachin and Shiraz. OPD patients informed that OPD may be delayed because doctors are  on rounds.

\- Improve the consistency of nurse handovers with documentation and sharing of emergency drugs and equipment  status photos (should include 5 Vasofix, 5 IV fluids) to the whatsapp group.

\- Ensure final prescriptions by 5 PM for the next 24 hours and last discharge by 3 PM.

Doctor & OPD Coordination

\- Address doctor/OPD issues with quick 15-minute interventions as soon as the patient registers in the reception counter.

\- ward Rounds from 11 AM–1 PM and OPD from 8–11 PM.

All documents including OT notes and anesthesia notes should be complete as per NABH norms

Every wednesday  10 am ultrasounds will be done . Dr Manish Agrawal will be called by Neesha . Dr Tushar Bagde 8983146848 will be available 9 to 10.30 am everyday except sundays for ultrasound in Hope hospital. Inform patients beforehand

* * *

Operations - Kashish and Diksha

\- Audit or update TV display of videos( patient educational videos should play 24 hours) and patient token management in the front office.

On every discharge - Rooms should be got cleaned and TV remotes checked, water and electricity, dustbin empty etc. and locked and handed over to reception staff

Sufficient bedsheets and patient uniforms (5 at least) in stock should be available for emergencies. Discard torn clothes without buttons.

Nurse calling bell to be installed next to each patient

On Bill submission, IPD file will be handed over to Kashish within 1 hour. Sign of a person handed over in a register is compulsory.

Cleanliness \- Mopping and sweeping has to be done by night staff by 8 am. Photos of dirty areas have to be shared in a cleanliness group.

Billing deadlines have to be taken seriously and monitored and reported to CMD

Whenever a patient is sent for Ct or MRI tell them beforehand that they should have meals as it takes 5 hours for the scan. They will have to make arrangements for food at the center.  Make standard instructions for all the patients that are sent for scans!

* * *

Marketing - Abhishek

Fielding of 11 team members to tell that they have come to the right hospital with the consultant and equipment available  - guards, housekeeping staff included

Referral

The MRI and CT can be sent to “Insight” and for ultrasound also call radiologist from insight.. Every wednesday  10 am ultrasounds will be done .  Manish Agrawal will be called by Neesha

OPD Marketing

1st week of October. Local free OPD for Ayushman yojna patients between 8 am to 11 pm evertyday. 20 percent discount of all charges

Maintain referral register and discharge wise referral payment register

## 📌 Priority-Based Note on Patient-Wise Reconciliation and Financial Reporting

* * *

### 🔴 1\. Mandatory Patient-Wise Reconciliation (Top Priority)

Why It’s Critical:

- Avoids Misrepresentation: Without individual patient-level reconciliation, the system will continue to show outstanding balances even if amounts have been deducted or settled. This misleads the management into believing dues are pending from corporates, skewing financial reports.

- Track Deduction Sources: It is impossible to trace which deductions (Y amount) have been made and on what grounds unless each payment is matched to individual patients.

- IT Audit and Legal Compliance: In the event of an IT audit or dispute, patient-level documentation is essential for validating corporate deductions and ensuring accountability. Otherwise, we need to pay tax considering the entire amount billed as income!!!


Immediate Action Items:

- Link UTR numbers from corporate payments (e.g., WCL, Railways) with individual patient bills.

- Use data downloaded from corporate portals to cross-reference with internal billing records.

- Maintain a master Excel sheet to map:


- Patient Name

- Bill Number

- Claimed Amount

- Received Amount

- Deducted Amount (with reason if available)

- UTR Number

- Status (Pending/Settled)


* * *

### 🔶 2\. Integrated Ledger Maintenance (High Priority)

Why It’s Critical:

- Holistic Visibility: Keeping records only in the billing department leads to fragmented information. Synchronization across:


- Billing Department

- Patient Ledger

- Corporate Ledger

   ensures transparent financial health tracking.


- Profit/Loss Calculation: Profitability and organizational financial status depend on correct recognition of liabilities and receivables. Missing this leads to wrong estimations of revenue or surplus.


Instructions:

- Implement a centralized accounting ledger view that shows all patient-wise and corporate-level transactions.

- Ensure every deduction or payment is reflected across all relevant ledgers in real-time.

- Align ERP or billing software to support this tri-level recording system.


* * *

### 🟡 3\. Recovery and Claim Management (Medium Priority)

Key Observations:

- 2–3 Year Overdues: Many invoices sent to WCL remain unpaid or partially paid over long periods.

- Unjustified Deductions: Numerous entries show arbitrary deductions with no explanations or claim records.


Recommendations:

- Start immediate follow-up on long-pending claims—prioritize by age and value.

- For deductions:


- Investigate causes (e.g., documentation errors, approval issues).

- Maintain backup records for possible re-claim.

- Develop a “Deductions Register” for audit trail.


* * *

### 🔵 4\. Efficiency and Delay Tracking (Important for Strategic Planning)

Challenges:

- Inability to calculate average delay in corporate payment cycles due to the lack of reconciliation.

- Affects cash flow forecasting and impacts operational planning.


Suggested Actions:

- Once patient-wise reconciliation is in place, generate reports showing:


- Average number of days between billing and payment.

- Delay trends per corporate body.

- Delay trends per department.


This will assist leadership in negotiations and credit policy formulation.

* * *

### 🟢 5\. Operational Follow-up and Coordination (Ongoing Priority)

Assigned Coordinators:

- Dr. Murali and Mr. Gaurav Agrawal are the primary hospital contacts for working with CA Nikhil Rathi’s team.


Next Steps:

- Prepare for next review meeting scheduled for Monday, 2nd June 2025, to evaluate reconciliation progress and finalize audit terms.


* * *

## ✅ Conclusion

To ensure financial clarity, correct accounting, and efficient recovery, the hospital must enforce a robust patient-wise reconciliation mechanism and ledger integration. This is fundamental not just for financial reporting but for making accurate business decisions regarding revenue cycle management and liability recognition.

Let me know if you'd like help designing the Excel template or workflow system for this process.

* * *

### SOP of receptionist to followup with the leads of Justdial

Justdial Dashboard \- Always follow up on the Justdial dashboard,.The dashboard should always be open in front of you. The call can be for Ayushman hospital, Hope or Raftaar ! Phones will not always ring. Most cases only notifications are received!

Script:

1. Good Morning \- Greeting.

2. Inquiry for Ayushman/Hope/ Raftar \- Respond to inquiries immediately for the hospital/raftaar, particularly related to the category of the enquiry. Example - orthopaedics, gastroenterologist, ambulance service etc.

3. Know the Doctors Names and  Availability well in advance! \- Dr. Nikhil Khobragade is available from 12 PM to 4 PM
4. Consultant list and their OPD timings should be in the pin board in front of you!.[Consultant List -OPD Timing](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1igK6Ny77mSfA4lzgM_dIwJojZzVzHtjguVHe3lM5wp4/edit?gid%3D0%23gid%3D0&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181075873&usg=AOvVaw2T_YlGwKDjg0VU5zA0Qe-h)

5. Appointment Confirmation \- Confirm appointments for the day immediately.

   डॉक्टर की उपलब्धता \- डॉ. निखिल खोब्रागड़े 12 बजे से 4 बजे तक उपलब्ध हैं।

   अपॉइंटमेंट पुष्टि \- आज के लिए अपॉइंटमेंट kab chahiye?

Doctor or ambulance Search Process of patient in Justdial:

- e.g.,Patients Search for Orthopedic Surgeon- Patients don't search for names of orthopaedic surgeons in justdial

- 7 hospitals listed in just dial are given the inquiry by justdial - Top 5 of listing and another 2 in rotational manner .

- TAT (Turn Around Time) for responding by receptionist  is within 3 minutes.
- If you delay in responding another hospital will call the patient and get the patient diverted!

1. जस्टडायल डैशबोर्ड \- हमेशा जस्टडायल डैशबोर्ड पर लीड्स को कैटेगरी अनुसार फॉलो करें।

2. गुड मॉर्निंग \- अभिवादन।

3. आयुष्मान अस्पताल के लिए पूछताछ \- अस्पताल के लिए पूछताछ का जवाब दें, विशेष रूप से गैस्ट्रोलॉजिस्ट से संबंधित।

4. डॉक्टर की उपलब्धता \- डॉ. निखिल खोब्रागड़े 12 बजे से 4 बजे तक उपलब्ध हैं।

5. अपॉइंटमेंट पुष्टि \- आज के लिए अपॉइंटमेंट की पुष्टि करें।

6. वेंडर सर्च प्रक्रिया:


- ऑर्थोपेडिक सर्जन की खोज करें।

- 7 वेंडर्स को पूछताछ दी जाती है।

- TAT (टर्नअराउंड टाइम) का जवाब 3 मिनट के अंदर दिया जाता है।


नीचे आयुष्मान अस्पताल के संपर्क विवरण हैं।

### Hope Group of Hospitals

### Hope Hospital - सुरक्षा कर्मचारी जिम्मेदारियां: \- Sakshi

1\. सामान्य सुरक्षा और प्रशासन:

- इंडक्शन डे पर मोबाइल नंबर एक्सचेंज: इंडक्शन डे पर कर्मचारियों और लीडरशिप टीम के मोबाइल नंबर एक्सचेंज किए जाएंगे, और सभी को एक-दूसरे के नाम और नंबर सेव करने होंगे, साथ ही सुरक्षा एजेंसी के मालिक का नंबर भी सेव करना होगा।

- भीड़ (Mob) की स्थिति में पुलिस को सूचित करना: अगर कोई भीड़ हंगामा करती है, तो पुलिस से संपर्क करना और फिर सुरज और राहुल को सूचना देना ताकि सहायता मिल सके।

- आपातकालीन संपर्क सूचनाएं: अस्पताल की हर मंजिल पर आपातकालीन संपर्क नंबर को प्रमुख रूप से प्रदर्शित किया जाना चाहिए।

- इनवर्ड और आउटवर्ड रजिस्टर बनाना: सभी उपकरणों और वस्तुओं के रिकॉर्ड रखना जो अस्पताल में आए या गए हों। इन वस्तुओं की फोटो खींचकर निर्धारित WhatsApp ग्रुप में शेयर करनी चाहिए।

- कर्मचारी बैग चेक करना: सभी कर्मचारियों के बैग्स को चेक करना जब वे अस्पताल में प्रवेश करें या उसे छोड़ें, ताकि प्रतिबंधित वस्तुएं जैसे तम्बाकू, शराब, या अन्य गैरकानूनी सामान अंदर न आएं। ज्वलनशील वस्तुएं, स्टोव, लाइटर, माचिस आदि लाना प्रतिबंधित है। बाहर का खाना अस्पताल में लाना मना है।

- इंटरकॉम नंबर पता होना चाहिए: सभी कर्मचारियों को इंटरकॉम नंबर पता होने चाहिए। अगर कोई विज़िटर लीडरशिप टीम के सदस्य से मिलना चाहता है, तो गार्ड को इंटरकॉम पर संपर्क करना चाहिए और सदस्य से पूछने के लिए अपनी जगह नहीं छोड़नी चाहिए।

- रोगी बैग और पॉकेट चेक करना: सभी रोगियों और उनके परिवारों के बैग और पॉकेट्स को अस्पताल में प्रवेश करते समय चेक करना चाहिए। प्रतिबंधित वस्तुओं को जब्त करना।

- लिफ्ट का उपयोग: लिफ्ट का उपयोग केवल मरीजों के परिवहन के लिए किया जाए, कर्मचारियों के लिए नहीं।

- बिजली की खपत: अस्पताल में अत्यधिक बिजली के उपयोग को सीमित करना।

- अग्नि सुरक्षा: कर्मचारियों को यह जानना चाहिए कि आग लगने की स्थिति में फायर पंप को कैसे चालू करें। जनरेटर को चालू और बंद करना भी कर्मचारियों को पता होना चाहिए। फायर एक्सटिंग्विशर का उपयोग कैसे करें, यह भी जानना जरूरी है।

- मॉक ड्रिल्स: आपातकालीन तैयारी के लिए नियमित मॉक ड्रिल्स करना।

- कर्मचारी प्रबंधन: प्रमुख कर्मचारियों के मोबाइल नंबर का रजिस्टर रखना ताकि आपातकाल में कर्मचारियों की पहचान की जा सके।

- मोबाइल फोन जब्त करना: अस्पताल की मोबाइल उपयोग नीति का उल्लंघन करने वाले कर्मचारियों के मोबाइल फोन जब्त किए जाएंगे।

- उपकरण और चाबी रजिस्टर: उपकरणों और चाबियों का विस्तृत रिकॉर्ड रखना और शिफ्ट बदलाव के समय उनकी सही गिनती सुनिश्चित करना।


2\. नाइट गार्ड्स - आयुष्मान अस्पताल:

- 24/7 सेवाएं: नाइट गार्ड सेवाएं 24/7 उपलब्ध करनी चाहिए। अगर अगला शिफ्ट कर्मचारी नहीं आता, तो वर्तमान स्टाफ को अस्पताल छोड़ने की अनुमति नहीं होगी।

- कर्मचारी बैग और पॉकेट चेक करना: नाइट गार्ड्स को कर्मचारियों के बैग और पॉकेट चेक करने की जिम्मेदारी दी जाएगी जब वे अस्पताल छोड़ रहे हों।

- तम्बाकू और शराब नहीं: अस्पताल परिसर में तम्बाकू या खारा पूरी तरह से प्रतिबंधित है।

- बैक एंट्री गेट: बैक एंट्री गेट को सुबह 5 बजे के बाद खुला रखना।

- लिफ्ट प्रबंधन: लिफ्ट को हमेशा ग्राउंड फ्लोर पर उपलब्ध रखना चाहिए, और इसे 4th फ्लोर से ग्राउंड फ्लोर तक कर्मचारियों के परिवहन के लिए उपयोग नहीं करना चाहिए।

- फायर पंप क्षेत्र की सुरक्षा: फायर पंप क्षेत्र के पास एक गार्ड हमेशा ग्राउंड फ्लोर पर होना चाहिए।

- सामग्री का फोटो लेना: गार्ड्स को सभी सामानों की तस्वीरें लेनी होंगी जो अस्पताल में आने और जाने के दौरान शिफ्ट होती हैं और WhatsApp ग्रुप में शेयर करनी होगी, साथ ही एक रजिस्टर भी रखना होगा।


3\. अस्पताल संपत्ति और व्यक्तिगत सामान की जांच:

- बैग चेक पॉलिसी: सभी व्यक्तिगत बैकपैक्स अस्पताल में लाने की अनुमति नहीं है। कर्मचारी प्रवेश द्वार पर एक डेस्क स्थापित किया जाएगा जहां उनके बैग चेक किए जाएंगे। सुरक्षा कर्मचारी द्वारा दैनिक चेक किए जाएंगे।

- अनधिकृत कब्जा: अस्पताल की संपत्ति जैसे दवाइयां, IV बोतलें, या OT उपकरण आदि का अनधिकृत कब्जा पाया गया तो इसके लिए अस्पताल की नीति के अनुसार कार्रवाई की जाएगी।


* * *

दोनों अस्पतालों के लिए सामान्य दिशानिर्देश:

4\. फ्रंट ऑफिस संचालन और रिपोर्टिंग:

- रोगी प्रवेश और डिस्चार्ज: रोगी प्रवेश और डिस्चार्ज प्रक्रियाओं को सुचारू रूप से बनाए रखना, इसके लिए एक रजिस्टर बनाना जिसमें सभी भर्ती और डिस्चार्ज किए गए रोगियों का रिकॉर्ड हो।

- OPD और IPD ट्रैकिंग: OPD और IPD रोगियों का ट्रैक रखना और सभी जरूरी जानकारी बिलिंग विभाग को समय पर साझा करना।

- परामर्श रिकॉर्ड: OPD परामर्श का सही रिकॉर्ड रखना, जिसमें रोगियों को tarif के हिसाब से (जैसे प्राइवेट, योजना) कैटेगरी में वर्गीकृत किया गया हो।

- कर्मचारी समन्वय और संचार: रिसेप्शन डेस्क को हमेशा मैनड रखना और कर्मचारियों को WhatsApp के माध्यम से अपडेट देने के लिए प्रोटोकॉल का पालन करना।

- CCTV निगरानी: अस्पताल के विभिन्न क्षेत्रों (जैसे रिसेप्शन, गलियारे, शौचालय) की नियमित जांच करना और यह सुनिश्चित करना कि सुरक्षा या सफाई में कोई चूक न हो।


5\. हाउसकीपिंग और सफाई प्रोटोकॉल:

- दैनिक बिस्तर बनाना और लिनन प्रबंधन: हाउसकीपिंग स्टाफ को यह सुनिश्चित करना है कि हर दिन बिस्तर ठीक से बनाए जाएं और लिनन की उपलब्धता की नियमित रिपोर्ट दी जाए।

- सुविधा निरीक्षण: अस्पताल के सभी क्षेत्रों (रोगी कमरे, बाथरूम, गलियारे) को साफ और अच्छी स्थिति में रखना। दैनिक निरीक्षण करना और दस्तावेज़ बनाना।


6\. कर्मचारी प्रशिक्षण और प्रदर्शन निगरानी:

- ओरिएंटेशन: नए कर्मचारियों को अस्पताल की प्रक्रियाओं पर एक विस्तृत ओरिएंटेशन देना, जिसमें सॉफ़्टवेयर उपयोग, बेड अलॉटमेंट, और बिलिंग प्रबंधन शामिल हो।

- समय की पाबंदी और उपस्थिति: कर्मचारियों की उपस्थिति को कड़ी निगरानी में रखना और देर से आने या बिना अनुमति के छुट्टी लेने के लिए परिणाम लागू करना।

- कर्मचारी आचरण: नर्सों और कर्मचारियों को पेशेवर आचरण मानकों का पालन करने के लिए कहना, जैसे रोगी संचार और स्वच्छता प्रोटोकॉल।


7\. आपातकालीन और गंभीर देखभाल प्रोटोकॉल:

- आपातकालीन प्रतिक्रिया: सभी कर्मचारियों को आपातकालीन परिस्थितियों से निपटने के लिए प्रशिक्षित करना। आपातकालीन स्थितियों में रोगी देखभाल के लिए स्पष्ट प्रोटोकॉल का पालन करना।

- उपकरण की उपलब्धता: यह सुनिश्चित करना कि सभी चिकित्सा उपकरण, जैसे वेंटिलेटर और ऑक्सीजन सिलेंडर, आपातकालीन उपयोग के लिए तैयार और कार्यशील स्थिति में हों।


8\. कर्मचारी रिपोर्टिंग जिम्मेदारियां:

- दैनिक रिपोर्टिंग: प्रत्येक इंचार्ज द्वारा दैनिक रिपोर्ट पेश की जानी चाहिए (जैसे नर्स, वार्ड बॉय, सुरक्षा) जिसमें उपकरण की स्थिति, रोगी देखभाल, और किसी भी मुद्दे का विवरण हो जो ध्यान देने की आवश्यकता हो।

- प्रतिक्रिया प्रणाली: रोगियों से दैनिक प्रतिक्रिया प्राप्त करना और यह सुनिश्चित करना कि इसे गुणवत्ता सुधार के लिए रिपोर्ट किया जाए।


9\. सुरक्षा गार्ड्स जिम्मेदारियां (नया प्रोटोकॉल):

- कर्मचारी बैग और पॉकेट चेक करना: सुरक्षा कर्मचारियों को कर्मचारियों के बैग और पॉकेट चेक करने की नीति लागू करनी है जब वे अस्पताल छोड़ रहे हों।

- सामग्री का फोटो लेना: सुरक्षा को यह सुनिश्चित करना है कि जो भी सामान अस्पताल में आ रहा या जा रहा है, उसकी फोटो ली जाए और सही रजिस्टर के साथ WhatsApp ग्रुप में शेयर की जाए।


### Hope Hospital - Security Staff Responsibilities:

1\. General Security and Administration:

- On induction day, The staff’s mobile and the leadership team’s mobile number are exchanged and all have to save each other’s Name along with the name in their mobile and also the number of the owner of the security agency.
- In case of a mob creating a ruckus, the police have to be contacted and then Suraj and Rahul have to be informed for reinforcement. The emergency contacts have to be displayed prominently in each floor of the hospital
- Maintaining Inward and Outward Register: Ensure records are kept of all equipment and items being moved into or out of the hospital. Photographs of the items must be taken and shared in the designated WhatsApp group.
- Employee Bag Checks: Bags of all employees are to be checked when entering or leaving the premises to prevent the entry or exit of prohibited items such as tobacco, alcohol, or other contraband. Carrying inflammable items, stove, lighter, matches etc.  is prohibited. Outside food is not allowed in hospital.
- Intercom Numbers should be known to all the staff. In case a visitor wants to meet a member of the leadership team. The guard should contact the member on intercom and should not leave the position to ask the member if the person can be let inside.
- Patient Bag and Pocket Checks: All patients and their families must have their bags and pockets checked upon entry to the hospital. Prohibited items should be confiscated.
- Lift Use: Ensure lifts are used exclusively for patient movement and not for staff use.
- Energy Consumption: Restrict excessive consumption of electricity across the hospital.
- Fire Safety: Ensure that staff are aware of how to start the fire pump in the event of a fire emergency. How to start the Generator and switch off the electrical mains should be known.How to use the fire extinguisher should be known.
- Mock Drills: Conduct regular mock drills for emergency preparedness.
- Staff Management: Maintain a register of key staff and their mobile numbers, ensuring proper identification of staff in emergencies.
- Mobile Phone Confiscation: Confiscate any mobile phones of employees found violating the hospital’s mobile usage policy.
- Equipment and Key Register: Keep detailed records of equipment and keys, ensuring they are accounted for during shift changes.

2\. Night Guards - Ayushman Hospital:

- Round-the-Clock Services: Ensure that night guard services are available 24/7. If the next shift employee fails to turn up, the staff must not leave until the shift is covered.
- Employee Bag and Pocket Checks: Night guards are responsible for checking employees’ bags and pockets as they leave the hospital.
- No Tobacco and Alcohol: Tobacco or kharra is strictly prohibited within hospital premises.
- Back Entry Gate: Keep the back entry gate open after 5 AM.
- Lift Management: Ensure that the lift is always available on the ground floor, and it should not be used for transporting staff from higher floors to the ground floor.
- Fire Pump Area Guarding: A guard must always be stationed near the fire pump area.
- Snap of Articles: Guards must take snapshots of all items being moved in and out and share them in the WhatsApp group, keeping a register of the same.

3\. Hospital Property and Personal Belongings Check:

- Bag Check Policy: All personal backpacks are prohibited from entering the hospital. A desk will be set up to check bags at the employee entrance. Daily checks will be conducted by security staff.
- Unauthorized Possession: Any unauthorized possession of hospital property such as medicines, IV bottles, or OT instruments will be dealt with according to the hospital’s policies.

* * *

### General Guidelines for Both Hospitals:

4\. Front Office Operations and Reporting:

- Patient Admission and Discharge: Ensure smooth patient admission and discharge processes by maintaining a register for all admitted and discharged patients. Ensure all documents and records are updated.
- OPD and IPD Tracking: Track the number of patients in OPD and IPD, and ensure that all necessary information is shared with the billing department on time.
- Consultation Records: Maintain accurate records for OPD consultations, including the categorization of patients by tariff type (e.g., private, Yojna).
- Staff Coordination and Communication: Ensure that the front desk is always manned and that staff follow all communication protocols, including using WhatsApp for sharing updates.
- CCTV Surveillance: Conduct periodic checks of hospital areas (e.g., reception, corridors, and toilets) to ensure no lapses in security or cleanliness.

5\. Housekeeping and Cleanliness Protocols:

- Daily Bed Making and Linen Management: Housekeeping staff should ensure that all beds are made daily with fresh linen and report linen availability regularly.
- Facility Inspection: Ensure that all hospital areas (patient rooms, bathrooms, and corridors) are clean and well-maintained. A daily inspection must be carried out and documented.

6\. Staff Training and Performance Monitoring:

- Orientation: New staff should receive a comprehensive orientation on hospital procedures, including software usage, bed allotment, and billing management.
- Punctuality and Attendance: Staff attendance must be monitored rigorously, with consequences for tardiness or unapproved leave.
- Employee Conduct: Nurses and staff must adhere to professional conduct standards, including patient communication and hygiene protocols.

7\. Emergency and Critical Care Protocols:

- Emergency Response: Ensure that all staff members are trained to handle emergencies. A clear protocol should be followed for patient care during emergencies (e.g., surgeries, critical care).
- Equipment Availability: Ensure that all medical equipment, including ventilators and oxygen cylinders, are readily available and in working condition for emergency use.

8\. Staff Responsibilities for Reporting:

- Daily Reporting: Daily reports should be submitted by all in-charges (e.g., nurses, ward boys, security) regarding the status of equipment, patient care, and any issues that need attention.
- Feedback System: Collect daily feedback from patients regarding their care and ensure it is reported for quality improvement.

* * *

9\. Security Guards Responsibilities (New Protocol):

- Bag and Pocket Check for Employees: Security will enforce the policy of checking employees' bags and pockets when they leave the hospital premises.
- Snap Posting: Security must take photos of any equipment or items moved in or out of the hospital and share them in the designated WhatsApp group, with a proper register maintained.

* * *

### Position: Operation Theatre (OT) technician and helper Staff  Department: Surgical Operations  Reports To: OT Supervisor / Senior Surgeon

### Job Responsibilities:

Should attend zoom meets at 9 am everyday. They have to know how to join zoom meets

1. Pre-Operative Preparation:


- Assist in preparing the operation theatre before surgery, including sterilizing instruments, setting up the required surgical equipment, and ensuring a sterile environment.

- Verify patient details and surgical procedure according to the operation schedule.

- Ensure that all necessary patient consent forms are signed before surgery.


2. Surgical Assistance:


- Assist surgeons and surgical teams during the operation by handing over surgical instruments, providing suction, and preparing sutures.

- Ensure the surgeon's needs are met and anticipate required equipment or assistance during the procedure.


3. Sterilization and Infection Control:


- Strictly adhere to infection control protocols by ensuring that all instruments, equipment, and surfaces in the OT are properly sterilized before and after use.

- Maintain cleanliness and sterilization of OT areas, including surgical instruments, drapes, and other accessories.

- Disinfect surfaces and equipment regularly and manage waste disposal following hospital guidelines.


4. Post-Operative Assistance:


- Note the surgery name, implant and anaesthesis type in the file and in whatsapp group
- Assist in transferring patients to recovery or post-op wards.

- Ensure that post-operative care instructions are followed, and appropriate documentation is completed.

- Maintain the post-operative condition of equipment and prepare for the next surgery.


5. Equipment Management:


- Take snaps of all instrument sets, Patient positions for various surgeries, types of plasters and thomas splint, tourniquet and snaps of table accessories for training purposes
- Ensure all surgical equipment is operational and ready for use. Perform routine checks on the surgical instruments before each operation.

- Post images of all equipments with a note that they are working
- Report any damaged or malfunctioning equipment immediately and coordinate repairs or replacements.

- Keep track of equipment usage and maintain proper inventory levels of medical supplies.


6. Patient Safety:


- Monitor patient vitals (temperature, heart rate, blood pressure) during surgery to ensure they remain stable.

- Assist in securing patients on the operating table and ensure proper positioning to minimize the risk of injury.

- Prepare and administer anesthesia or other medications under supervision, as required.


7. Documentation and Record-Keeping:


- All OT notes and consents to be shared in OT whatsapp group
- Fumigation register and autoclave registers to be posted in whatsapp group
- Maintain accurate records of surgeries performed, including surgical instruments used, patient details, and post-operative instructions.

- Update OT logs and patient surgical history promptly and accurately.

- Ensure that all forms and consent documents are correctly filled out and stored.


8. Collaboration with Surgical Team:


- Collaborate closely with surgeons, anesthetists, nurses, and other OT staff to ensure the smooth flow of operations.

- Participate in pre-surgical briefings and post-surgical debriefings to ensure effective communication.

- Ensure seamless transitions between shifts and coordinate with the next OT staff to prepare for the next surgery.


9. Handling of Medications and Implants:


- Assist in preparing medications, surgical instruments, and implants for the surgical procedure.

- Ensure that the correct surgical implants (e.g., pacemakers, stents) are used and documented appropriately.

- Safely manage and store drugs used during surgery.


10. Compliance with Hospital Protocols:


- Ensure that all surgical activities comply with hospital policies, health and safety regulations, and NABH standards.

- Attend mandatory training sessions on new surgical procedures, equipment, and infection control methods.

- Ensure adherence to hospital ethical standards and patient confidentiality protocols.


* * *

### Key Skills Required:

- Technical Skills: Knowledge of surgical instruments, sterilization methods, and patient care.

- Attention to Detail: Ensure precision in surgical preparations, equipment handling, and patient care.

- Communication: Clear communication with the surgical team to ensure smooth procedures.

- Time Management: Ability to manage multiple tasks in a high-pressure environment.

- Problem-Solving: Ability to resolve issues related to equipment malfunctions or operational challenges during surgery.


* * *

### Salary & Growth Opportunities:

- Salary in line with hospital standards and experience.

- Regular skill-enhancement training and workshops.

- Potential for promotion to senior OT roles or administrative positions within the surgical department.


Hospital Guidelines for nursing Staff and Patient Management:

1.Zoom app download ..id and password 9373111709

2\. Nurses can be asked to do duty in both hospitals.

Introduce yourself to patients

3\. Introduction of Consultants to Patients:

\- Ensure that every patient, including stable ones, is introduced to the attending consultant in half an hour. This is important for the clarity of care and building rapport with the patient.

4\. Room Management and Cleanliness:

Any patient room, whether occupied by a stable or discharged patient, should be cleaned or locked within half an hour of discharge. The room key should be promptly handed over to the Director’s chamber. This is to avoid misuse of rooms or potential mismanagement of hospital facilities.

5\. Prohibited Activities in Hospital:

\- No eating or bringing food inside the hospital premises.

\- No outside photography is allowed.

Consumption of alcohol or any prohibited substances within the hospital is strictly forbidden.

6\. Mobile Phone Policy:

\- Staff should handover their phones to reception during working hours to ensure professionalism and minimize distractions.

\- Staff should be mindful of maintaining uniform standards and punctuality. Always be in proper uniform and on time for shifts.

7\. Leave and Time-off:

\- Prior notice of at least 24 hours should be given for leave requests.

\- Mass leave should be avoided as it can disrupt hospital operations. For example, the previous incident where mass leave caused the hospital to be closed for two days is not acceptable.

8\. Strict Adherence to Guidelines:

\- Staff should ensure that they adhere to all the above guidelines, as failure to do so could disrupt hospital operations and lead to unnecessary challenges.

Welcome to the 816th Morning huddle -

The time has changed to 8.45 am.. The grace period refers to the amount of time after the official attendance time during which an employee can still arrive without facing a penalty or consequences. After this grace period, a penalty (such as a mark for tardiness) is typically applied to the employee's attendance record.

For example, if the work start time is 9:00 AM and the grace period is 15 minutes, employees can arrive by 9:15 AM without any penalty. If they arrive after that, a tardiness penalty may be imposed.

Eduslot by Gaurav -

Hope Hospital Staff Protocols for Enhanced Patient Experience and Efficiency

To improve the impression that Hope Hospital staff leave on patients, the following key areas have been identified for enhancement based on the hospital’s Standard Operating Procedures (SOPs) and Induction Manual.

Monthly Rule Cycle

- The rule designated for the 1st of the month will be repeated on the 16th.
- The rule for the 2nd of the month will be repeated on the 17th, and so forth.
- Gemba walk

* * *

1st of the Month – Financial Discipline

- All transactions must be recorded in the hospital software in real-time.
- Receipts must be issued for every payment, including those from the canteen.
- Staff, except those at the reception counter, must not ask for tips or money from patients.
- All payments must be made via UPI or bank transfer; cash transactions are prohibited.
- Cashiers will deposit all cash received, and payments will be made only through the bank.

* * *

2nd of the Month – Night Duty Alertness

- ICU lights must remain on, and curtains should be open at night.
- No staff member should sleep during duty hours.
- Mobile phones must be deposited at the counter before the shift.
- Every hour, staff must sign the alert register and call 18002330000 to confirm alertness.
- All ambulance services must be routed through Raftaar Emergency Services.
- Staff must switch off unused equipment and electrical devices. The staff operating the equipment will be responsible for its maintenance.

* * *

3rd of the Month – Patient Interaction & Communication

- Staff must greet and acknowledge patients warmly, addressing them by name when possible.
- Active listening should be encouraged, with a focus on empathy and understanding patient concerns.
- Staff should always use polite language and maintain professionalism.
- Basic phrases in Hindi and Marathi should be learned to communicate better with patients.
- Microsoft Office is not permitted for hospital communications; only Google Docs, Sheets, or Slides should be used.
- All corporate bills, discharge summaries, and OPD summaries must be processed within Hopesoftwares.com using ChatGPT API instead of Google Drive.
- Deceased patients must be properly labeled in the software to avoid follow-up calls by Raftaar telecallers.
- The hospital's call center must efficiently handle outgoing reminders and bulk WhatsApp messaging.

* * *

4th of the Month – Staff Appearance & Professionalism

- Staff must wear the designated uniform (blue shirt and black pants for front office and admin) along with their ID badge at all times.
- Personal hygiene and a professional appearance must be maintained.
- Regular training sessions will be conducted on professional behavior, ethics, and patient interaction.

* * *

5th of the Month – Patient Assistance & Guidance

- Lab and radiology reports or certificates must be completed within 30 minutes by the respective technician.
- Clear signage and personal guidance must be provided to help patients navigate the hospital.
- Dedicated personnel must assist elderly patients, pregnant women, and disabled patients.
- Helpdesks must be staffed 24/7 to answer patient queries.

* * *

6th of the Month – Response Time to Patient Needs

- All OPD and new stable IPD admissions must be attended to immediately.
- Patient inquiries must be responded to within 5-10 minutes.
- Doctors and nurses must see patients within 30 minutes of admission.
- Staff must escalate patient concerns within 3 minutes for immediate resolution.

* * *

7th of the Month – Patient Feedback Mechanism

- Every discharged patient must provide written or video feedback.
- A weekly review of complaints will be conducted during morning huddles, with corrective actions taken.
- Staff must encourage patients to use the “Speak Up” policy to share their concerns, ensuring prompt action.

* * *

8th of the Month – Facility Cleanliness & Comfort

- Daily cleaning inspections must be conducted for toilets, wards, and common areas.
- Air fresheners should be used in wards to control odor and maintain fresh ventilation.
- Rooms must be deep cleaned and prepared within 30 minutes of patient discharge.

* * *

9th of the Month – Patient Safety & Security

- Escort services must be provided for patients during movement inside and outside the hospital.
- Staff must be trained to follow emergency protocols and assist patients efficiently.
- Medication administration must be double-checked using barcode scanning.

* * *

10th of the Month – Staff Morale & Training on being loyal to Hope

- Loyalty to Hope hospital will be given priority in deciding employee of the week/month/year
- Employee of the Month awards will recognize outstanding staff members esp marketing and sales executives.
- Weekly soft skills training will be conducted on communication, conflict resolution, and emotional intelligence.
- Team-building activities will be organized, including turf cricket watches competitions, awards, and outings.

* * *

11th of the Month – Leveraging Technology for Efficiency

- Microsoft software is banned in Hope Hospital. All data must be maintained in hospital software and Google Docs.
- Digital Queue Management must be implemented to reduce patient wait times.
- Staff must have instant access to patient records to prevent service delays.
- Automated WhatsApp and SMS updates must notify patients about reports, appointments, and payments.

* * *

12th of the Month – [Building a Positive Hospital Culture](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1BQRgHQ5NMqtfuDZnusofDrTxSTlGIzpwYKfp450CMFs/edit?tab%3Dt.0&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181178338&usg=AOvVaw3DVg2zyKJiuK0yUojXbwn7)

- Staff must maintain a positive attitude in WhatsApp groups and meetings.
- Each department must take ownership of patient satisfaction.
- Daily leadership rounds by senior management (Shrikant, Suraj, and Gaurav) must ensure patient engagement and issue resolution.

* * *

13th of the Month – Marketing & Patient Follow-Ups

- Reminder calls for OPD and discharged patients must be completed by the 5th day after discharge/OPD
- Physical follow-up calls must be made by field marketing staff:

- Nagpur-based referees by the 15th
- Outstation referees by the 30th

* * *

14th of the Month – Financial Transparency & Efficiency

- Vendor payments must be reviewed and submitted for approval in the morning.
- All financial transactions, including billing and expenses, must be reconciled in Tally, not hospital software.
- A daily cash flow analysis must be conducted for Hope and Ayushman hospitals.
- The finance team must review liabilities and future expenses to ensure financial sustainability.
- Monthly and quarterly budget planning must be conducted, adjusting forecasts based on the past month's performance.
- Major expenditures must receive advance approval from the Director.

* * *

15th of the Month – HR & Staff Salary Compliance

- Salaries for Reception, OPD Nurses, Billing, and Pharmacy staff must be processed between the 12th and 15th.
- Devendra Yada’s salaries must also be paid on this date.
- A “Go Green” performance assessment, similar to BNI, must evaluate attendance, professionalism, and teamwork.
- Staff must complete mandatory training sessions (billing, OPD procedures, patient safety) and acknowledge policy updates via Google Docs.
- Payroll discrepancies must be reported by the 15th, with HR resolving them within three working days.
- Attendance records must be finalized, and any unauthorized absences reported to department heads.

* * *

Whatsapp group review:

Maintenance :Wednesday and saturdays will be solar panel cleaning days. Update -                 We need list of engineers to call fir lift and pump

1\. Emergency & Disaster Preparedness ( night alert group,  Maintainance, handover, nurses groups)

- There is no mention of a disaster response plan for mass casualties, natural disasters, fires, or cybersecurity breaches.
- The emergency evacuation protocol should be clearly defined for all hospital departments.
- Mock drills for disaster response need to be conducted and documented regularly.

2\. Comprehensive Risk Management ( litigation group)

- The document mentions financial risks, operational inefficiencies, and technology adoption, but there is no clear plan for risk mitigation.
- Cybersecurity threats, such as data breaches in HMIS or hacking of financial transactions, need better-defined countermeasures.
- Legal and compliance risks (such as lawsuits, insurance fraud prevention, or consent form handling) should have a detailed section.
- [" List of crisis situations - Risk Management and Insurance in Healthcare."](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1rYcuQm_m_ZIjq3C3sGWvjMFw1bJHegC93AEfTvdX06I/edit?tab%3Dt.0%23heading%3Dh.g4gy1xyhjjft&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181189692&usg=AOvVaw1kYTmqeRbm6KyNiwFZb-Id)

3\. Patient Rights & Ethics Policies (appreciation testimonial group)

- The document lacks a structured patient rights and ethics policy.
- Informed consent procedures for treatments and high-risk surgeries need clear guidelines.
- Handling of patient grievances, second opinions, and dispute resolution mechanisms are not well-defined.

4\. Inventory & Supply Chain Management (equipment group, Nurses group)

- A shortage of critical hospital items (e.g., emergency drugs, ventilators, or implants) is mentioned, but there is no structured procurement or forecasting mechanism.
- A minimum stock level policy for life-saving drugs and disposables should be in place.
- There should be automated tracking of stock with alerts for refilling before shortages occur.

5\. Continuous Medical Education (CME) & Training (doctors only group )

- There is no structured plan for continuous training of hospital staff (nurses, RMOs, front office, billing).
- Specialized skills development like CPR training, first-aid for industrial injuries, or handling pediatric and geriatric emergencies should be emphasized.
- Patient counseling skills training for doctors and receptionists should be introduced.

6\. Marketing & Community Engagement (marketing group)

- Check if google and justdial listing is top ranking,. social media posts in instagram and Mobile numbers are live and active in google business listing (Raftaar tester to report-)
- While there is a focus on referral marketing, the hospital lacks a clear PR and branding strategy to boost awareness.
- Social media and online reputation management need a structured review cycle.
- CSR initiatives, free health camps, and patient education workshops should be part of community outreach.

7\. Staff Mental Health & Well-being ( Late, absent group)

- There are no mental health or burnout management programs for doctors, nurses, and frontline workers.
- Employee assistance programs (EAPs) for counseling and psychological support should be included.
- A structured staff feedback and grievance redressal policy is missing.

8\. Ambulance & Emergency Services Protocol ( mohan nagar group- raftaar)

- Response time metrics for ambulance dispatch are not mentioned.
- There should be a digital tracking system for monitoring ambulance movements.
- Paramedic training for ambulance staff should be standardized.

9\. NABH Accreditation & Compliance Tracking (SOP & doctors only group)

- The document mentions NABH standards, but there is no structured compliance checklist.
- Internal quality audits should be conducted at regular intervals.
- Clinical indicators tracking (like infection rates, mortality rates, and readmission rates) should be structured.

10\. Revenue Leakage & Financial Audits ( Accounts group will be reviewed after the open morning huddle)

- The financial policy does not address revenue leakage due to incorrect billing, wastage, or fraud.
- Outsourced service contracts (like pathology labs and diagnostic centers) should have a structured review system.
- Internal financial fraud detection mechanisms should be mentioned.

* * *

7 quiz questions

based on the SOP document that can be asked in the morning huddle to ensure staff engagement and awareness of hospital protocols:

1️⃣ Financial Discipline (1st & 16th of the Month)

Question:

What is the hospital’s policy on cash transactions for patient payments?

✅ Answer: Cash transactions are prohibited. All payments must be made via UPI or bank transfer, and receipts must be issued for every transaction.

* * *

2️⃣ Night Duty Alertness (2nd & 17th of the Month)

Question:

What steps should ICU night-duty staff take to ensure alertness during their shift?

✅ Answer:

- ICU lights must remain on, and curtains should be open at night.
- Staff must sign the alert register every hour and call 18002330000 to confirm alertness.
- Mobile phones must be deposited before the shift.

* * *

3️⃣ Patient Interaction & Communication (3rd & 18th of the Month)

Question:

How should staff communicate with patients to ensure a positive experience?

✅ Answer:

- Greet and acknowledge patients warmly, addressing them by name.
- Use polite and professional language at all times.
- Learn basic phrases in Hindi & Marathi for better communication.
- Avoid using Microsoft Office; instead, use Google Docs, Sheets, or Slides for documentation.

* * *

4️⃣ Facility Cleanliness & Comfort (8th & 23rd of the Month)

Question:

What are the three key cleanliness standards that must be maintained in patient rooms and wards?

✅ Answer:

1. Daily cleaning inspections must be conducted.
2. Air fresheners should be used to control odor and maintain fresh ventilation.
3. Rooms must be deep cleaned and prepared within 30 minutes of patient discharge.

* * *

5️⃣ Patient Safety & Security (9th & 24th of the Month)

Question:

How should staff ensure proper medication administration and patient safety?

✅ Answer:

- Use barcode scanning to double-check medication administration.
- Escort services must be provided for patients moving inside and outside the hospital.
- Follow emergency protocols and assist patients efficiently.

* * *

6️⃣ Leveraging Technology for Efficiency (11th & 26th of the Month)

Question:

What technologies are required for smooth hospital operations, and which software is banned?

✅ Answer:

- Microsoft software is banned in Hope Hospital.
- Digital Queue Management must be implemented to reduce wait times.
- WhatsApp and SMS updates must notify patients about reports, appointments, and payments.

* * *

7️⃣ HR & Staff Salary Compliance (15th & 30th of the Month)

Question:

By which date should staff salaries be processed, and what must employees do to ensure compliance?

✅ Answer:

- Salaries for Reception, OPD Nurses, Billing, and Pharmacy staff must be processed between 12th and 15th of the month.
- Employees must complete mandatory training sessions and acknowledge policy updates on Google Docs.
- Payroll discrepancies must be reported by the 15th, and HR must resolve them within 3 working days.

* * *

📌 How to Conduct the Quiz in the Morning Huddle:

1️⃣ Ask one question daily at random to different staff members.

2️⃣ Encourage a team-based quiz format with quick rewards (e.g., “Star of the Day” recognition).

3️⃣ Use role-play scenarios to reinforce key protocols.

4️⃣ Track who answered correctly and recognize active participation.

### Staff Training Plan – Hope/Ayushman Hospital & Raftaar

Training Responsibility

As on 21st march 2025, “Training and HR” will now be established as a high-level critical department alongside “Private Doctor Marketing and Security “(headed by Suraj), “Corporate Liaisoning and Marketing” (currently led by Shrikant), Raftaar technology and startup (currently led by Aman Rajak), and Finance of Hope group (overseen by Gaurav). All these will be independently managed by these leaders and directly report to the CMD, Dr Murali BK

- Lead Trainers: Dr Muralii will conduct the first training in each department starting with reception during morning huddle (and between 5pm to 6 PM) on 21st, 22nd and 23rd of March. This session will be recorded for future training. It is compulsory for the leadership team to attend so that they are able to train the rest of the staff. The future training will be held by lead trainers and leadership team. Gaauravand Suraj will be support directors of all training.  Gaurav and Abhishek (Primary trainers) have been appointed as lead trainers since they are physically present in all morning huddles for the last few months and to effectively address the staff, physical presence at 9 am is essential.
- Supporting Trainers (for front office staff): Kajal, Chetna, Shashank, and other leadership team members with over one year of experience in training and operations.
- Induction Sessions: Each key staff member must conduct a session as per the annual training and  sign-off induction sheet. [Annual Training  and Induction sheet](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1mn7-LGEmY4JtI3YLYB6JumbgRN9ZcLZ6miQF8uGJI_c/edit?tab%3Dt.0&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181216437&usg=AOvVaw1If_P-AkuL7cIhCwOZnmYr)

* * *

Why Training is Important?

- Instances like Sonum handling corporate patients without proper training led to serious patient dissatisfaction.
- Structured training ensures consistent service quality, minimizes errors, and improves patient satisfaction.
- The same training must be repeated for every newly appointed staff and regular repeat training of present employees is necessary to maintain standards.
- Recent feedback from patients have shown that majority of negative feedback from patients have been because of lack of coordination at frot desk
