Training Schedule & Attendance Guidelines – Hope/Ayushman Hospital & Raftaar

Training Timings

- Morning Huddle: Daily at 9:00 AM (Mandatory for all staff).
- Evening Training Hour: 5:00 PM – 6:00 PM (Dedicated training slot).
- Attendance: Compulsory for all front office, security (guards, male/female bouncers), admin, and billing staff.

Front Office Training & Huddle Management

- Conducted By: Gaurav and Abhishek will lead all training sessions and morning huddles.
- Strict Discipline: The sessions will not be interrupted unless explicitly requested by the trainers.

Attendance & Guest Registration

- Zoom Guest Form: A mandatory form must be filled for all guests joining the morning huddle via Zoom.
- Attendance Coordinator: Kajal is responsible for ensuring full participation and maintaining attendance records.

Security Staff Training

- Guards and Bouncers will undergo the same training as front office staff.
- They must be trained to handle reception duties, including answering calls when receptionists are busy.

Discussion Guidelines for Morning Huddle & Training Sessions

- Focus on Positivity: Only good deeds, recognitions, and positive staff contributions will be discussed.
- Maintaining a Professional Image: Since external guests will be present, discussions should highlight the hospital’s strengths.
- No Negative Discussions: Patient complaints, staff mistakes, or operational concerns will not be addressed during these sessions.

Addressing Performance Issues

- MCOM Meeting (Post-Huddle Discussion):

- Any staff concerns, criticisms, or negative feedback will be handled privately in the MCOM meeting.
- Attended by key leadership team members, this meeting will focus on staff performance, problem resolution, and operational improvements.

* * *

Structured Training Program for Front Office Staff/Telecallers for enquiries related to Hope group of hospitals

1\. Defining Roles & Responsibilities

To prevent operational confusion, responsibilities must be clearly separated: 4 videos will be shared in the training channel - [https://www.youtube.com/@ayushmanhospital7459](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.youtube.com/@ayushmanhospital7459&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181224705&usg=AOvVaw1y8KLzfQokmsXUsDi8GrY_)

| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Task | Responsible Person |
| Video 1 | Handling Reception Calls & Patient Queries | Senior receptionist on duty and Raftaar Telecallers |
| Video 2 | Patient Admissions & Front Desk Queries | Pragati and Azhar (Receptionist) |
| Video 3 | Patient Photos & Video Feedback Collection | Sonum and Jagruti(Patient Experience Executive) |
| Video 4 | Billing & Financial Transactions | Front desk, billing and accounts team |

Device Allocation Plan

- Reception Mobile: Used only for answering calls and WhatsApp queries.
- Video Collection Mobile: Used only for patient feedback collection and documentation (Handled by Sonum and Jagruti).
- Labeling & Assignment: Devices should be clearly labeled, and staff trained on their specific usage.
- If only one mobile is available, prioritize call answering and schedule fixed time slots for video collection say, 1 PM to 2 PM.

* * *

A list of key things the front office staff needs to know to ensure smooth operations:

1. Key decision makes, leadership team of Hope group
2. How to log into zoom using ID and Passcode -9373111709
3. How to introduce yourself to our clients and patients
4. Consultant Names and Schedules:


- The front office staff must be familiar with the names, departments, and working hours of consultants. For example, Dr. Suhas Tiple is a clinician specializing in chest-related procedures, working from 9 AM to 11 AM and 3 PM to 5 PM .
- It’s essential for the front office to track consultant availability and ensure that the patients are assigned the correct consultants based on their specialties.

5. Common Diagnoses and Surgeries:


- Front office staff must know the common diagnoses associated with each department and be able to recognize the basic categories of surgeries. For example:

- Orthopedic surgeries like arthroscopic procedures .
- Cardiological procedures such as coronary angiograms (CAG), and percutaneous coronary interventions (PTCA) .
- Radiology including ultrasound and CT/MRI scans .

6. Surgical Procedures:


- The front office needs to be aware of different types of surgeries and their corresponding billing codes, such as:

- Arthroscopy with implants .
- CAG and PTCA in cardiology .
- Spinal surgeries with specific implant cost caps .

7. Corporates and TPAs  - Admission and Billing Procedures:


- It is crucial for front office staff to accurately update billing information related to consultation, surgical procedures, and diagnostic tests. For example:

- Ensure that the consultation fees for OPD and IPD patients are accurately entered .
- Be familiar with payment procedures and corporate billing requirements .

8. Patient Records and Documentation - fitness certificates :


- Medical records must be kept up to date with diagnoses, consultation summaries, and discharge details .
- Front office staff should be involved in maintaining registers like OPD/ IPD, death and birth records, and referral registers .

9. Surgeon and Consultant Payment Protocols:


- The front office must know the payment protocols for surgeons, including surgeon fees for specific cases like MJPJAY and PMJAY .

10. Handling Emergency Situations:


- Front office staff should be well-versed in handling emergency situations, including:

- Notifying the relevant consultant for critical care or specialist referrals .
- Coordinating with security staff and medical teams for immediate patient care.

11. Discharge/ Death / Dama Procedures:


- Discharge summaries must be verified by consultants, ensuring the correct treatment plan is in place before the patient leaves .
- The front office staff should confirm final payments before processing patient discharges .

* * *

2\. Time Management & Workflow Training

- Conduct a brief daily training session during Morning huddle on handling multiple tasks without missing calls or delaying documentation.
- Workflow Design for Efficiency:

- Reception staff should focus on call handling and patient queries.
- The video collection team should not engage in call answering.

Example Workflow:

1. Patient arrives → Pragati (Receptionist) handles admissions & initial queries.
2. Consultation & treatment → Queries handled via WhatsApp/call.
3. Feedback Collection → Sonum captures video feedback separately.

* * *

3\. Implementing a Backup System for Missed Calls

To ensure zero missed patient queries, implement a tracking system:

✅ Missed Call Log Register:

- All missed calls must be logged and returned within 10 minutes.
- A dedicated staff member ensures all calls are addressed before shift ends.

   ✅ WhatsApp Auto-Reply Setup:
- Instant auto-reply message:

  "Thank you for contacting Hope Hospital. Our team will get back to you shortly."

   ✅ Call Forwarding System:
- If the receptionist is unavailable, calls are automatically forwarded to a backup staff member or Raftaar toll-free number.

* * *

4\. Coordination via WhatsApp Group

Internal WhatsApp Group – “Shifting Patients, Reception…”

- Reception staff must post the missed call log at the end of each shift.
- Updates about patient movement, pending admissions, and unresolved queries should be posted daily.

* * *

5\. Alternative Solutions for Efficient Operations

✅ Hands-Free Equipment:

- Provide one side earphone to reception staff to handle calls while multitasking.

   ✅ Dedicated Chat Support:
- Assign a separate phone number for WhatsApp queries if patient inquiries increase.

   ✅ Automated Call Handling:
- Calls should be redirected to a toll-free number if the receptionist is engaged in another task.

* * *

6\. Daily Monitoring & Continuous Improvement

✅ Daily Morning Huddle (9 AM):

- Review missed calls & unresolved queries \- in the whatsapp group “ shifting and reception”
- Check video feedback collection efficiency.

   ✅ Role Rotation (Every 15 Days):
- Staff should be trained on different responsibilities (call handling, video collection, admissions).

   ✅ Review of Feedback & Performance:
- Regularly assess patient feedback and adjust training as needed.

* * *

Training Topics Based on Patient Feedback

1. Patient Communication

- Handling difficult or frustrated patients professionally.
- Using polite, clear, and empathetic language.

2. Response Time Improvement

- Ensuring patients receive prompt attention to avoid delays.
- Reducing waiting times at the reception desk and billing counter.

3. Complaint Resolution & Escalation

- Training staff on how to handle complaints effectively.
- When to escalate issues to senior management.

4. Front Office SOP Training

- Admission process and handling corporate & private patients.
- Managing billing, documentation, and patient records.

5. Technology Training

- Proper use of hospital management software for tracking patient interactions, billing, and scheduling.

6. Role-Playing & Simulation

- Conduct mock drills on handling emergency patient cases at reception.

* * *

7\. Regular Evaluation & Recognition

✅ Performance Monitoring:

- Track individual performance based on call handling, patient feedback, and complaint resolution.

   ✅ Incentives & Recognition:
- Reward staff members who excel in patient communication and efficiency.
- Acknowledge their efforts during team meetings.

By implementing this structured training program, Hope and Ayushman Hospital can significantly enhance front office efficiency, reduce patient complaints, and improve overall patient satisfaction. 🚀

* * *

Execution details and structured accountability mechanisms.

A clear SOPs on escalation to prevent operational chaos has to be described.

Updated Escalation Procedures for Receptionists

To ensure a smooth and efficient escalation process, the following escalation hierarchy must be strictly adhered to in Ayushman Hospital:

1\. Handling Violent Patients or Aggressive Relatives

When faced with an aggressive patient or relative, the receptionist should follow these steps:

- Step 1: Attempt de-escalation using calm, empathetic, and professional communication.
- Step 2: If the situation escalates or cannot be managed by the receptionist, immediately contact Suraj (Head of Private Patient Management) for intervention. Call nearest Police station. The contact numbers of various police station are. …Rahul Bouncer also should be immediately informed
- Step 3: If Suraj is unavailable, Gaaurav(Head of Corporate Patient Liaison) should be contacted for further assistance.
- Step 4: If neither Suraj nor Gaauravis available, escalate the issue to Gaurav, Kajal, or Shripad (leaders of different departments within Ayushman Hospital) to address the situation.
- Step 5: If all these contacts are unavailable, the situation must be immediately escalated to Dr. Murali BK (CMD), who will handle the issue personally.

2\. Handling Critical Incidents like Mob Violence or Medical Errors

For critical incidents such as mob violence or medical errors:

- Step 1: The receptionist should prioritize patient and staff safety by contacting the security team headed by Rahul immediately.  Call nearest Police station.
- Step 2: After ensuring the safety of those involved, contact Suraj for any violent incidents or emergencies with private patients.
- Step 3: If Suraj is unavailable, Gaauravshould be contacted, especially if corporate patients are involved.
- Step 4: If neither Suraj nor Gaauravis available, the receptionist should escalate the issue to Gaurav, Kajal, or Shripad for immediate action.
- Step 5: If these contacts are unavailable, escalate the issue immediately to Dr. Murali BK (CMD).

3\. Handling Medical Errors or Malpractice Allegations

For medical errors or allegations involving malpractice:

- Step 1: The receptionist should document the incident thoroughly, including patient details and any involved medical personnel.
- Step 2: Notify Suraj (for private patients) or Gaaurav(for corporate patients) for an initial review of the case.
- Step 3: If neither Suraj nor Gaauravis available, contact Gaurav, Kajal, or Shripad for further escalation and resolution.
- Step 4: If none of the above contacts is available, immediately escalate the issue to Dr. Murali BK (CMD).

4\. Handling General Operational Issues

For day-to-day operational challenges, such as delays in patient care or resource unavailability:

- Step 1: The receptionist should attempt to resolve minor issues directly or escalate them to the relevant department.
- Step 2: If the issue remains unresolved within a reasonable time, contact Gaurav or Aman. For equipment related issues , BME Atul should be contacted immediately/
- Step 3: If Gaurav/Atul  or Aman are unavailable, escalate the matter to Kajal, or Shripad for assistance.
- Step 4: If all the above are unavailable, escalate the issue immediately to Dr. Murali BK (CMD).

5\. Emergency Protocol During Night Shifts

During night shifts, if Suraj and Gaauravare unavailable:

- Step 1: The night in-charge, such as Kajal or Shripad, will take over the escalation process. They will coordinate with the security team and other departments to ensure proper handling of the situation.
- Step 2: If neither Kajal nor Shripad is available, the issue must be immediately escalated to Dr. Murali BK (CMD).

* * *

Updated Escalation Flowchart

|     |     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Incident Type | Escalation Process | Primary Contact | Secondary Contact | Tertiary Contact | Final Contact |
| Violent Patient / Aggressive Relative | Attempt de-escalation -> Suraj -> Gaaurav-> Gaurav/Kajal/Shripad -> Dr. Murali BK | Suraj, Rahul (Private Patient Lead) | Gaaurav(Corporate Lead) | Gaurav, Kajal, Shripad (Leads) | Dr. Murali BK (CMD) |
| Mob Violence / Critical Incident | Immediate action -> Suraj -> Gaaurav-> Gaurav/Kajal/Shripad -> Dr. Murali BK | Suraj, Rahul (Private Patient Lead) | Gaaurav(Corporate Lead) | Gaurav, Kajal, Shripad (Leads) | Dr. Murali BK (CMD) |
| Medical Error / Malpractice | Document incident -> Suraj -> Gaaurav-> Gaurav/Kajal/Shripad -> Dr. Murali BK | Suraj (Private Patient Lead) | Gaaurav(Corporate Lead) | Gaurav, Kajal, Shripad (Leads) | Dr. Murali BK (CMD) |
| General Operational Issues | Resolve -> Suraj -> Gaaurav-> Gaurav/Kajal/Shripad -> Dr. Murali BK | Gaurav, Atul, Aman | Gaaurav(Corporate Lead) | Kajal, Shripad (Leads) | Dr. Murali BK (CMD) |
| Night Shift Issues | Immediate escalation -> Kajal/Shripad -> Dr. Murali BK | Kajal (HR Lead) | Shripad (Raftaar Lead) | Dr. Murali BK (CMD) |  |

General Operational Issues - Electrical, carpenter, Plumbing issues to be sorted by calling and scheduling a UC app service agent and posting in the maintenance whatsapp group! Escalate to the president if not resolved in 3 hours.

Improvements to the Training Plan

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Issue Identified | Improvement Suggestion |
| structured evaluation | Introduce weekly quizzes every saturday during morning huddle, role-play assessments, and patient feedback surveys post-training. |
| Roles in training responsibilities | Primary and backup trainers ( Kajal and Chetna)  assigned to avoid confusion. Clearly define roles in a responsibility matrix. |
| Emergency handling training | Add crisis management drills for receptionists, security staff, and RMOs. Include sessions on handling irate patients, mob control, and medical negligence complaints. |
| Over-reliance on WhatsApp groups | Implement a hospital CRM dashboard for real-time tracking of patient queries and staff performance instead of relying on WhatsApp. |
| Concrete incentive system | Create a structured rewards system for high-performing staff and penalties for repeated inefficiencies (e.g., warning letters, training refreshers). |
| Missing department-specific training | Expand training to nurses (infection control, ICU protocols), RMOs (clinical documentation, medical ethics), billing staff (insurance handling, fraud prevention), and marketing teams (referral management). |
| Cybersecurity & patient data privacy training | Conduct annual cybersecurity training to ensure compliance with data protection laws and prevent patient data leaks. |

Additional Enhancements to be suggested by Trainers:

1. Case Studies & Real-Life Examples


- Incorporate real scenarios from past patient complaints or operational mishaps.
- Example: "A patient complained about being given the wrong package estimate. How should the reception staff handle this?"

2. Regular Cross-Training Between Departments


- Receptionists should know basic billing.
- Security staff should be able to handle emergency situations at the front desk.
- RMOs should understand insurance claim documentation.

3. Formal Training Manual & Video Library

   videos will be shared in the training channel - [https://www.youtube.com/@ayushmanhospital7459](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.youtube.com/@ayushmanhospital7459&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181305581&usg=AOvVaw01RwO-ZK4zyw0OGcO3Sjl2)

- Create a digital training library where employees can revisit sessions.
- Provide PDF guides on critical SOPs.

4. Annual Refresher Training


- Conduct mandatory refreshers every 6 months to reinforce training.

In addition to the history of the hospital, its staff strength, departments and organogram what are the other information needed for the owner of 2 hospitals Hope hospital and Ayushman nagpur hospital and a startup - raftaar help emergency seva to be added as knowledge in chatgpt to help make critical decisions in management and help improve the occupancy of the hospitals

To further assist the owner of Hope Hospital, Ayushman Nagpur Hospital, and Raftaar Help Emergency Seva in making critical management decisions and improving occupancy, it would be beneficial to add the following areas of knowledge for the monthly meeting to be held on 2nd of everymonth!:

Agenda - monthly meeting  -  for Critical Management Decisions and Occupancy Improvement

In monthly meting a detailed information is to be discussed for the management of Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital, including the startup Raftaar Help Emergency Seva, that can assist in making informed and critical decisions. This information will help optimize hospital operations, improve patient occupancy, and streamline resource management. The areas to be covered include:

1. Hospital Operational Metrics and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs): Kajal


- Current and target occupancy rates for both hospitals.

- Average patient length of stay (LOS) and patient turnover.

- Admission and discharge trends over 3 years
- Conversion rates from OPD to IPD over 3 years.

- Patient wait times and their impact on satisfaction.


2. Financial Performance and Cost Management:Gaurav


- Detailed revenue reports, including breakdowns by service (e.g., surgeries, diagnostics, consultation fees).

- Tracking of accounts payable
- Strategies to manage cash flow, particularly for high-cost surgeries and cashless patients.

- Monthly, quarterly, and annual financial summaries, including profitability analysis.


3. Marketing and Patient Acquisition Strategies: Suraj


- Patient acquisition strategies to increase hospital visibility and attract new patients (e.g., digital marketing, local partnerships, outreach programs).

- Community engagement strategies (health camps, free check-ups, seminars).

- Effectiveness of referral programs and patient retention techniques.

- Branding and promotional efforts to raise awareness about hospital specialties and services.

- Social media strategies and website traffic analytics for patient leads.


4. Staff Training, Development, and Performance Management: Gaurav, Abhishek


- Staff development programs, including continuous education, certifications, and skill enhancements.

- Training schedules for both clinical and non-clinical staff (e.g., billing staff, front office operations, nurses, security).

- Performance evaluation systems and feedback loops to improve staff engagement and satisfaction.

- Leadership and management training for senior hospital executives.

- Staff absenteeism, turnover rates, and recruitment strategies.


5. Patient Experience and Service Quality:Kajal


- Methods for improving patient satisfaction (e.g., feedback collection, response times, service protocols).

- Ensuring the quality of patient care across various departments (ICU, OPD, IPD, Emergency).

- Patient complaint management systems and their effectiveness.

- Regular patient surveys and the implementation of their feedback.

- Hygiene, room cleanliness, and maintenance protocols to ensure a pleasant patient environment.


7. Compliance, Risk Management, and Legal Considerations: Gaurav


- Adherence to healthcare regulations (e.g., NABH accreditation, medical licensing, patient safety protocols).

- Regular audit reports for financial, operational, and clinical processes.

- Legal matters regarding patient disputes, insurance claims, and corporate policies.

- Risk management strategies for both hospitals, including insurance and emergency preparedness.


8. Technology and IT Integration: Aman


- Use of hospital management software for patient records, billing, and operational reporting.

- Integration of telemedicine platforms and digital health tools for better patient engagement.

- Maintenance of the hospital’s IT infrastructure to avoid downtime and system errors.

- Data security and patient privacy measures in line with legal requirements.

- Automation in patient appointment scheduling, lab report generation, and discharge summaries.


9. Emergency and Critical Care Management (Raftaar Help Emergency Seva):Aman


- Operational effectiveness of the Raftaar Emergency Seva (ambulance services, emergency response times, and technology integration).
- Internet marketing and SEO for Raftaar and 3 other companies - Ambufast Pvt ltd, Hope ambulance, Ayushaman Ambulance  and its effectiveness

- Coordination between hospitals and ambulance services for optimal patient transportation.

- Managing emergency patient cases, including critical care protocols and response time.

- Geolocation tracking, real-time updates, and ambulance fleet management.

- Partnerships with local ambulance providers and other healthcare services.


10. Sustainability and Long-Term Strategic Goals:Dr Murali

Long-term strategic plans to improve hospital infrastructure (e.g., expansion, equipment upgrades).

- Sustainable financial planning and cost-saving measures (e.g., green technologies, reducing waste).

- Expanding the service portfolio based on emerging medical needs and community demands (e.g., pediatric care, geriatric care, diagnostic imaging).

- Future collaborations with TPAs,  insurance providers, government healthcare schemes, and corporate partnerships.especially for Ayushman nagpur hospital and Raftaar..
- Bed Management, Ward Utilization, and Capacity Planning:Gaauravincludes billing


- Effective strategies for bed allocation and management to optimize occupancy.

- Identifying and managing underutilized beds or rooms (e.g., optimizing premium rooms for private patients).

- Shifting patients between wards and hospitals  to manage demand during peak times.
- Billing discrepancies and their resolution process (including corporate billing).
- Tracking of accounts receivable including TPA payments and insurance settlements.

Murali’s dream was to own his own hospital.In 2005 he finally managed to collect enough funds from family to build his own hospital. A beautiful state of the art hospital with 35 beds.This was a risk as he was only 30 plus a young surgeon who independently financed and started HOPE Hospital.

### Security Staff Responsibilities:

1\. General Security and Administration:

- On induction day, The staff’s mobile and the leadership team’s mobile number are exchanged and all have to save each other’s Name along with the name in their mobile and also the number of the owner of the security agency.
- Most important task is to lock all patient rooms not in use…It has been noticed that the ward boys and other staff utilise the rooms not in use.
- In case of a mob creating a ruckus, the police have to be contacted and then Suraj and Rahul have to be informed for reinforcement. The emergency contacts have to be displayed prominently in each floor of the hospital
- Maintaining Inward and Outward Register: Ensure records are kept of all equipment and items being moved into or out of the hospital. Photographs of the items must be taken and shared in the designated WhatsApp group.
- Employee Bag Checks: Bags of all employees are to be checked when entering or leaving the premises to prevent the entry or exit of prohibited items such as tobacco, alcohol, or other contraband. Carrying inflammable items, stove, lighter, matches etc.  is prohibited. Outside food is not allowed in hospital.
- Intercom Numbers should be known to all the staff. In case a visitor wants to meet a member of the leadership team. The guard should contact the member on intercom and should not leave the position to ask the member if the person can be let inside.
- Patient Bag and Pocket Checks: All patients and their families must have their bags and pockets checked upon entry to the hospital. Prohibited items should be confiscated.
- Lift Use: Ensure lifts are used exclusively for patient movement and not for staff use.
- Energy Consumption: Restrict excessive consumption of electricity across the hospital.
- Fire Safety: Ensure that staff are aware of how to start the fire pump in the event of a fire emergency. How to start the Generator and switch off the electrical mains should be known.How to use the fire extinguisher should be known.
- Mock Drills: Conduct regular mock drills for emergency preparedness.
- Staff Management: Maintain a register of key staff and their mobile numbers, ensuring proper identification of staff in emergencies.
- Mobile Phone Confiscation: Confiscate any mobile phones of employees found violating the hospital’s mobile usage policy.
- Equipment and Key Register: Keep detailed records of equipment and keys, ensuring they are accounted for during shift changes.

2\. Night Guards - Ayushman Hospital:

- Round-the-Clock Services: Ensure that night guard services are available 24/7. If the next shift employee fails to turn up, the staff must not leave until the shift is covered.
- Employee Bag and Pocket Checks: Night guards are responsible for checking employees’ bags and pockets as they leave the hospital.
- No Tobacco and Alcohol: Tobacco or kharra is strictly prohibited within hospital premises.
- Back Entry Gate: Keep the back entry gate open after 5 AM.
- Lift Management: Ensure that the lift is always available on the ground floor, and it should not be used for transporting staff from higher floors to the ground floor.
- Fire Pump Area Guarding: A guard must always be stationed near the fire pump area.
- Snap of Articles: Guards must take snapshots of all items being moved in and out and share them in the WhatsApp group, keeping a register of the same.

3\. Hospital Property and Personal Belongings Check:

- Bag Check Policy: All personal backpacks are prohibited from entering the hospital. A desk will be set up to check bags at the employee entrance. Daily checks will be conducted by security staff.
- Unauthorized Possession: Any unauthorized possession of hospital property such as medicines, IV bottles, or OT instruments will be dealt with according to the hospital’s policies.

* * *

General Guidelines for Both Hospitals:

4\. Front Office Operations and Reporting:

- Patient Admission and Discharge: Ensure smooth patient admission and discharge processes by maintaining a register for all admitted and discharged patients. Ensure all documents and records are updated.
- OPD and IPD Tracking: Track the number of patients in OPD and IPD, and ensure that all necessary information is shared with the billing department on time.
- Consultation Records: Maintain accurate records for OPD consultations, including the categorization of patients by tariff type (e.g., private, Yojna).
- Staff Coordination and Communication: Ensure that the front desk is always manned and that staff follow all communication protocols, including using WhatsApp for sharing updates.
- CCTV Surveillance: Conduct periodic checks of hospital areas (e.g., reception, corridors, and toilets) to ensure no lapses in security or cleanliness.

5\. Housekeeping and Cleanliness Protocols:

- Daily Bed Making and Linen Management: Housekeeping staff should ensure that all beds are made daily with fresh linen and report linen availability regularly.
- Facility Inspection: Ensure that all hospital areas (patient rooms, bathrooms, and corridors) are clean and well-maintained. A daily inspection must be carried out and documented.

6\. Staff Training and Performance Monitoring:

- Orientation: New staff should receive a comprehensive orientation on hospital procedures, including software usage, bed allotment, and billing management.
- Punctuality and Attendance: Staff attendance must be monitored rigorously, with consequences for tardiness or unapproved leave.
- Employee Conduct: Nurses and staff must adhere to professional conduct standards, including patient communication and hygiene protocols.

7\. Emergency and Critical Care Protocols:

- Emergency Response: Ensure that all staff members are trained to handle emergencies. A clear protocol should be followed for patient care during emergencies (e.g., surgeries, critical care).
- Equipment Availability: Ensure that all medical equipment, including ventilators and oxygen cylinders, are readily available and in working condition for emergency use.

8\. Staff Responsibilities for Reporting:

- Daily Reporting: Daily reports should be submitted by all in-charges (e.g., nurses, ward boys, security) regarding the status of equipment, patient care, and any issues that need attention.
- Feedback System: Collect daily feedback from patients regarding their care and ensure it is reported for quality improvement.

* * *

9\. Security Guards Responsibilities (New Protocol):

- Bag and Pocket Check for Employees: Security will enforce the policy of checking employees' bags and pockets when they leave the hospital premises.
- Snap Posting: Security must take photos of any equipment or items moved in or out of the hospital and share them in the designated WhatsApp group, with a proper register maintained.

* * *

## Housekeeping Staff Induction Training – Trainer Sakshi

## Hope & Ayushman Hospitals

1\. Introduction to Hospital & Team

- On Day 1, each new housekeeping staff member must be:


- Introduced personally to all key hospital staff, including front office executives, floor managers, nursing in-charges, resident doctors, and supervisors.

- Given a brief tour of the hospital – wards, ICU, OT, pantry, reception, nurse stations, utility areas, and waste collection points.

2\. Uniform, Discipline & Mobile Policy

- Staff must be in proper uniform with their ID card displayed at all times.

- Mobile phones are strictly prohibited during duty hours.


- All personal mobile phones must be deposited at the reception before reporting to duty.


- Housekeeping staff must remain awake and alert during night shifts. Sleeping on duty is strictly not permitted.


* * *

3\. Cleaning, Dusting & Ward Maintenance

- Training on:


- Most important task is to lock all patient rooms not in use…It has been noticed that the ward boys and other staff utilise the rooms not in use.
- Cleaning Protocols: Wet & dry mopping techniques, high-touch surface cleaning, OT aseptic cleaning (if applicable).

- Dusting: Beds, walls, rails, bedside tables, monitors, and high areas like tube lights and fans.

- Daily Checklist for ward cleanliness must be maintained.

- Special attention to be given to patient beds, corners, washrooms, and nurse stations.


* * *

4\. Biomedical Waste (BMW) Management

- Explain the coloured bag system for biomedical waste segregation:


- Yellow – Human anatomical waste, soiled waste.

- Red – Contaminated waste (tubing, IV sets).

- White (translucent) – Sharps (needles, blades).

- Blue – Glassware and broken ampoules.


- Emphasize no mixing of waste and proper disposal timings.

- Ensure gloves, mask, and apron are worn during waste handling.


* * *

5\. Food & Feeding Support

- Housekeeping staff must ensure:


- Patients receive meals on time as per schedule.

- NBM (Nil by Mouth) patients are not given food or water by mistake.

- For Ryle’s Tube (RT) / Ritu Feed patients:


- Staff should inform the nurse if food is pending or any issue is noticed.


- Understand and follow instructions such as “NBM”, “NPO”, or “RT Feed Ongoing”.


* * *

6\. Basic Bedside Patient Care Assistance

While clinical care is nurse-led, housekeeping must support in:

- Changing diapers (especially at night), with privacy and dignity.

- Positioning of bedridden patients every 2 hours to prevent bed sores.

- Back care – help with turning patients for cleaning or nursing purposes.

- Providing urinals and urine collection pods as needed.

- Assist in part preparation, cleaning the patient’s body area before procedures.


* * *

7\. Ward Inventory & Documentation Assistance

- Maintain cleanliness of patient charts, vitals boards, and care plans.

- Ensure bedside drawers, trays, and dustbins are clean and stocked.

- Alert nurse if supplies are running low or if linen needs change.


* * *

8\. Staff Communication Protocol

- All housekeeping staff should:


- Know the names and phone numbers of the following:


- Resident doctors (RMO) on each shift.

- Floor in-charge nurse.

- Reception & Emergency contact.

- Maintenance, security, and admin team.


- Be trained on whom to report to in case of:


- Patient complaint or fall.

- Emergency cleanup.

- Missing or uncollected waste.


* * *

9\. Emergency and Night Duties

- Staff must:


- Report any spills, blood, or vomit immediately to nurse and clean per SOP.

- Be alert for calls from nurse station or patient bell.

- Never leave the ward unattended without informing the shift supervisor.


* * *

10\. Review & Acknowledgment

- A daily checklist and logbook to be maintained by the supervisor for:


- Attendance.

- Cleaning quality.

- Food distribution.

- Feedback from nursing team.


- After induction, staff must sign a form confirming:


- Understanding of their responsibilities.

- Compliance with hospital policies.

- Acknowledgment of mobile, night duty, and waste handling rules.


* * *

### JD - Billing executive

Hope Group of Hospitals

Position: Billing Executive

Department: Financial & Billing Operations

Location: Hope Hospital, Nagpur

Reports To: Billing Manager / Finance Director

Job Responsibilities:

1. Patient Billing & Documentation:


- Generate and process invoices for OPD, IPD, and emergency services.

- Verify patient details and treatment records before billing.

- Ensure surgeon and physician visit charges are correctly included in the billing.

- Update billing activities daily in the hospital software.


2. Insurance and TPA Billing:


- Process claims for cashless insurance (Ayushman Yojana, CGHS, ECHS, corporate empanelment).

- Coordinate with TPA desk for approval and documentation.

- Follow up on outstanding payments from insurance and corporate partners.


3. Billing Accuracy & Compliance:


- Verify hospital tariff for procedures, consultations, and investigations.

- Address patient inquiries regarding billing discrepancies and payment plans.

- Ensure accurate billing of medical implants and high-value consumables.


4. Coordination with Departments:


- Work closely with reception, accounts, RMOs, and consultants to ensure seamless billing.

- Cross-check discharge summaries with final billing for accurate records.


5. Financial Transactions & Record-Keeping:


- Maintain logs for cash transactions, bank transfers, and online payment receipts.

- Handle patient deposits, refunds, and payment receipts with accuracy.

- Keep detailed records of OPD and IPD billing for internal audits.


6. Software & Technology Use:


- Utilize hospital management software for billing and reporting.

- Report any software issues to the IT team and assist in troubleshooting.

- Generate daily, weekly, and monthly billing reports.


7. Reporting & Compliance:


- Prepare daily reports on outstanding and pending patient bills.

- Send reminders for recovering outstanding payments.

- Ensure billing compliance with NABH and hospital policies.

- Attend training sessions for billing accuracy and fraud prevention.


Key Skills Required:

- Technical Knowledge: Experience with hospital billing software.

- Accuracy & Attention to Detail: Ensure zero billing errors.

- Communication Skills: Professional interaction with patients, doctors, and insurance providers.

- Time Management: Prioritize tasks to ensure timely bill processing.

- Problem-Solving: Address billing discrepancies and resolve patient concerns effectively.


Salary & Growth Opportunities:

- Salary as per hospital standards.

  .

- Opportunities for promotion in financial operations.

What is the goal setting of the BHAG?

A big hairy audacious goal is a compelling, long-term goal that is intriguing enough to inspire employees of an organization to take action. The term is abbreviated as BHAG, which is pronounced bee-hag. Goals are in cards kept in our wallet. We have it as screensavers and on all walls at home!

Here is the structured goal-setting for the leadership of the 100-bedded Hope Hospital, formatted for easy copying and pasting into a Google Doc without special characters:

\-\-\-

Goal Setting for Achieving 75% Occupancy at Hope Hospital

Objective:

Improve operational and clinical strategies to achieve a target occupancy rate of 75% in Hope Hospital.

1\. Specific

Goal: Improve patient acquisition strategies to increase admissions by enhancing the hospital's visibility and reputation within the community.

Action Steps:

\- Partner with local physicians and clinics to increase referrals.

\- Boost the hospital’s online presence through targeted digital marketing campaigns that highlight specialties and successful treatments.

\- Organize community health camps and seminars to raise awareness and engagement.

2\. Measurable

Goal: Develop a system to closely monitor patient admissions and occupancy rates on a monthly basis to achieve a 75% occupancy rate.

Action Steps:

\- Implement software tools for daily tracking of admissions and discharges.

\- Set progressive interim occupancy targets (e.g., 60% within 3 months, 70% within 6 months).

\- Perform monthly reviews of strategy effectiveness and make necessary adjustments based on data.

3\. Achievable

Goal: Enhance the overall quality of care to boost patient satisfaction and retention.

Action Steps:

\- Conduct ongoing customer service and patient care training for all staff.

\- Establish a robust patient feedback system to regularly collect and act on patient reviews.

\- Upgrade medical equipment and protocols to maintain a high standard of care.

4\. Relevant

Goal: Expand and improve service offerings in areas with high demand and growth potential.

Action Steps:

\- Carry out market research to pinpoint services with increasing demand.

\- Enhance capabilities in key departments such as geriatrics, pediatrics, or elective surgery.

\- Hire specialists and provide additional training to existing staff to support new services.

5\. Time-bound

Goal: Reach the goal of 75% occupancy within one year through strategic phases.

Action Steps:

\- Establish quarterly milestones for admissions and service improvements.

\- Regularly (monthly/quarterly) assess progress towards the annual target and refine strategies as necessary.

\- Recognize and celebrate achieved milestones to maintain staff motivation and commitment.

\-\-\-

By following these structured and strategic goals, Hope Hospital can effectively direct its efforts towards significant improvements in occupancy rates and overall service quality.

### 1.3 "Speak Up" Policy

1\. Purpose: To provide guidelines and procedures for employees to report concerns about unethical, illegal, or unsafe practices within the organisation. This policy aims to foster a safe environment for reporting without fear of retaliation.

2\. Scope: This SOP applies to all employees, contractors, vendors, and stakeholders associated with the organisation.

3\. Policy Statement: The organisation is committed to maintaining the highest standards of ethics, integrity, and transparency. The "Speak Up" policy ensures that all concerns related to misconduct are addressed promptly and adequately.

4\. Reporting Procedure:

4.1. Initial Reporting:

- Employees should report any concerns to their immediate supervisor.
- If the employee feels uncomfortable reporting to their supervisor, or if the concern involves their supervisor, they can escalate it to the HR department or designated ombudsman.

4.2. Anonymous Reporting:

- The organisation will provide an anonymous reporting mechanism (like a hotline or online portal) for those who wish to maintain their anonymity.

4.3. Documentation:

- All reports should be detailed, including names, dates, evidence (if available), and any other pertinent information.
- Even anonymous reporters are encouraged to provide as much detail as possible.

5\. Investigation:

5.1. Upon receiving a report, the concerned department will initiate an investigation.

5.2. All investigations will be conducted impartially, maintaining confidentiality as much as     possible.

5.3. The designated investigation team will comprise individuals not directly involved in the reported concern.

5.4. Appropriate action will be taken based on the results of the investigation, which could include disciplinary actions, training, policy modifications, etc.

6. Non-Retaliation:

6.1. Employees who report concerns in good faith will be protected from any form of retaliation or adverse employment actions.

6.2. Any employee found retaliating against a reporter will face strict disciplinary action.

7. Training and Awareness:

7.1. All employees will receive training on the "Speak Up" policy during their induction and periodically afterwards.

7.2. Posters, email communications, and workshops will be used to promote awareness of the policy throughout the organisation.

8. Record Keeping:

8.1. All reports and investigations will be documented and archived securely by the HR department for a defined period, as per legal requirements or company policy.

8.2. Periodic reviews will be conducted to assess the effectiveness of the policy and make necessary adjustments.

9\. Responsibilities:

9.1. Employees: To report concerns promptly and provide support during investigations when required.

9.2. Supervisors: To foster an environment where employees feel comfortable reporting concerns and to escalate reports as per the policy.

9.3. HR/Ombudsman: To ensure concerns are addressed appropriately, investigations are conducted impartially, and confidentiality is maintained.

10\. Review:

The "Speak Up" policy SOP will be reviewed annually or as needed to ensure it remains effective and relevant to the organisation's needs.

### 1.4 Speak up - Anonymous Reporting Form

[https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLScqryVJuDBH3FXrPQL9346ZN7ru2APIPRE4hogPh9qTIRAUmw/viewform](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLScqryVJuDBH3FXrPQL9346ZN7ru2APIPRE4hogPh9qTIRAUmw/viewform&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181453804&usg=AOvVaw05G-Wfh2ebkSJl4JstwqHV)

Anonymous Reporting Form

Purpose: This form is designed to allow our staff to report any concerns, issues, or suggestions related to our workplace. Your feedback is invaluable, and we encourage open communication to foster a positive work environment.

Instructions:

Completing the Form: Please fill in as much detail as possible. The more specific you are, the better we can understand and address the issue.

Anonymity:

This form is set up to collect responses without capturing personal data or email addresses.

However, please refrain from providing any personally identifiable information within the content of your report if you wish to remain anonymous.

Remember, Google might log IP addresses or other data, so while we won't know who submitted the form, absolute anonymity cannot be guaranteed if there were to be an external investigation into Google's data.

Response and Action:

All submissions will be reviewed by \[relevant department/team/person\].

While we may not be able to provide direct feedback on anonymous reports, please know that every report is taken seriously and will be acted upon as necessary.

No Retaliation: Our organisation is committed to ensuring a safe environment for all employees. Retaliation against anyone for submitting a report is strictly prohibited and will be treated as a serious violation of our policies.

Optional Contact Details: If you're comfortable and wish to be contacted for any clarifications or updates on your report, you may provide your contact details in the relevant section. However, this is entirely optional.

Use Judiciously: Please use this form responsibly and only for its intended purpose. Frivolous or false reporting can hamper our ability to address genuine concerns.

Alternative Reporting: If you're uncomfortable using this form or have concerns about anonymity, please consider reaching out to \[alternative reporting method, e.g., HR department, supervisor, or a dedicated helpline\].

Thank you for taking the time to provide feedback. Your voice matters, and we're committed to ensuring a safe, transparent, and positive work environment for everyone.

### 1.82 Appointment of a consultant

Introduction

This SOP outlines the responsibilities and duties of a consultant -  Dr. Suhas Tiple, who has been appointed as a clinician in the Hope and Ayushman group of hospitals.

Appointment Details

Position: Clinician

Appointee: Dr. Suhas Tiple

Working Hours: 9am to 11am and 3pm to 5pm

Duties and Responsibilities

Dr. Suhas Tiple will be in charge of the morning Outpatient Department (OPD) and Inpatient Department (IPD).

He will make rounds to ensure all patients are being adequately cared for and their medical needs are being met.

He will review all patient files to maintain an understanding of patient conditions and progress. He will be responsible for maintaining up-to-date records on all his patients.

As a clinician, he will provide consultations, make diagnoses, and manage the treatment of the patients under his care.

Specialization

Dr. Suhas Tiple will attend to all patients at Hope group of Hospitals requiring a chest physician's expertise or procedures.

Compensation

Dr. Suhas Tiple's monthly salary will be INR 1,00,000. This remuneration includes all procedures performed by him.

General Expectations

Dr. Suhas Tiple is expected to adhere to the ethical and professional standards set by the hospital and the medical profession.

He is expected to be punctual, respectful, and mindful of patient needs and concerns.

He is expected to participate in professional development and training including NABH as required by the hospital.

This SOP should be read and signed by Dr. Suhas Tiple to confirm his understanding and acceptance of the terms of his appointment. The SOP will be reviewed and updated periodically, or as necessary, to ensure it remains relevant and accurate.

### 1.83 consultant - Implant issues

I would like to discuss a recent event involving the treatment of a patient who hails from the Madhya Pradesh police department. This patient had sustained a shoulder injury and was operated on by Dr. D G, a proficient orthopedic surgeon at our institution. During the operation, an implant worth INR 80,000 was used as a part of the treatment procedure.

Given the financial considerations and the credit nature of our dealings, I had earlier communicated to Dr. D G about the constraints regarding the high-value implants. We often have to wait for nearly six months to receive payment for these costly implants, which leads to a significant amount of funds being locked away during this period. For this reason, I had suggested capping the value of implants at INR 15,000, particularly for patients treated on credit.

Moreover, another instance further complicates the matter. Shortly after the first episode, Dr. S, arthroscopic surgeon admitted a patient who is a beneficiary of the ESI scheme. He carried out an operation on this patient and used implants that were valued at a staggering INR 1,50,000. It must be mentioned that the financial clearance for such a high-cost implant can be challenging to obtain.

Taking into account these circumstances, we have decided to introduce a policy to maintain our financial health and to ensure sustainable treatment options for our patients. The new policy mandates that all surgeons who intend to operate in our facilities must sign a consent form. This consent form explicitly states that implants valued over INR 15,000 cannot be used for patients being treated on a cashless basis.

This measure aims to streamline the process and manage the financial aspects of patient care more efficiently, ensuring that we can continue to provide quality healthcare services to all our patients. Furthermore, it sets a clear expectation with our medical staff regarding the financial constraints of the hospital while catering to cashless patients, thereby preventing any potential miscommunication or misunderstanding in the future.

I believe this approach will allow us to better serve our patients, whilst ensuring the financial stability of our esteemed institutions, the Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital.

CONSENT FORM FOR CONSULTANTS REGARDING USE OF MEDICAL IMPLANTS

Dear Consultant,

This letter is to inform you of the financial policy of Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital concerning the use of high-value medical implants during surgeries. This policy is essential for the continued effective and efficient management of our financial resources, as well as to ensure the viability of our commitment to providing high-quality healthcare services to all our patients.

The key points of the policy are as follows:

All consultants who wish to operate in our facilities are required to adhere to this policy, without exceptions.

The use of medical implants in patients being treated on a cashless basis is subject to a value cap of INR 15,000.

Any deviation from this policy must be justified by the patient's medical need and must be pre-approved by the hospital's management.

By signing below, you, as a consultant at our hospitals, agree to abide by this policy and understand that failure to do so may result in disciplinary action as deemed necessary by the hospital management.

We greatly appreciate your understanding and cooperation in this matter.

Please sign and date below to indicate your agreement to the above terms.

Name of Consultant:

Signature:

Date:

Please return the signed form to the Hospital Management Office by \[insert date\]. Failure to do so may result in temporary suspension of surgical privileges until the form is received.

Thank you for your attention to this matter and for your ongoing commitment to providing the best possible care to our patients.

Sincerely,

Dr. Murali B K,

Chairman & Managing Director,

Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital.

OPD Summaries and Discharge Summaries:

- Consultants will prepare detailed OPD summaries and Discharge summaries themselves.
- They will collaborate with Resident Medical Officers (RMOs) and Front Office staff in the preparation.
- Complaints, events, examination findings, and medications will be included, adhering to specific guidelines.
- Patient confidentiality must be maintained; no mention of patient name, sex, or age.
- A separate diagnosis paragraph will be included, and medications and investigations will be provided in table format.
- Patients without specific comorbidities will be mentioned, and all patients will be called for review in 3 days.
- Insights into recent medical research, patient management techniques, and digital health trends may be included.

Ethical Guidelines:

- Consultants will not solicit patients.
- Written, surgery-specific consent must be obtained by them before surgery.

Daily Practices:

- Daily notes must be recorded.

# Suggested holidays for Mohan Nagar staff - Telecallers and Developers only:

Makar Sankranti (January) - A significant harvest festival celebrated with kite flying and traditional sweets.

Republic Day (January 26) - A national holiday celebrating the adoption of the Constitution of India.

Maha Shivratri (February/March) - A major Hindu festival dedicated to Lord Shiva, celebrated with fasting and night-long vigils.

Holi (March) - The festival of colors, marking the arrival of spring and celebrated with vibrant colors and festivities.

Gudi Padwa (March/April) - The Maharashtrian New Year, celebrated with traditional rituals and festivities.

Independence Day (August 15) - A national holiday commemorating India's independence from British rule.

Ganesh Chaturthi (August/September) - A major festival in Maharashtra, celebrating the birth of Lord Ganesha with grand processions and idol immersions.

Navratri / Dussehra (September/October) - A festival spanning nine nights celebrating the divine feminine, culminating in Dussehra, which marks the victory of good over evil.\

Diwali (October/November) - The festival of lights, one of the most significant festivals in Hinduism, celebrated with lighting lamps, bursting fireworks, and sharing sweets.

2\. Marketing and Front Office Operations - presidents report to Suraj

[Ernest Shackleton and the Endurance Expedition](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/14p7RGUggdEH7jjrISR9aLaI1KDE7xWodWrNfobJBIZc/edit?usp%3Dsharing&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181535386&usg=AOvVaw0obwp_IikgttMXhN457tDk) Story on leadership skills

Replying to messages from customers and patients on WhatsApp

5-point Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for replying to messages from customers and patients on WhatsApp for Ayushman, Hope, and Raftaar reception phones:

1\. Prompt Acknowledgment

- Response Time: Always reply within 5-10 minutes of receiving a message during working hours.
- Template: Start with a polite acknowledgment:

  "Thank you for contacting \[Ayushman/Hope/Raftaar\] Reception. How can we assist you today?"

2\. Listen and Clarify

- Understand the Query: Read the message carefully. If the query is unclear, ask for specific information.
- Template:

  "Could you please provide more details regarding \[your concern/appointment/treatment\] so we can assist you better?"

3\. Provide Accurate and Clear Information

- Direct Assistance: Offer clear, precise, and concise answers based on the query. Always ensure the information provided is accurate and up-to-date.
- Template:

  "Your appointment with Dr. \[Name\] is confirmed for \[Date\] at \[Time\]. Please arrive 15 minutes early."

  OR

  "The Ayushman Scheme covers \[specific services\]. For further details, you can visit our website or contact us directly."

4\. Escalate When Necessary

- Forwarding Complex Queries: If the query requires special attention, inform the customer and escalate the issue to the relevant department.
- Template:

  "I will connect you with our \[relevant department/medical team\] to provide more information on this. Kindly give us a moment."

5\. Closing the Conversation

- Polite Conclusion: Always end the conversation with a thank you and confirmation of next steps if required.
- Template:

  "Thank you for reaching out to \[Ayushman/Hope/Raftaar\]. We hope this helps! Let us know if you need any further assistance. Have a great day!"

### 2.00 Referral Payment Guidelines for Marketing Staff:

- When calculating the doctor referral fee to be passed to the doctor, the hospital deducts the surgeon's fees, anesthetist's fees, and lab and radiology charges etc. exactly as mentioned in the patient's bill. It has been observed that presently, only the actual charges paid by the hospital to the surgeon are being deducted, which is incorrect. 30% to 20% of the remaining amount after these deductions is passed on.
- Marketing staff are strictly prohibited from transferring any referral payments directly from hospital accounts into their personal accounts.
-  Instead, referral payments must be processed through the hospital’s standard payment procedures. Marketing staff are not authorised to make any payments to referees before receiving funds from the hospital.
- The Chief Managing Director (CMD) will review the patient’s bill and approve the referral payment, which will not exceed 20% of the total bill. All referral payments to referees must be transparent and compliant with hospital policy.
- All referees to be introduced to Dr Murali. No payments to be done to referees not introduced to CMD
- Resident Doctors have to identify direct patients and report to CMD. They will not call marketing staff when direct patients come to hospital!

![](<Base64-Image-Removed>)

![](<Base64-Image-Removed>)

At our institution, when admitting cashless patients, a standardized protocol is observed where surgeries are postponed for the initial two days of admission, except in emergency cases. Furthermore, patients are not discharged until two days after surgery. This comprehensive policy ensures ample time for administrative processes and postoperative care.

Admission and Surgery Delay:

- Repeated Reminders: From the date of admission, there will be systematic and repeated reminders regarding the two-day delay in surgery, allowing time to complete the paperwork.
- Cross Watermark on Admission Notes: A cross watermark will be displayed on the admission notes sheet printed as soon as the patient is registered. This watermark serves as a visual cue for the surgical delay.
- Automated Notifications: Messages will appear on all documents and reports printed from the software, effective for two days from the date of admission, emphasizing that the patient should not be posted for surgery.

  Sample Notification: "Attention: This patient is not scheduled for surgery until two days post-admission. All necessary paperwork must be completed during this period. Thank you for your cooperation."

Discharge Protocol:

- Two-Day Postoperative Stay: Patients will remain under observation for two days following surgery, enabling thorough monitoring and recovery.
- Watermark on Discharge Summary: The discharge summary page for corporate patients will contain a watermark that disappears only after the two-day postoperative period has elapsed and the discharge process is completed in the software.

  Sample Notification: "Notice: This patient is required to stay for observation for two days following surgery. Discharge should not be processed until the postoperative period has been satisfied."

The notices printed on reports or notes will clearly articulate the reasons for these delays, emphasizing that the patient is not fit for surgery during the two-day preoperative period and must remain in the hospital for two days post-surgery.

In essence, corporate patients will be scheduled for surgery only after two full days from the date of admission and will not be discharged until two days following surgery. This process is designed to ensure that all preoperative and postoperative procedures are meticulously followed, maintaining the integrity and quality of patient care within our facility.

### 2.42 Marketing: Referral process

To ensure a smooth referral process and avoid any disputes or confusion, it is crucial to establish a clear referral policy and follow the guidelines. Here are some recommendations for managing the referral register and marketing group:

- No blank spaces: Ensure that the referral register does not have any blank spaces where the referral information is recorded. Fill out the referral information immediately upon admission to maintain accurate and up-to-date records.
- Referral communication: Referrals should be communicated to the marketing group before a patient is admitted. This helps establish a clear understanding of who referred the patient and avoids any potential disputes over claims.
- Mandatory posting in marketing group: To further ensure transparency and avoid duplicate claims, it is mandatory to post the referral information in the marketing group after the patient's admission. This provides a clear record of the referral and helps in resolving any potential disputes.
- Documentation: Maintain a clear and organised record of all referrals, including the referrer's name, contact information, and the date of referral. This information should be easily accessible to relevant staff members.
- Dispute resolution: In case of multiple claims on the same patient, establish a dispute resolution process that involves reviewing the referral register and marketing group communications to determine the accurate referral source. Ensure that the process is fair and transparent.
- Regular audits: Conduct regular audits of the referral register and marketing group to identify and rectify any discrepancies or errors. This helps maintain the integrity of the referral process and ensures accurate record-keeping.
- Marketing staff should not collect money directly from patients.

Referral incentives are given only after the bill is properly made and approved by management.

Rules/SOP for billing Staff for timely bill file submission

- If a file is delayed beyond 1 week for submission of all documents and if all queries are not answered by 1 week then the concerned billing executive should immediately inform in the billing whatsapp group that it is delayed.
- A team of 3 in house Auditors - Rishab and  Priyanka will track all bills that have not been submitted on a daily basis and report  separately by direct message

There is a 1 month (from date of discharge) deadline before which we have to submit documents. We need to verify for any NMI or queries .

### 2.5Front office: Admission of Private Patients

OPD:

1. पेट दर्द क लिए कोनसे डॉक्टर देखते है ? पहले फिजिशियन देखते है, फिर कंसलटेंट \- Dr Nikhil Khobragade देखते है, और phir सीनियर कंसलटेंट फिजिशियन -Dr Rajkondawar dekte hai.  हड्डी की तकलीफ है, तोह फ़िज़ियोथेरेपिस्ट और ओनर्स भी देखते है.

2. हमारा काम कब तक होगा ?  सर २ बजे तक जाचोकी रिपोर्ट्स आएगी, ३ बजे तक MRI की रिपोर्ट्स आती है, और ४ बजे तक सीनियर कंसल्टंट फिजिशियन -Dr Rajkondawar  दिखाते है.

3. आयुष्मान कार्ड से फ्री में इलाज होता है क्या? OPD क लिए आयुष्मान कार्ड नहीं चलता है, अगर IPD में कोई बड़ा सर्जरी होता है तोह २०% का डिस्काउंट मिल सकता है.

4. जाचे  सब यही होती है ना ? पुरे सेंट्रल नागपुर में १ ही जगह पैर बड़ा मशीन है, वही हम आपको भेजते है I Investigation ka center नीचेमे ही है.

Identify the private patient: When a private patient arrives at the hospital, the receptionist should confirm their status as a private patient and offer them a room in the fourth floor, specifically rooms 201, 203, 206, or any other room designated for private patients.

Gather information: The receptionist should ask the private patient or their accompanying family member about their medical history, any current symptoms, and the reason for admission. This information, along with the referral letter sent by the corporate, will be used to write the admission note.

Contact the doctor: The receptionist should then contact the doctor in charge and inform them of the private patient's arrival. The doctor will assess the patient's condition and determine the urgency of the patient's treatment.

Write the admission note: The receptionist  should use the information gathered from the private patient, the referral letter, and the doctor's assessment to write an admission note. This note should include the patient's medical history, symptoms, diagnoses, surgeries, and any relevant complications indicated for urgent surgery.

The receptionist should then update the hospital's software to reflect the patient's admission, and provide the relevant information to be included in the admission note. The RMO will then write a comprehensive admission note, which should include the patient's diagnosis, surgeries, and any urgent surgeries indicated by the consultant or noted in the referral letter.

Urgent surgery: If the doctor determines that the private patient requires urgent surgery, it should be performed within 2 hours of their admission to the hospital.

Patient rounds and counselling: All building staff and admin staff should take rounds and conduct counselling sessions with the private patients in their room or chamber. This will ensure that the patients are comfortable and have all their questions answered.

Reporting: After each round, the staff should provide a report to the group to ensure that everyone is updated on the patients' conditions.

Update patient information: The receptionist should regularly update the patient's information in the hospital's system to ensure that all relevant medical information is accessible to the medical staff.

Note: This SOP should be followed strictly to ensure that private patients receive prompt and efficient medical attention. The hospital staff should prioritise the needs of private patients and ensure that their treatment is given the utmost urgency.

### 2.6 Front office: job description

### Essential Training Topics for all new appointees

1. Hospital Management Software Usage

- Bed allotment and registration processes (OPD/IPD).
- Managing billing activity sheets and generating bills.
- Updating patient admission and discharge information.

2. Customer Interaction and Communication

- Polite and professional interaction with patients and families.
- Effective handling of patient queries and concerns. Should be familiar with frequently performed surgeries, diagnosis, consultants and their qualifications and specialisation.
- Managing WhatsApp inquiries and providing timely responses.

3. Standard Operating Procedures (SOPs)

- Admission processes for private and cashless patients.
- Documentation and record-keeping protocols.
- Daily reporting of patient-related activities.

4. Operational Guidelines

- Room allocation and inspection procedures.
- Coordination with nurses and housekeeping for patient readiness.
- Maintaining cleanliness and functionality of reception areas.

5. Patient Feedback and Complaint Resolution

- Collecting and managing patient feedback (video/written).
- Addressing complaints effectively and escalating when necessary.

6. Billing and Financial Transactions

- Processing patient payments and issuing receipts.
- Ensuring compliance with hospital billing protocols.
- Avoiding errors in patient financial records.

7. Professional Conduct and Hospital Policies

- Understanding the hospital’s code of conduct.
- Training on the "Speak Up" policy for reporting unethical practices.
- Compliance with security checks and handling hospital property.

8. Emergency and Special Scenarios

- Handling patient emergencies and urgent surgeries.
- Coordination with doctors for critical patient needs.
- Familiarity with rental equipment processes like ventilators.

9. Technology and Equipment Handling

- Familiarity with reception software and basic troubleshooting.
- Ensuring functionality of communication devices and systems.

10. Feedback Analysis and Continuous Improvement

- Analyzing data from patient feedback forms.
- Implementing improvements in service quality based on feedback.

11. Teamwork and Collaboration

- Collaborating with nursing, administrative, and housekeeping teams.
- Participating in morning huddles and providing updates.

       12\. No late coming or absenteeism for 1 month. No offs allowed during the training period of 1 month. Have to inform the director to take off. Can not adjust off days according to own convenience.

The videos running at the reception should be monitored and the latest videos should be displayed in the TV at the reception.

Getting video feedback, Google reviews from all patients leaving the hospital is important so that they don't complain to the authorities or political leaders outside the hospital.

The most important issue is responding to patient calls regarding histopathology or any other reports. Every inquiry must receive a satisfactory answer. It is the lab technician's responsibility to promptly reply to all inquiries and provide an approximate date for the report. All inquiries and responses should be recorded in a register, ensuring that each query is addressed promptly and the response is documented in the register.

The lab technician is responsible for promptly responding to all inquiries and providing an approximate date for when the reports will be ready. All inquiries and responses must be recorded in a register. No patient should have to complain that, despite repeated inquiries, no satisfactory answer was given.

A register should be maintained at the reception, accessible to all receptionists, indicating the expected availability of pathology reports.

All WhatsApp messages must be replied to within 1 hour. The responsibility for responding to these messages lies with the OPD Supervisor, currently Kajal. All reception staff and Kajal are required to report to Gaurav.

Everyday discharge summary including bills will be given for approval and checking to Gaurav agrawal.

Every day, OPD and IPD patients should be segregated by departments according to the respective specialties. The report must include the number of patients for both OPD and IPD, categorised by each specialty. This daily report should be shared between 6 to 7 PM.

Every emergency patient should be informed about the Rafter Emergency Seva

Every patient feedback should be in a video or written format it is compulsorily to shared with Gaurav

Inbound call register should be maintained on reception.

[The most important issue is responding to patient calls regarding histopathology or any other reports](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1z6glo56aLPk9rNjc1wxBjblCmOkj-UCDIKBhGN7rxC0/edit?usp%3Dsharing&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181591548&usg=AOvVaw1DY7QAykXrVA65dvU6XS3f)

As a receptionist, some of the key duties include:

The proper allotment of clean and ready hospital beds is a critical aspect of hospital management and patient care, primarily falling under the purview of the reception staff. This process includes several steps to ensure maximum patient comfort and safety, along with efficient hospital operations.

Allocation Based on Gender and Need: Receptionists, while allotting beds, must be aware of the gender-based separation of wards. Male patients should not be admitted into female wards and vice versa. This step ensures patient privacy and comfort. Furthermore, bed allotment should also consider the specific needs of patients, such as need for ICU, post-operative care, isolation etc.

- Cleaning After Discharge: Once a patient is discharged, the room must be thoroughly cleaned by the housekeeping staff. This cleaning process includes disinfection of all touchpoints like bed rails, bedside tables, chairs, door handles, light switches, bathroom fixtures, and other patient equipment.
- Locking Vacant Rooms: After the room has been cleaned and is ready for the next patient, it must be locked. This prevents unauthorised entry and maintains the cleanliness and readiness of the room for the next occupant.
- Using Room Fresheners: To ensure a pleasant and welcoming environment, room fresheners should be sprayed in rooms after cleaning. However, the choice of fragrance should be mild and neutral to avoid causing discomfort to patients with allergies or sensitivities to strong scents.
- Room Inspection by Receptionist: Patients will have to wait in casualty till the room is ready both in day and night. Before allotting the room to the next patient, a final inspection should be carried out by the receptionist. They should confirm the room's cleanliness, the working condition of medical equipment, functioning of lights, fans, ACs, and other amenities, and the
- overall readiness of the room.A relative is first escorted to the room to verify if the room is to their liking before the patient is moved in.
- Bed Allotment: Once the room has been inspected and deemed ready, it can be allotted to new patients. The receptionist should update the hospital management system with the patient's details and the allotted bed.

Sending all discharge summary PDF's to the treating consultants before handing them over to patients.

Informing the respective consultant on admission, discharge or shifting to ICU, that their patient has been admitted in the hospital or shifted to ICU under their care.

Checking the working status of reception phones regularly to ensure smooth communication.

Maintaining records of inward and outward patients, appointments, and records for OPD, IPD, and Yellow Fever.

Directing patients to the CMD chamber for Yellow Fever vaccination.

Recording all calls made to the hospital in a register for future reference.

Keeping records of patients sent for CT, MRI, or other investigations and equipment taken out of the hospital for repairs.

Reserving three rooms with attached toilets for cash patients.

Providing a written handover to the next shift staff.

Organising food for all inpatients.

Checking the phone charges of landlines and ensuring they are paid on time. Payment can be made using gpay, through the link https://portal2.bsnl.in/myportal/cfa.do.

Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for Receptionist - Job Description

- Responsibilities and Duties:

2.1. Newspaper and Magazine Availability:

- Regularly check and ensure that newspapers and magazines are available in the reception area for OPD patients and visitors.
- Keep the reading material organised and replenish them as needed to provide an engaging and pleasant waiting experience.

2.2. TV Publicity Material:

- Ensure that the TV in the reception area displays the hospital's publicity material, relevant health information, and updates about hospital services and facilities.
- Monitor the TV regularly to verify that the content is up-to-date and visually appealing.

2.3. Token System for OPD:

- Operate the token system efficiently to manage the patient queue and avoid overcrowding.
- Issue tokens to patients for their appointments and direct them to the respective waiting areas or consultation rooms.

2.4. Wristband for Registered OPD Patients:

- Provide wristbands to all registered OPD patients for easy identification and tracking during their visit to the hospital.
- Instruct patients about the importance of wearing the wristband throughout their hospital stay.

2.5. Communication:

- Handle incoming phone calls and transfer them to the appropriate department or personnel.
- Take and relay messages accurately and promptly.
- Respond to general inquiries via phone or in-person courteously and professionally.

2.6. Patient Records Management:

- Maintain records of inward and outward patients, appointments, and other relevant details for both OPD and IPD.
- Ensure the confidentiality and security of patient information.

2.7. Yellow Fever Vaccination:

- Direct patients seeking Yellow Fever vaccination to the CMD chamber and provide them with any necessary information or instructions related to the vaccination process.

2.8. TV and Phone Management:

- Check the working status of reception phones regularly to ensure smooth communication and address any issues promptly.
- Monitor the TV to ensure that it runs the hospital's publicity material and other relevant content effectively.

2.9. Shift Handover:

- Provide a written handover to the next shift staff, including important updates, pending tasks, and any relevant information for seamless continuity of reception operations.

- Reporting and Compliance:

3.1. Report any technical issues related to the token system, TV display, or reception phones to the relevant department for prompt resolution.

3.2. Adhere to hospital policies and protocols related to patient interaction, confidentiality, and service quality.

- Training and Development:

4.1. Participate in training programs and workshops to enhance communication and customer service skills.

4.2. Stay updated with hospital services, facilities, and new promotional campaigns to provide accurate information to patients.

- Supervision:

The receptionist reports directly to M Com.

### 2.7 Handling Patients at the Reception Counter

* * *

When a patient arrives at the reception, it is our foremost duty to ensure their comfort and satisfaction. As the first line of contact, the following standards and procedures are to be observed:

- Room Preference:

- If the room is not to the patient's liking, immediately offer an alternative. If all rooms are occupied, the patient should be temporarily moved to a ward while their relative or companion waits in the reception area.

- Amenities:

- Ensure that each room is equipped with functioning electricity, including fans, air conditioning, lights, and switchboards.
- The room should undergo a thorough cleaning, with a focus on deep cleaning and sterilisation.
- Bathrooms should be in pristine condition. This includes operational taps, washbasins, showers, tiles, flooring, and especially corners. The toilet pot and seat, including the area behind it, must be cleaned daily to maintain hygiene. Ensure there are no leakages.
- Each bathroom should be fitted with an air freshener for a pleasant atmosphere.
- Check rooms thrice a day for any discarded alcohol bottles (Alcohol Sum
- Upon admission, the patient should be provided with fresh bed linen, sheets, pillow covers, a blanket, and a bottle of water.
- All rooms should exude a fresh and welcoming scent upon opening. The use of room fresheners is encouraged.
- Ensure bathroom and room doors are properly fitted with latches and handles.

- Communication:

- Once a room is prepared, promptly notify the front office and Sister Famida. The room should be locked, with the key kept securely.

- Maintenance:

- If there are any stains or damages in the room, contact the painter without delay.
- Always recheck the room's condition before assigning it to a patient. If any issues arise, change the room immediately to ensure the patient's comfort.

- Waiting Procedure:

- During the room verification process, patients and their relatives can relax in the reception area. If there's any delay or concern, kindly ask the patient’s relative to wait in the reception area, ensuring their comfort at all times.
- [Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for "Speak Up" Policy](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1kUvUp7ExQuzn3dSuIqZSJdoOIK8oxA4W-NtrzeBpyMc/edit?usp%3Dsharing&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181611587&usg=AOvVaw1y5wVsOLqg3Yqrcb6Q79Tc)
