- Group tab should not be used by any employee.
- Appropriate ledger heads for expenses are to be properly entered.[Click here for the list of expense head](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/19FIwhTHvV0DePXabkJs4HUhaQNoY0daKgi7PF683fyo/edit%23gid%3D341293105&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181614260&usg=AOvVaw07MiGh2Q6ysuKpk9CFozsp)s
- Expenses of the hospital should be approved immediately by bringing the payment voucher for approval. All vouchers have to be submitted at 5 PM.
- Receipts from OPD patients should not be in advance button. Proper bill is to be made for all patients.
- Choose ‘credit ’ as an option for giving a discount to patients to finalise the bill.
- The balance sheet is presently not viewable in our software. The developer is working on it.
- Manual JV has to be made for all corporate bills - credit and cash i,e,. Including CGHS serving patients.
- The "completed bills” register has to be updated daily. The register will be taken in accounts and the accountant will post all JVs for the day.

These expense heads are to be used for JV

- IPD Visit fees payment \- IPD Visit fees paid to consultants
- Opd consultation payment \- OPD consultation payments to consultants
- Surgeon charges payable \- Surgeons fees
- RMO consultation payable \- RMO payment

# 3\. Financial and Billing Operations - Shrikant

### 3.1 Billing:  Standard Operating Procedure for Documentation by Billing Staff

Purpose: The purpose of this Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) is to ensure that the billing staff follows a standardised process to verify the accuracy of patient information, diagnoses, and surgical procedures to prevent billing errors.

Scope: This SOP applies to all billing staff at Hope Hospital.

Procedure:

Patient Complaints: The billing staff must verify that the patient complaints mentioned in the referral letter and medical history match with the complaints recorded in the discharge summary.

Referral Letter: The billing staff must cross-check the referral letter and ensure that the diagnosis and surgical procedures mentioned in the letter match with the discharge summary.

Medical History: The billing staff must verify that the medical history recorded in the referral letter correlates with the diagnosis and surgical procedures mentioned in the discharge summary.

Diagnosis: The billing staff must ensure that the diagnosis mentioned in the referral letter and medical history matches with the diagnosis recorded in the discharge summary.

Surgical Procedures: The billing staff must ensure that the surgical procedures performed and recorded in the discharge summary match with the diagnosis mentioned in the referral letter and medical history.

Treating Surgeon: The billing staff must verify the accuracy of the above information with the treating surgeon and not the resident medical officer.

Communication with Consultant or Treating Specialist: The billing staff must communicate with the consultant or treating specialist if there are any discrepancies in the information mentioned in the referral letter, medical history, diagnosis, and surgical procedures recorded in the discharge summary.

CMD Review: The billing staff must bring the file for the CMD's review only after ensuring that all the information mentioned in the referral letter, medical history, diagnosis, and surgical procedures recorded in the discharge summary match and have been verified by the treating surgeon.

Conclusion: This SOP will ensure that the billing staff at Hope Hospital follows a standardised process to verify the accuracy of patient information, diagnoses, and surgical procedures, which will prevent billing errors and ensure patient satisfaction.

Subject: Instructions for TPA and Insurance Desk

In our ongoing effort to provide excellent service and ensure smooth processes in our hospital, I would like to bring to your attention the following instructions and updates.

Himanshu will be instrumental in providing training to Shreekant about the various nuances of general insurance. We expect this exercise to improve our general insurance processes considerably.

TPA Desk Knowledgeability: The TPA desk should possess comprehensive knowledge about insurance policies. This includes understanding room eligibility. In cases where room eligibility is lower, adjustments should be made in surgeon fees and RMO charges, as there is no cap on doctors' fees. This strategy should prevent an increase in the copay amount.

Cashless Patients Deposit: For patients using the cashless treatment option, a minimum deposit of Rs. 10,000 should be collected. Furthermore, patients should not be charged for TDS deductions.

Co-Pay Deductions: Please remember, co-pay amounts should be collected directly from patients.

Corporate and Institutional Camps: We are planning health camps in corporate offices, engineering colleges, MSEB, and MIDC. It is essential that we gather the database of these events for effective communication through Whatsapp blasts.

Documentation and Billing: Bills and other essential documents should be sent without delay. The dispatch of files through our runner boys should be immediate to avoid any delay in payment processing.

These instructions are intended to streamline our services and improve patient experience at our hospitals. Your strict adherence to these points is expected and appreciated.

### 3.3 Billing: Arthroscopy:

[https://docs.google.com/document/d/1AKKvWwCfUuiGgZO6V\_mX8JjxrOl\_wf7d7sjA5i1fxlQ/edit](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1AKKvWwCfUuiGgZO6V_mX8JjxrOl_wf7d7sjA5i1fxlQ/edit&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181632223&usg=AOvVaw0QINDAdv3OdWzY-30lMTE-) Thsi is the link for what implants to bill during arthroscopic surgeries

Regarding the billing for arthroscopic procedures.. We have to select the code which is 19000 which says “arthroscopy with implants” whenever an implant is used. If I ACL is done, do not use the code which says “ACL reconstruction” because that surgery is of lower value. That can be used as an additional code to the” Arthroscopy with implants” code. The implant that should be used when there is no radiologically visible implant is “fast fix” fast which is a suture material which is used for arthroscopic surgery and it can be billed up to 40000.

### 3.4 Billing:  Protocol for Inclusion of Surgeon and Physician Visit Charges in IPD Patient Bills

our policy regarding the billing for surgeon and physician visits during a patient's in-patient stay at our hospital.

As per our standard operating procedures, it is essential to charge for all visits by the treating surgeon or physician for the duration of the patient's stay in the hospital. These charges should be applied from the date of admission right up to the date of discharge.

Each of these interactions plays a significant role in the patient's recovery process and should thus be reflected accurately in the In-Patient Department (IPD) bill. This includes regular rounds, medical assessments, post-surgery check-ups, and other pertinent patient interactions.

Accurate and comprehensive billing helps to maintain transparency with our patients and their families regarding the cost of services provided. It also ensures that our medical professionals are adequately compensated for their dedicated service.

Please ensure that this protocol is followed without exception. It is our collective responsibility to ensure accurate billing practices, enhancing

Your vigilance in identifying and promptly reporting these issues contributes significantly to the overall functionality and efficiency of our operations. It ensures that we can provide the best possible service to our patients and maintain the high standard of care that is expected of us.

I trust in your diligence and appreciate your cooperation in adhering to these guidelines. By working together, we can ensure that our digital infrastructure supports our operations as efficiently as possible.

I recommend the following Standard Operating Procedures (SOPs) to the Billing Executive and Resident Doctors:

Patient File Format: Every patient file must contain the format provided, with the reference letter attached to the inside front cover of every file. This will ensure that the proper diagnosis and complaints are documented for each patient.

Correlation of Diagnosis: The diagnosis of the complaints in the referral letter should correlate with the diagnosis and the surgery performed on the patient. This will ensure that the documents we submit to corporators are accurate and complete.

Consultant Consultation: Before any patient is discharged, the consultant must be consulted to ensure that the discharge summary is correct. No discharge summary should go to the patient before the consultant has corrected it.

Treatment Plan: The consultant will be the only doctor who will write the treatment plan after discharge. This will ensure that the patient receives the proper treatment and follow-up care.

### 3.8 Billing/ Admin: Mandatory Updating of Patient Information across Departments and Final Payment Confirmation before Discharge

- Consultant Visits, Radiology, Blood Labs and Surgeries: It is mandatory that the billing for all patient services, including consultant visits, radiology procedures, laboratory tests, and surgeries, be updated in our system software daily. This will ensure that the records are comprehensive and reflect the accurate amount due from the patients.
- Patient Shifting: It is crucial that all patient shifting, whether within the hospital or upon discharge, be recorded promptly in the system. This helps to maintain the accurate tracking of patients within our facilities and aids in the correct billing.
- Shift Piece HO: All information regarding shift pieces and House Officers' duties must be promptly updated. This allows us to manage workload efficiently and ensures the appropriate assignment of responsibilities.
- Patient Discharge: The discharge of any patient from our hospitals should only be processed after the final payment is confirmed and appropriately recorded in our system. It is important that all outstanding charges are settled to ensure financial accuracy.
- Updating of Shifting Group or Outstanding Update: The discharge or shifting of any patient must be updated within the 'Shifting Group' or 'Outstanding Update' in our software system. This will ensure we maintain accurate and up-to-date records of all patient movements within and from our facilities.

These procedures are of the utmost importance in maintaining the high standards of service at both Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital. Ensuring that they are strictly followed will significantly contribute to the smooth functioning of our hospitals, the satisfaction of our patients, and the maintenance of our excellent reputation.

### 3.10 Billing: Improving Billing Accuracy & Training for Front Office Staff

it has become paramount to address an important issue concerning our billing accuracy. It has come to our attention that on 21st July 2023, an inconsistency was identified in the final bill of a patient who underwent surgery at our hospital. The procedure performed was not accurately documented, raising concerns about the comprehensiveness and precision of our billing process.

This occurrence underscores the necessity to enforce stringent quality control in our billing procedures, ensuring the comprehensive recording of all medical services delivered to our patients. Not only does this safeguard our credibility, but it also enhances patient trust and satisfaction, which are central to our hospital's ethos and mission.

In order to mitigate such incidents in the future, I am urging you to organise an immediate training session and a monthly session (First monday of every month)  for both the night and front office staff, including Pragati, Nisha, Rishab, and other members involved in the reception and front office area. This training should emphasise the critical importance of updating patient bills in our hospital software system every 6 hours, with diligent documentation of all services rendered.

Furthermore, an investigation into the underlying causes of this incident should be initiated. The findings from this inquiry will not only help to rectify the current oversight but will also be instrumental in strengthening our future training sessions. Understanding the root causes will allow us to constructively address these issues, enhancing the overall efficiency of our billing procedures.

Your leadership and collaborative efforts in this endeavour are crucial. ### 3.13  Billing : Anesthesiologist Fee Structure

At both Ayushman and Hope Hospitals, we adhere to the following payment scheme for anaesthesia services:

Short General Anesthesia (GA) - Rs. 1,500

Spinal Anesthesia - Rs. 2,500

General Anesthesia for private patients - Rs. 3,500

We would like to note that for empaneled patients seeking cashless treatment, the above charges are less by Rs. 500 per category. This means:

Short GA for empaneled patients - Rs. 1,000

Spinal Anesthesia for empaneled patients - Rs. 2,000

GA for empaneled patients - Rs. 3,000

Please note that these charges are constant, irrespective of the ASA grade or the complexity of the procedure.

### 3.14 Billing: RMOs , Doctors, Billing, Reception, Admin staff: Corporate

Topic: Instructions for Corporate patient’s protocol for: Admission , Discharge and use of Implants in the surgeries.

ADMISSION AND DISCHARGE PROTOCOL:

[MPKAY पुलिस दस्तावेजों की सूची](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1UijtwVskQDeMVnBRJOA7KVEq3eNtglKSwnSX-GsUDVM/edit&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181656929&usg=AOvVaw26uNwITZ0FC6t0O3H-7T4N)

CORPORATE PATIENT FROM CGHS, ECHS, NHA, SEC RAILWAY, CENTRAL RAILWAY, WCL, MPKAY, M.P. POLICE, ORDNANCE FACTORY AND ANY CORPORATE FOLLOWING CGHS TARIFFS.

Hard and soft copies of the documentation from Corporates towards the issue of  Referral , Approvals for permission of days extension, Implants, Unlisted procedures etc.  is very essential part of the treatment.

1. Admission are of two types :

1. Admission with proper referral ( Planned Admission ) : If patient comes with admission referral we have to take admission. We have to treat the patient for ailments for which the referral is issued. It is always mentioned on the referral the ailments/procedure for which the patient is referred.

If we start giving treatment to the patient for ailments for which he/she has not been referred.  Then the corporate organization will reject hospital  bill claim.Its is the loss for hospital.

Quation: What to do when patient are complaints about some other problem (ailments) apart from the ailments mentioned on the referral letter?

Answer: In such cases, before starting the treatment immediately call on the Billing Executive concern and narrate him the exact issue. He will immediately contact the referring authority of the concern corporate and address the issue. If corporate permits the new course of treatment then they will issue fresh referral with direction to submit proper justification from treating doctor with investigations if any required by them.  In case corporate authority rejects the permission for treatment other than referred ailments then hospital administration will counsel the patient and its relatives and clearly briefed them about the view of the corporate and asks to go for the treatment for which he/she is referred.

Note :

1. Apex A for echs - For any unlisted procedure (Surgery) /Implant/ ailments ( Non Referred ailment) hospital has to take proper permission with due submission of Case Summary/Quotation and  Clinical Justification to Corporate authorities when patient is admitted in the hospital and before the surgical treatment.
2. CGHS Ceiling for Implants is of Rs. 65000/- for TKR and other procedures.
3. In case of use of unlisted Implant above the Ceiling prices, the proper permission in advance with due submission of Quotation, justification from the operating Surgeon needs to be taken.  Final decision is of corporate authority whether to give or not to give permission.
4. It is always advisable to use the implant within price band (Ceiling rates) of the CGHS.

2.  Emergency admission ( Unplanned Admission):

If patient comes in emergency without admission referral.  We have to take admission.

Upon admission immediately inform Billing Executive. Collect Beneficiaries Card, Adhar Card and any old files and documents. Billing Executive will immediately in coordination with treating doctor will prepare Case summary, Quotation and Fill concern forms to seek referral. After the receipt of the referral the rest of the admission protocol  will be same as point (a).

We cannot deny the emergency admission. We have to treat the patient for ailments for which he came.  In case the facility not available with the hospital, we have to provide proper treatment to stabilize the patient and then only with the help of Corporate authorities directives the said patient can be shifted to another health care facility.

Note :  It is always mentioned on the referral the ailments/procedure for which the patient is referred. Please give treatment for the same.

Question : - How long the hospital can keep the patient ? Whether permission is required for hospital stay more than initial approved stay.

Answer : -  Generally the Seven days initial permission for hospital stay is given with referral. In echs the initial approval is of 12 days. On 10th day ask for extension if required.  If the treatment period extend then hospital administration has to take further days stay permission at least 48 hrs before the initial stay limit expires.  For extended stay  permission the concern papers to be submitted to Corporate on 5th day of patients stay in the hospital.  For Extended days stay justification from treating doctor is needed.  If we take official permission from the corporate then hospital can go ahead with treatment part of the patient and hospital will be secured for getting patients treatment bill sanctioned and get paid. There are different hospital stay slabs of Corporate. Hence it is always advisable for RMOS and Billing Executives to be in contact with each other.

New rules 25th April 2024 for ECHS patients onwards

What is Apex A,B and C?

Upto 2000 Rs medicines can be given on discharge!

5400 is the present ICU charges/day

Day care, within 6 hours - 500 rs will be paid to the hospital as room rent.

Stent

Angioplasty-  maximum payable amount - 1st 2 stents  -23,625/stent, 3rd will cost - 12000 rs

All implants, costly drugs - carton - MICr code, batch number

Chemotherapy drugs are excluded from package

10 percent discount on MRP on chemotherapy drugs

Can't charge more than 2 consultation or visits in a day

Discharge protocol of the patient from the Corporates.

Question : - Can we discharge the patient abruptly or without consulting the Billing Executive?

Answer : -  No! We cannot discharge the patients from Corporates immediately unless it is emergency. If we do discharge the patient abruptly then hospital billing will get hampered badly and there are chances that many expenses of the hospital will be not paid.

For all surgeries and procedures there are packages offered by the Corporates ( CGHS Tariffs).

Question: - What is meant by Package and are the Packages having hospital days capping?

Answer: - Package is having Package value.  According to Package value each Package value is having the fixed hospital days stay limit.

As per the CGHS,ECHS, MPKAY, WCL, SECR guidelines the Packages are derived as below:

1. Package Value above Rs. 5000/- and upto Rs. 10,000/- 03 Days Package (hospital days stay is allowed)
2. Package Value above Rs. 10,000/- and up to Rs. 25,000/- 05 Days Package (hospital days stay is allowed)
3. Package Value above Rs. 25,000/- 07 Days Package (hospital days stay is allowed)
4. Package Value below  Rs. 5000/- 01 Days Package (hospital days stay is allowed)

Surgical/ Procedures Package includes following :

1. Hospital Stay (Ward/ Pvt Room/ICU, and Ventilator, Monitor, O2…etc) within package days .
2. Consultant, Doctors, RMOs  and Nursing Charges
3. Pathology investigations within package days
4. Pharmacy medicines issued within package days
5. Radiology tests carried out within package days
6. CT/MRI and any investigations and Test carried out within package days
7. ECG and any other expenses incurred towards the treatment during this package  period.

Note: -

1. Before the start of Surgical package it is advisable to carry out investigations / Tests required and issue medications in anticipation of the treatment by the treating doctor. Prevent doing costly investigation / tests and issue expensive medication during package days. Do required and mandatory Tests/ Investigations during these package days.  Try to do it after the completion of Package period.
2. For surgical package patients : Do not do surgery immediately , it can be done after few days of admission with the due discussion with Billing Executives.  Because in these buffer days  before surgical package starts, you can do required Tests/Investigation and issue medications required in anticipation of treatment of the patient.

Do not discharge the patient before the end of its surgical package. It is highly  advisable to discharge the patient few days after the end of Surgical package. On discharge medicines and many investigations may get deducted if we discharge the patient before  the surgical package ends.  It is recommended to get in touch with Billing Executives concern before the plan of Surgical Package patients. Because in many Corporates specially Insurance/ TPA patients, Final approval on final bill need to be taken before patients discharge. Hence please plan discharge with due discussion with Billing Executives.

### 3.15 Accounts : Job Description for Cashier

To ensure that your organization stays on top of notices from Income Tax, TDS, and GST portals, it is crucial to implement a systematic approach. Here are some detailed tips and tricks to help you stay aware and respond promptly to any new notices:

1\. Centralize Communication:

- Dedicated Email ID: Use a dedicated email ID (e.g., CMD@HopeHospital.com) for all communications from the Income Tax, TDS, and GST portals. Ensure this email ID is not changed or reset without proper authorization.
- Passwords and userIDs of the income tax, tds and gst portals will not be changed by CAs and accountants. It will be changed by Dr Murali only.
- Multiple Access Points: Ensure that at least two trusted individuals (like the Head Accountant - Priyanka and Head Accountant - Satish) have access to this email to avoid disruptions due to unforeseen circumstances.

2\. Daily Portal Checks:

- Assign Responsibility: Designate a specific accountant, presently Priyanka to check the Income Tax, TDS, and GST portals daily. This person should have a checklist to ensure all relevant sections of the portals are reviewed.
- Backup Personnel: Have a backup person, presently Gaurav in place who can take over the responsibility if the primary accountant is unavailable.

3\. Notification Alerts:

- Email Forwarding: Set up email forwarding rules so that notices received on CMD@HopeHospital.com are also forwarded to the accountant (finance@hopehospital.com) and another responsible person (like the finance manager) for redundancy.
- SMS Alerts: Where possible, register for SMS alerts on the portals to receive notifications about new notices or updates.

4\. Logging and Tracking:

- Notice Register: Maintain a notice register (digital or physical) where each notice is logged with the date of receipt, reference number, type of notice, and due date for action.[shrikanth@thehopehospital.com](mailto:shrikanth@thehopehospital.com)
- Action Tracker: Alongside the notice register, maintain an action tracker that records the steps taken to address each notice, deadlines, and current status.

5\. Document Management:

- Cloud Storage: Use a secure cloud storage solution - google drive folder, to save copies of all notices. Organize them by financial year, type of notice, and status (e.g., pending, resolved).
- Access Control: Limit access to these documents to authorized personnel only, ensuring confidentiality and integrity.

6\. Regular Updates and Reviews:

- Weekly Meetings: Hold a weekly meeting, Monday at 12 noon  with the accounting and finance team to review all notices received during the week and the actions taken.
- Compliance Calendar: Maintain a compliance calendar that includes all key dates related to tax filings, payment deadlines, and notice responses. Ensure reminders are set up well in advance. [shrikanth@thehopehospital.com](mailto:shrikanth@thehopehospital.com)

7\. Training and Awareness:

- Regular Training: Conduct regular training sessions for the accounting team on how to handle different types of notices and updates from the Income Tax, TDS, and GST portals.
- Policy Manual: Develop a policy manual detailing the steps to be taken upon receiving a notice, including escalation procedures for urgent or complex matters.

8\. Audit and Review:

- Internal Audit: Schedule periodic monthly internal audits to ensure that the process of handling notices is being followed correctly and efficiently.
- Compliance Review: Conduct a quarterly compliance review to ensure that all pending notices have been addressed and there are no outstanding issues.

9\. Professional Support:

- Consultants and Advisors: Maintain a list of tax consultants and legal advisors who can be contacted for advice on complex notices or compliance issues.The list should include Milind Bhusari, Dani Hiranwar , Shanu Agarwal, Pramod Nikalje, Harish Dudeja, Vishal Ratnani, Nikhil Rathi,  Yash.

\*Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for Drug Procurement and Price Adjustment\*

Hope Pharmacy

\-\-\-

\*Objective:\*

To ensure the procurement of high-quality drugs at the most economical price for Hope Pharmacy, maintaining affordability for our patients while ensuring the pharmacy's sustainability. This SOP outlines the steps to be taken when a frequently sold drug undergoes a sudden price hike.

\*Scope:\*

This procedure applies to all pharmacy staff involved in the procurement, stocking, and sale of drugs at Hope Pharmacy.

\*Procedure:\*

1.⁠ ⁠\*Monitoring and Identification:\*

\- Pharmacy staff must regularly monitor the sales trends and prices of frequently sold drugs.

\- Any sudden price hike in these drugs must be reported to the Pharmacy Manager immediately.

2.⁠ ⁠\*Quotation Collection:\*

\- The Procurement Officer is tasked with collecting at least 3-4 quotations from different vendors for the drug in question.

\- The request for quotation must specify the need for identical quality and composition.

3.⁠ ⁠\*Vendor Evaluation:\*

\- Evaluate the quotations based on price, quality assurance, delivery timeline, and vendor reliability.

\- Preference should be given to vendors who have previously supplied high-quality drugs consistently.

4.⁠ ⁠\*Selection of Vendor:\*

\- Select the vendor offering the lowest price for the same quality and proportion as other vendors.

\- The Pharmacy Manager ( will take this decision ) must approve the selected vendor based on the evaluation.

    \- The final document must be reviewed and approved by the Pharmacy Manager and Financial Officer.

\*Responsibility:\*

•⁠  ⁠Pharmacy Staff: Monitoring drug sales and prices.

•⁠  ⁠Procurement Officer: Collecting quotations and vendor communication.

•⁠  ⁠Pharmacy Manager: Overseeing the procedure, vendor selection, and price adjustment.

•⁠  ⁠Financial Officer: Financial assessment and approval of price adjustment.

\*Review:\*

This SOP should be reviewed 3 month quotation or sooner if significant changes occur in the market or procurement process.

\-\-\-

This SOP is intended to maintain the balance between patient affordability and pharmacy sustainability, ensuring that Hope Pharmacy continues to serve the community effectively.

Cash Situation Handover: The Cashier is responsible for providing a comprehensive handover of the cash situation at the end of each day. For Hope Hospital, the handover is required by 5 PM each day. For Ayushman Hospital, the handover should be completed by 12 noon.

- Payment Vouchers Approval: All payment vouchers must be approved by the designated time each day. For Hope Hospital, approval must be done by 5 PM, and for Ayushman Hospital, by 12 noon. The Cashier is expected to review all vouchers for accuracy and compliance with company policies before giving their approval.
- Daily Cash Balance Reporting: The Cashier must report the cash balance to Dr. Murali B K each day by 5 PM for both hospitals. This report should detail all cash inflows and outflows for the day and should clearly indicate the closing cash balance.
- Outstanding Payables Discussion: At 3 PM each day, the Cashier at Hope Hospital is expected to meet with Gaauravto discuss the list of outstanding payables to vendors and consultants. Similarly, the Cashier at Ayushman Hospital should meet with Dr. Murali B K at 10 AM for the same purpose.
- Maintaining the Outstanding Payables List: The Cashier is responsible for maintaining and updating a list of all outstanding payables to vendors and consultants. This list should include details such as the amount payable, due date, and any other relevant information.
- Vendor and Consultant Payments: After discussing the outstanding payables with the relevant authorities, the Cashier is expected to process payments to vendors and consultants as per the agreed schedule and policies of the hospitals.

In carrying out these responsibilities, the Cashier must adhere to all internal financial controls, standard operating procedures, and policies of Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital. Confidentiality of financial information is paramount, and the Cashier is expected to act with utmost professionalism and integrity.

### 3.151 Directive for Storing Bank Details, PAN, and Cancelled Cheque Images on Padlet

To streamline our financial operations and ensure accuracy during the empanelment processes, I am directing a new protocol for the storage and utilization of our bank details, PAN associated with each account, and cancelled cheque images.

Effective immediately, all such information must be stored on Padlet and this will be our central repository for accessing these details. It is crucial that we no longer use or refer to the information stored in our Drive for these purposes. Using Padlet will help us maintain a better organized and more secure system, minimizing any potential errors during transactions or empanelment procedures.

Please follow the steps below:

1. Upload the bank details, including account numbers and bank names.
2. Attach the PAN associated with each bank account.
3. Include images of cancelled cheques for each account.

Ensure that each entry is clearly labeled and easy to access. It is imperative that everyone uses only the information from Padlet for all related tasks to avoid any discrepancies or errors.

This protocol is intended to safeguard our financial data and improve our operational efficiency. Compliance with this directive is mandatory for all staff involved in processing financial information and empanelment documentation.

### 3.17 Accounts: SOP for Surgeon Fees Payment and Accounting

### Implementation of a New Recording System for Surgical Services and Consultations

In our continuous effort to enhance our operational efficiency and financial tracking, I am initiating the implementation of a new record-keeping system. Please create and maintain a Google Sheet that records all services provided and surgeries performed by each consultant. The following columns should be included in the sheet:

Date: The date on which the service or surgery was performed.

Pt Name: The patient's name.

Surgery Name/Service Provided: The specific surgery or service that was performed.

Amount before TDS deduction: The total amount billed before any TDS deduction.

TDS AMT: The TDS amount deducted from the total bill.

Amount payable after deducting TDS: The net amount payable after TDS deduction.

PAID: Indicate whether the amount has been paid (Yes/No).

Date amount paid: The date on which the amount was paid.

BALANCE AMT: Any outstanding amount that remains unpaid.

Tariff: Specify whether the patient is categorized under Private, Yojna, or CGHS tariff.

Mode of payment: The method of payment used (e.g., cash, credit card, UPI).

This sheet will serve as a comprehensive record of all financial transactions related to surgical services and consultations provided by our hospital. It will aid in financial tracking, ensure compliance, and enhance transparency in our billing processes.

Please ensure this Google Sheet is updated promptly and accurately, and report to me with a weekly summary every Monday.

* * *

Objective: To ensure prompt and accurate payment of surgeon fees post-surgery and correct recording of the transactions in the accounting software.

Scope: This SOP is applicable to the Finance and Accounts Department responsible for processing payments and accounting for transactions related to surgeon fees.

Procedure:

1\. Pre-authorization of Yojna Patients:

1.1. Once a Yojna patient is scheduled for surgery, proceed with pre-authorization of the patient's medical coverage.

1.2. As part of the pre-authorization process, calculate the surgeon's fees, which are set at 30% of the total surgery cost.

1.3. Deduct 10% TDS (Tax Deducted at Source) from the calculated surgeon's fee.

2\. Journal Entry in Accounting Software:

2.1. After the TDS has been deducted, make a journal entry of the surgeon's fee in the accounting software.

2.2. Ensure all details are accurately recorded including date, amount, patient name, and other relevant details.

2.3. Review and verify the journal entry for accuracy.

3\. Crediting the Surgeon:

3.1. On the day prior to the surgery, credit the calculated fee (after TDS deduction) to the surgeon's account in the accounting system.

3.2. Ensure the credited amount matches with the figures recorded in the journal entry.

4\. Payment to the Surgeon:

4.1. Once the surgery is completed, process the payment to the surgeon as per the credited amount in the system.

4.2. Confirm the payment transaction and update the accounting software accordingly.

5\. Record Keeping and Audit:

5.1. Maintain proper records of all transactions, pre-authorizations, TDS calculations, and payments for future reference and audits.

5.2. Regularly review and audit the process to ensure compliance with the SOP and identify any areas for improvement.

Policy Review: This SOP should be reviewed annually or whenever significant changes occur in the payment or accounting processes.

Admin: SOP for IPD Dashboard - Initial Assessment Tab Usage

Objective: To standardise the use of the IPD Dashboard's Initial Assessment tab for entering instructions, tracking counselling status, and managing payments and agreed terms with patients.

Scope: This SOP is applicable to designated staff at Hope and Ayushman Hospitals who are responsible for managing the IPD Dashboard. Currently, Abhishek at Hope Hospital and Rishabh at Ayushman Hospital are the responsible individuals.

Procedure:

1\. Accessing IPD Dashboard:

1.1. Log into the IPD Dashboard with your authorised credentials.

1.2. Navigate to the "Initial Assessment" tab.

2\. Entering Instructions:

2.1. In the initial assessment tab, enter all necessary instructions related to the patient's case. Be detailed and clear to ensure proper communication of instructions.

3\. Counselling Status:

3.1. Use the green and red buttons to mark the status of patient counselling.

3.2. If counselling is successfully completed, click the green button. If counselling is not done or has been postponed, click the red button.

4\. Payment Information:

4.1. Clearly mention the amount to be paid to the surgeon and the amount to be passed on. Ensure accuracy to avoid any financial discrepancies.

5\. Patient Agreement Recording:

5.1. Clearly type what has been agreed with the patient and their family in the "Family Personal Note" text box.

5.2. Ensure the details entered are comprehensive and accurately reflect the agreement reached.

6\. Finalising and Saving Information:

6.1. Once all necessary information is entered and checked for accuracy, save the details in the system.

6.2. Ensure all changes are saved successfully before logging out or moving on to the next task.

Policy Review: This SOP should be reviewed annually or whenever significant changes occur in the IPD Dashboard usage or operational procedures.

This SOP aims to ensure standardised usage of the IPD dashboard, accurate information tracking, and smooth operations in both hospitals.

### 3.18 Accounts: SOP for Daily Update and Approval of Payables

Objective: To ensure that all payable amounts to referees, consultants, salaries, rent, vendors, etc., are updated, approved and managed in a timely manner. This is essential for maintaining positive relationships with all stakeholders and ensuring smooth operations.

Scope: This SOP applies to the Accounts In-Charge at both Hope and Ayushman Hospitals, who are responsible for updating, verifying and getting approval for all payables before 11 AM every day.

Procedure:

1\. Updating the Excel Sheet:

1.1. Access the designated Excel sheet for recording all payable amounts.

1.2. Update the Excel sheet with the payable amounts to referees, consultants, employees (salary), landlords (rent), and vendors. Make sure all data is correct and up-to-date.

2\. Verification:

2.1. Cross-check all entries to ensure their accuracy.

2.2. Rectify any errors found during the verification process.

3\. Seeking Approval:

3.1. Once the Excel sheet has been updated and verified, seek approval from the designated authority.

3.2. Ensure the approval process is completed before 11 AM each day.

4\. Failure to Comply:

4.1. Understand that this process is a primary duty for accountants and accounts in-charge.

4.2. Be aware that failure to comply with the stated timeline (11 AM deadline) will result in penalties as per the organisation's policy.

Policy Review: This SOP should be reviewed annually or whenever significant changes occur in the operations or payable management process.

This SOP aims to ensure regular updating and approval of all payable amounts to maintain strong relationships with consultants, referees, and other stakeholders, and to ensure the smooth operation of both hospitals.

\- Check for \*inconsistencies in GST rates\* applied on invoices versus official tax rates.

\- Ensure \*accuracy in debits and credits\*, referencing invoices and receipts.

\- \*Consolidate ledger accounts\* for the period.

\- Review and adjust ledger groupings for \*accurate financial reporting\*.

### Proper cash handling and accountability:

To all cashiers,

Effective immediately, please adhere to the following instructions to ensure proper cash handling and accountability:

1. Maintain a Physical Cash Book:

- Each cashier must maintain a physical cash book.
- Record every transaction accurately and promptly.
- The night duty cashier must hand over the cash book and cash to the day duty cashier at the end of each shift.
- Ensure the amount and time of handover are clearly documented.

2. Individual User Accounts:

- Each cashier must use their individual username when entering data in the software.
- A separate user account has been created for Priyanka.
- Under no circumstances should common usernames be used.

3. Accountability and Error Tracking:

- Using individual usernames will help in tracking entries and identifying errors accurately.
- Any discrepancies or errors can then be attributed to the responsible person, ensuring accountability.

Please comply with these instructions strictly to improve transparency and efficiency in our cash handling processes.

# 4\. Human Resources and Staff Management - Gaurav

### 4.1 HR: Departures from our official WhatsApp group, resignation

SOP for Resignation and Termination of Hope Hospital Staff

When a staff member wishes to resign from his position as an employee of Hope Hospital, a written letter has to be given with one month's notice to Hope Hospital.

The resignation will only be accepted if the concerned staff has given a proper handover and training to the individual who will take over his duties.

If the employee decides to leave the job without intimation he or she will forfeit the month's salary and any pending salary.

Any grievances may be discussed with either Ruby or Murali

GaauravBhalearao

Administrator

Hope Hospital

15.08.2017

As the owner of this hospital, I am aware of the recent departures from our official WhatsApp group and some staff members who have resigned and some have not joined back from their leave. I understand that some of our staff members may be feeling upset about compensation and concerns about raises for some staff members.

I want to remind all staff members that the hospital's WhatsApp group is an official communication platform and leaving it without proper authorization can result in disciplinary action. Additionally, resigning from the hospital without proper notice and not returning from leave without proper communication will also be considered as unprofessional conduct.

I would like to assure everyone that we take all concerns about compensation and raises seriously and are actively working to address them. However, leaving the group without proper authorization, resigning without proper notice, and not returning from leave without proper communication is not an appropriate way to address these issues.

I would also like to remind all staff members that they have the opportunity to discuss their concerns with their supervisors or HR department headed by Gaauravand handled by Tejaswini and Gaurav. We encourage them to do so.

I want to stress that the hospital values all of its staff members and that we are committed to creating a positive and fair work environment for everyone.

I would like to remind all staff members that they are a valuable part of our team and that we appreciate the hard work and dedication they put in to provide the best care for our patients.

We would like to work together to find a solution for any concerns and we would like to remind everyone that any kind of unprofessional conduct will not be tolerated.

Please let me or the HR department know if you have any concerns or issues that need to be addressed, and we will work together to find a solution.

Hope Hospital.: इस अस्पताल के मालिक के रूप में, मुझे हमारे आधिकारिक व्हाट्सएप ग्रुप से हाल ही में प्रस्थान और कुछ स्टाफ सदस्यों के बारे में पता है जिन्होंने इस्तीफा दे दिया है और कुछ अपनी छुट्टी से वापस नहीं आए हैं। मैं समझता हूं कि हमारे स्टाफ के कुछ सदस्य मुआवज़े को लेकर परेशान हो सकते हैं और कुछ स्टाफ सदस्यों की वेतन वृद्धि को लेकर चिंताएँ महसूस कर रहे होंगे।

मैं सभी स्टाफ सदस्यों को याद दिलाना चाहता हूं कि अस्पताल का व्हाट्सएप ग्रुप एक आधिकारिक संचार मंच है और उचित प्राधिकरण के बिना इसे छोड़ने पर अनुशासनात्मक कार्रवाई हो सकती है। इसके अतिरिक्त, उचित नोटिस के बिना अस्पताल से इस्तीफा देना और उचित संचार के बिना छुट्टी से वापस नहीं आना भी अव्यवसायिक आचरण माना जाएगा।

मैं सभी को आश्वस्त करना चाहता हूं कि हम मुआवजे के बारे में सभी चिंताओं को गंभीरता से लेते हैं और उन्हें संबोधित करने के लिए सक्रिय रूप से काम कर रहे हैं। हालांकि, उचित प्राधिकरण के बिना समूह छोड़ना, उचित नोटिस के बिना इस्तीफा देना, और उचित संचार के बिना छुट्टी से वापस नहीं आना इन मुद्दों को हल करने का एक उपयुक्त तरीका नहीं है।

मैं सभी स्टाफ सदस्यों को यह भी याद दिलाना चाहूंगा कि उनके पास अपने पर्यवेक्षकों या श्रीकांत की अध्यक्षता वाले एचआर विभाग और तेजस्विनी और अनिकेत द्वारा संचालित मानव संसाधन विभाग के साथ अपनी चिंताओं पर चर्चा करने का अवसर है। हम उन्हें ऐसा करने के लिए प्रोत्साहित करते हैं।

मैं इस बात पर जोर देना चाहता हूं कि अस्पताल अपने सभी स्टाफ सदस्यों को महत्व देता है और हम सभी के लिए एक सकारात्मक और निष्पक्ष कार्य वातावरण बनाने के लिए प्रतिबद्ध हैं।

मैं सभी स्टाफ सदस्यों को याद दिलाना चाहता हूं कि वे हमारी टीम का एक मूल्यवान हिस्सा हैं और हम अपने रोगियों की सर्वोत्तम देखभाल प्रदान करने के लिए उनके द्वारा की गई कड़ी मेहनत और समर्पण की सराहना करते हैं।

हम किसी भी चिंता का समाधान खोजने के लिए मिलकर काम करना चाहेंगे और हम सभी को याद दिलाना चाहेंगे कि किसी भी तरह का अव्यवसायिक आचरण बर्दाश्त नहीं किया जाएगा।

कृपया मुझे या मानव संसाधन विभाग को बताएं कि क्या आपकी कोई चिंता या समस्या है जिसे संबोधित करने की आवश्यकता है, और हम समाधान खोजने के लिए मिलकर काम करेंगे।

* * *

### 4.2 HR: Orientation ( Induction )

- Training Objective:

  Prepare training videos for new candidates at Hope Hospital, Ayushman Hospital, and Raftaar Emergency Seva to ensure proper understanding and use of hospital management software and medical workflows.
- Core Topics for Training Videos:

- Software Usage:

- Bed allotment procedures.
- Registration processes for OPD/IPD patients.
- Generating and managing bills through the billing activity sheet (Activity Sheet 19).

- Billing and Payment Management:

- Understanding and using advance statements.
- Tracking payments made by admitted patients.
- Identifying outstanding amounts and recovering payments effectively.
- Importance of maintaining accurate records of patient advance payments.

- Documentation and Notes Preparation:

- Creating discharge notes and OPD notes by nurses and doctors.
- Allocating surgeries and linking them to billing processes.
- Utilizing AI tools for efficient and accurate preparation of notes and records.

- Medical Training:

- Overview of the 10 most common diseases encountered in the hospital.
- Introduction to 10 common surgeries performed and their associated workflows.
- Familiarization with 10 key surgeons and their specializations.
- Overview of 10 key physicians and their department-specific expertise.

- Departmental Operations:

- Understanding departmental roles and responsibilities.
- Ensuring inter-departmental coordination for seamless patient care and management.

- Goals:

- Equip staff with essential skills for efficient hospital management.
- Enhance patient care through standardized processes.
- Foster familiarity with common medical conditions and surgical procedures handled in the hospital.
- Ensure clear understanding of AI integration in medical documentation.

10 points for the orientation of newly appointed nurses and other staff at both Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital:

Welcome and Introduction: The orientation should start with a warm welcome by the Head table consisting of the President, Vice-President, and Secretary Treasurer. Introduce the Management Committee team consisting of six senior managers from both hospitals.

Tour of the Hospitals: Arrange a detailed tour of both hospitals in the first week of induction. The tour should familiarise the nurses with different wards, operation theatres, emergency department, ICU, pharmacy, cafeteria, restrooms, and other important areas. Uniform, ID card and username ( for hope softwares) and email ID is provided within 1 week of appointment. Speak up policy is explained and is an integral part of 1st weeks training.

Roles and Responsibilities: Clearly define the roles and responsibilities of the nurses and other staff. Inform them about their daily duties, shift timings, patient care protocols, documentation procedures, and any specific tasks related to their roles. Who will report to them and whom they should report to should be defined and format of reporting is defined and shared.

Duties of Nurses:

- Administer the correct medication to the appropriate patient at the designated time.
- Possess comprehensive knowledge of the billing procedures for every patient.
- Promptly communicate critical reports to the respective consultants.
- Exhibit courteousness, always introducing themselves to both patients and doctors.
- Ensure the cleanliness and hygiene of the ward rooms and restrooms.
- Be diligent in conserving energy by turning off lights, fans, and air conditioners when rooms are unoccupied.

Hospital Policies and Protocols: Discuss the hospital's policies and protocols. This should include a notice period of one month in case of resignation, hygiene and infection control procedures, patient confidentiality and rights, reporting procedures, medication administration policies, and emergency response protocols.

Equipment Training: Arrange for the Biomedical Engineering (BME) team to provide training on the use of medical equipment. This training should include the use of patient monitors, infusion pumps, ventilators, and other specialised equipment.

Use of WhatsApp Groups: Educate them about the use of WhatsApp groups for various reporting purposes like the working status of equipment, consultant visits, and linen stock.

Documentation and Reporting: Train the nurses on how to document patient information, how to use the hospital's electronic health record system, and how to report any incidents or issues.

Mandatory Training Sessions: Inform them about the compulsory nurses training from 2 to 3 pm every Saturday. These sessions should focus on continuing education, professional development, and staying updated with the latest in healthcare.

Point of Contact: Introduce them to Kajal, who will be the single point of contact for all their concerns, queries, or information needs during their tenure at the hospital.

Safety Measures and Grievance Redressal: Train them on safety procedures and inform them about the hospital's grievance redressal mechanism. This includes fire safety, handling of biomedical waste, dealing with hazardous materials, and the procedures to voice any concerns or issues they might have.

Remember, a well-planned and comprehensive orientation is crucial in ensuring that your nursing staff is well-prepared to provide the highest quality of patient care.

### 4.3 HR: Punctuality

Let's ensure punctuality to streamline our OPD operations, as delays in investigations and reports have been causing inconvenience to our patients. Your timely arrival directly impacts patient satisfaction and overall hospital efficiency. Let's continue our commitment to providing the best healthcare experience.

Uniform and ID cards have to be issued to newly inducted staff within 1 week of joining. Uniforms have to be ordered from Amazon portal only. ID cards can be designed using canva.

### 4.4 HR: Salary SOP

1. Conduct a job analysis: Review the duties and responsibilities of each position in the hospital, including the required qualifications, education, and experience.
2. Research industry standards: Gather information on the typical salaries for similar positions in other hospitals of similar size and location.
3. Create a pay scale: Using the information gathered from the job analysis and industry research, create a pay scale that includes a range of salaries for each position.
4. Consider factors that affect pay: Take into account factors such as experience, education, certifications, and performance when determining a specific salary for each employee.
5. Review and revise: Regularly review the salary structure and make adjustments as necessary to ensure that it remains fair and equitable for all employees.
6. Communicate the salary structure: Clearly communicate the salary structure to all employees so they understand how their pay is determined and how they can advance within the organisation.
7. Be transparent: Be transparent and fair in your approach while deciding the salary structure.
8. Have an open-door policy: Encourage employees to bring up any concerns they have with their pay, and be willing to address them fairly and honestly.

### 4.5 HR:  Go Green personal performance scale

The Go Green personal performance scale is based on the following criteria:

- Givers Gain: Assessing the individual's willingness to give referrals and support to other members of the organisation. Evaluation on a scale of 1 to 20.
- Education: Assessing the individual's willingness to attend training and educational events to improve their skills and knowledge. Evaluation on a scale from 1 to 10.
- Attendance: Assessing the individual's attendance at meetings and events. Evaluation on a scale from 1 to 10.
- Networking: Assessing the individual's networking skills and ability to connect with other members of the organisation. Evaluation on a scale of 1 to 20.
- Business Development: Assessing the individual's ability to generate new business for the organisation. Evaluation on a scale of 1 to 20.
- Following Through: Assessing the individual's ability to follow through on commitments and take action on their goals. Evaluation on a scale of 1 to 20.

It's important to note that this can be modified as per the hospital's requirement and should be communicated and explained clearly to the staff. The training is given to all interested staff in the morning huddle conducted at 9 am every day. This will help to ensure that the performance assessment process is fair and objective, and that staff are aware of how their performance is being evaluated. The Go green points evaluation system should be used to rate the staff on each criteria, and the leadership team will be responsible for evaluating the staff on the criteria of networking, givers gain, business development, and following through.

### 4.6 HR: Physiotherapy Department Salary Slab

1\. Entry-Level Physiotherapist (0-2 Years of Experience)

- Qualification: Bachelor’s degree in Physiotherapy (BPT).
- Starting Salary: ₹15,000 per month.
- Timing: Minimum 4hrs shift
- Increment Policy: An annual increment of 10% based on performance.

2\. Mid-Level Physiotherapist (2-5 Years of Experience)

- Qualification: Bachelor’s degree in Physiotherapy (BPT) with additional certifications or a Master’s degree in Physiotherapy (MPT).
- Starting Salary: ₹20,000 to ₹25,000 per month.
- Timing: Full Time
- Increment Policy: An annual increment of 10-15% based on performance and additional responsibilities.

3\. Senior Physiotherapist (5+ Years of Experience)

- Qualification: Master’s degree in Physiotherapy (MPT) with specialised certifications.
- Starting Salary: ₹30,000 to ₹35,000 per month.
- Timing: Full Time
- Increment Policy: An annual increment of 15-20% based on performance, leadership, and contribution to research or development programs.

Special Considerations:

- Multiple Facility Responsibility: Physiotherapists asked to work across both Ayushman Nagpur Hospital and Hope Hospital will receive an additional monthly allowance of ₹5,000 to their base salary to compensate for the added responsibilities and travel.
- Continuing Education: Encourage and financially support advanced certifications and specialisations with a one-time bonus or salary adjustment upon completion.
- Performance Bonuses: Apart from the annual increments, consider introducing performance bonuses for exceptional patient care, innovation in treatment, and contribution to the hospital’s reputation.

Review and Adjustments:

- The salary structure should be reviewed annually to adjust for inflation, market standards, and the hospital's financial performance.
- Feedback from the physiotherapy team should be considered during the review to ensure the salary structure remains competitive and fair.

Implementation:

- This salary slab is to be implemented immediately, with adjustments made to existing employees' salaries where necessary to align with the new structure.
- All salary adjustments should be communicated clearly and transparently with the respective employees, ensuring they understand the rationale behind their salary and any changes made.

This structured approach aims to provide clarity, motivation, and a growth path for the physiotherapists at Ayushman Nagpur Hospital and Hope Hospital, ensuring that the compensation is competitive, fair, and in line with the industry standards, while also recognizing the unique contributions and responsibilities of each physiotherapist.

4.70 Memorandum of Understanding for Payment Policies and Surgical Procedures Between Hope Group of Hospitals and Medical  Consultants

### Memorandum of Understanding (MOU)

Between

Hope Group Hospitals

And

Doctors, Consultants, and Anesthetists

* * *

Introduction

This Memorandum of Understanding (MOU) is made and entered into by and between Hope Group Hospitals (hereinafter referred to as "the Hospital"), owned by Dr M Hope hospital Pvt Ltd. and the Doctors, Consultants, and Anaesthetists (hereinafter referred to as "the Practitioners"). The purpose of this MOU is to delineate the terms and conditions related to payment policies, surgery tariffs, consultation fees, and other related matters to ensure financial stability, transparency, and consistency in the Hospital's operations.

Purpose

The aim of this MOU is to:

1. Standardize and clarify payment procedures.
2. Adjust tariffs for surgeries and consultations.
3. Establish a clear framework for the engagement of consultants and anaesthetists.
4. Ensure timely payments and professional conduct.
5. Enhance financial management and operational efficiency.

Background

Historically, the Hospital has operated with informal arrangements regarding payments and tariffs. As healthcare services have evolved, so have financial practices. To align with contemporary needs and maintain a sustainable financial model, the Hospital's management, under the leadership of Dr. Murali BK, has decided to formalize these practices. This MOU serves to mitigate misunderstandings, ensure timely payments, and foster a professional and cooperative working environment.

Terms and Conditions

1\. Response and Treatment Initiation

1. Consultants, anesthetists, and surgeons should visit admitted patients within 1 hour of receiving a call from the hospital and start treatment immediately.
2. Surgeons and anesthetists should not postpone surgeries.
3. Anaesthetist should attend to all calls at night. Extra Emergency night charges will be paid. Only anesthetists willing to do night calls will be given calls for day cases.

2\. Consultation Fees

- For cashless (Yojna and Panel)  patients, OPD consultation is 350 and IPD visit is 500 for Ayushman hospital patients and for private patients, OPD consultation is 500 and IPD visit is 1000 for Ayushman hospital patients.
- OPD consultation is 500 and IPD visit is 1000 for Hope hospital patients considering the distance to be traveled to reach the hospital.
-  Ultrasound charges to the radiologist are 800 for Hope hospital and 500 for Ayushman hospital.

3\. Ultrasound Charges

- Radiologists:

- ₹800 for Hope Hospital (ultrasound)
- ₹500 for Ayushman Hospital (ultrasound)

4\. Delay in Payment for Cashless Cases

1. Payments for cashless cases will be delayed by three months from the date of service.
2. The Hospital will share the username and password of CGHS, PMJAY, and MJPJAY with the consultants to verify if the payments have been made to the hospital.

5\. Surgery Tariff Adjustments

- Surgery Timing:

1. Surgeries performed between 10 PM and 5 AM, surgeon and anaesthetists will be paid 20% more than the agreed-upon tariff.

- Anesthesia Charges for Private Patients:

1. General Anesthesia (GA): ₹3500
2. Spinal and Regional Anesthesia: ₹2500
3. Other Anesthesia / Standby/short GA / Sedation: ₹1500

- Anesthesia Charges for Cashless Patients:

1. General Anesthesia (GA): ₹3000
2. Spinal and Regional Anesthesia: ₹2000
3. Other Anesthesia / Standby/short GA / Sedation: ₹1000

- Extended Surgery Charges for Private Patients:

1. Surgeries lasting more than three hours and up to five hours: GA charges will be ₹4000.
2. Surgeries exceeding five hours: GA charges will be ₹4500 (capped).

If multiple surgeries are performed in one sitting the second surgery is paid 50 percent and third surgery will be paid 25 percent of the tariff

6\. Anaesthetist Engagement

- Surgeons must inform the anaesthetist (if they bring their own anaesthetist) of the Hospital's tariff rates.
- Anaesthetists must agree to the Hospital's tariff before engaging in surgery.

7\. Consultation Payments

1. OPD and IPD visit charges for all patients will be paid within 24 hours of the consultation.
2. Payments for technicians or assistants accompanying cardiologists or surgeons, The charges to pay assistants and technicians is for  CAG- Rs 1000 & PTCA - A maximum ofRs 2000
3. No advance payments will be made to surgeons, anaesthetists, or their assistants. No payment in advance should be insisted for any reason.

8\. Discounts

1. Hospital employees receive a 50% discount on surgeon fees.
2. Relatives of hospital staff receive a 25% discount on surgeon fees.

9\. Payment Procedures

1. Payments should not be collected directly from patients by the Practitioners.
2. All payments must be deposited at the hospital counter.
3. The Chief Accountant will handle all payments to consultants and surgeons.
4. The payment counter is separate from the receipt counter to ensure proper financial tracking.

10\. Referral Payments

1. If a patient is referred by a consultant, the patient will pay ₹1000 to the Hospital as OPD consultation charges.

1. Out of this amount, the consultant will be paid ₹800 within 24 hours.

2. For hospital patients, the patient will pay ₹1000 to the Hospital as OPD consultation charges.

1. Out of this amount, the consultant will be paid ₹500 within 24 hours.

3. All payments will be processed in the accountant's chamber, not at the front office reception desk.

11\. Equipment for Specialized Surgeries

1. ENT surgeons, laparoscopic surgeons, and arthroscopic surgeons must bring their own scopes to operate in Hope Hospital.
2. Patients cannot be shifted to Ayushman Hospital as it is considered unethical and against the terms and conditions with the Yojna and corporates.

12\. Consultant Appointments and On-Call Days

- The Hospital will appoint a minimum of 2 consultants in each speciality and allot on-call days on mutual consent.

13\. Charges for High-Risk Patients

- The surgeons and anesthetists' charges for HIV and HbSAg positive patients will be a maximum of 50 percent more than the agreed upon tariff in both panel and private patients. Consultants will not refuse treating to perform HIV and HbsAg positive patients.

14\. Implant Procurement

1. Implants, including those for cardiac, neuro, and peripheral angio cath lab procedures, will be purchased by the hospital.
2. All arthroscopic implants will be clubbed with the surgeon’s fees package if procured by the surgeon. There is a cap of ₹9000 for the cost of arthroscopic and spine implants for all joints.
3. Gastroenterology implants have to be approved by hospital management 24 hours prior to the date of the procedure.

15\. Patient Counseling and Estimates

- Consultants may need to counsel patients to increase the estimate of surgical treatment. This does not allow surgeons to increase their fees.
- Patients admitted directly to the hospital, even if looking for a specific consultant, are considered hospital patients due to promotional activities.

16\. Review and Contact Restrictions

1. Consultants will not call patients to other hospitals or clinics for review.
2. Consultants are not allowed to share their mobile number or contact details with patients.
3. Consultants cannot solicit Hope hospital employees to work for them.

17\. Specialist Referrals

- Patients needing specialist opinions must be referred to doctors within the Hope group of hospitals only.

18\. Investigation Protocols

- Individual Investigations above Rs 3000 if required for cashless patients have to be discussed with the Director Corporate before speaking to the patient or relatives, prescribing or writing the requisition.  All investigations must be done within the Hope group of hospitals. If unavailable, the hospital management decides the location and charges for the investigations.

19\. Medication Procurement

- Individual medicine cost above Rs 3000 if required for cashless patients have to be discussed with the Director Corporate before speaking to the patient or relatives, prescribing or writing the requisition. All medicines must be procured from the hospital pharmacy, and only the available brands should be prescribed.

20\. Influence on Call Preferences

- Consultants should not influence resident doctors or managers to be preferred for call duty over other consultants.

21\. If a patient is referred by a consultant, the profit is shared equally between the hospital and the referring doctor.The expenses are deducted before calculating profit

22\. The hospital will share a “surgeries performed” statement by the 25th of the month for the previous month. The statement will have the surgeries and procedures performed, TDS deducted and the amount payable.

* * *

Conclusion

This MOU reflects the commitment of both Hope Group Hospitals and the Practitioners to uphold these standards, ensuring operational efficiency, timely and fair compensation, and a positive working environment. By formalizing these guidelines, the Hospital aims to enhance transparency and consistency in its financial dealings, benefiting all stakeholders involved.

* * *

Signatories

On behalf of Hope Group Hospitals:

Dr. Murali BK

Signature: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

On behalf of the Practitioners:

\[Consultant's Name\]

Signature: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

Date: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

Effective Date: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

By signing below, both parties agree to the terms and conditions outlined in this MOU.

### 4.9 Nurses: Job description

Responsibility for medication management: Ensure that oral medications are securely packaged in envelopes and accurately labelled.

- Patient Identification and Safety: Guarantee all in-patient department (IPD) patients receive a wristband with the appropriate registration sticker for seamless identification and tracking.
- Enhancing Patient Communication: Nurses must strive to improve communication with patients, making sure to obtain informed consent for all procedures.
- Encouraging Cohesion Among Nursing Staff: Maintain respectful, polite, and collaborative communication with other nursing staff to foster unity within the team.
- Effective Handovers: Both oral and written handovers should be clear, comprehensive, and detailed to ensure continuity of patient care.
- Document Management: Utilise clips files specifically for IPD patients instead of OPD files to maintain proper patient records.
- Medication Reconciliation: Verify the medications the patient is taking when they are admitted to the hospital to prevent medication errors.
- Billing Management: Update the billing activity sheet daily to ensure accurate tracking of patient financial transactions.
- Tracking Consultant Visits: Keep track of consultant visits by updating both the register and the relevant WhatsApp group.
- Recording Patient Room Changes: Promptly update the register and the relevant WhatsApp group whenever there is a change in an IPD patient's room.

### 4.91 Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for Daily Bed Making and Reporting on Available Linen

\#### Purpose

To establish a consistent and efficient process for daily bed making in the healthcare setting and to ensure accurate reporting and management of available linen, thereby promoting patient comfort, hygiene, and infection control.

\#### Scope

This SOP applies to all nursing staff responsible for patient care and bed management in the healthcare facility.

\#### Responsibilities

\- \*\*Nursing Staff\*\*: Responsible for making beds daily and reporting on linen availability.

\- \*\*Nurse Manager/Supervisor\*\*: Ensures compliance with the SOP, manages linen inventory, and addresses any discrepancies or shortages.

\- \*\*Housekeeping Department\*\*: Provides clean linen as per the requirements and schedules regular linen deliveries.

\#### Materials Needed

\- Clean bed linen (sheets, pillowcases, blankets)

\- Protective gloves

\- Linen hamper or container for soiled linen

\#### Procedure

\##### Daily Bed Making

1\. \*\*Preparation\*\*:

\- Wash hands thoroughly and put on protective gloves.

\- Gather all necessary clean linen before approaching the bed.

\- Ensure the room is adequately ventilated and the patient is comfortable with the bed-making process.

2\. \*\*Stripping the Bed\*\*:

\- If the patient is out of bed, remove all used linen and place it directly into the linen hamper. Avoid shaking the linen to minimize the spread of pathogens.

\- If the patient is in bed, perform a modified bed making, changing one side at a time to ensure the patient’s comfort and safety.

3\. \*\*Making the Bed\*\*:

\- Place the bottom sheet evenly on the bed, tucking in corners and sides securely under the mattress.

\- Add the top sheet, blanket, and any additional layers required, ensuring they are aligned and tucked in neatly.

\- Replace the pillowcase and position the pillow comfortably at the head of the bed.

4\. \*\*Finalizing\*\*:

\- Ensure all linen is smooth and free from wrinkles to prevent skin irritation or pressure ulcers.

\- Dispose of gloves and wash hands after completing the bed-making process.

\##### Reporting on Available Linen

1\. \*\*Daily Inventory Check\*\*:

\- Conduct a daily count of all linen in use and in storage.

\- Check for any damaged or soiled linen that needs replacement.

2\. \*\*Reporting\*\*:

\- Record the inventory count on the designated linen inventory sheet or system.

\- Report any shortages, excesses, or issues with the quality of linen to the nurse manager/supervisor.

3\. \*\*Communication with Housekeeping\*\*:

\- Coordinate with the housekeeping department for the replenishment of linen and the proper disposal or laundering of soiled linen.

\- Ensure a continuous feedback loop for any changes in linen quality or supply needs.

\#### Compliance

\- Adhere to infection control policies and procedures when handling clean and soiled linen.

\- Follow patient confidentiality and privacy laws during the bed-making process.

\#### Documentation

\- Maintain accurate records of linen usage and inventory on a daily basis.

\- Document any patient feedback or incidents related to bed making or linen quality in the patient’s care report.

\#### Review and Update

\- This SOP should be reviewed annually or as needed to reflect changes in guidelines, procedures, or linen management practices.

\- Staff training sessions should be conducted following any significant updates to the SOP.

\#### Approval

\*\*\[Signature of Approving Authority\]\*\*

\*\*Date: \[Insert Date\]\*\*

This SOP is designed to ensure a standardized approach to bed making and linen management, enhancing patient care and operational efficiency in the healthcare setting.

Subject: Mandatory Daily Notes in IPD Files

Daily Notes in IPD Files:

It is mandatory to write daily notes in the IPD files for all inpatients.

These notes should include observations, examination findings, patient responses, treatments administered, and any significant events or changes in condition.

The notes must be clear, concise, and written in a professional tone.

Proper documentation ensures continuity of care and provides an accurate record for future reference.

Please ensure that the notes are recorded on the same day without delay, and that they comply with our hospital's documentation standards.

This practice is in line with our commitment to patient well-being, evidence-based medicine, and transparency in care. Your adherence to this guideline is crucial in maintaining the quality of patient care and fostering trust and confidence in our services.

### 4.10 Nurse : Salary Criteria at Hope & Ayushman Hospital

Objective: The purpose of this SOP is to establish a transparent and fair salary criteria for nurses based on their education, experience, and overall performance (Go Green) at Hope & Ayushman Hospital. This SOP aims to attract and retain skilled nursing staff and promote a positive work environment.

1\. Salary Bands: The salary bands for different nursing positions (GDA, ANM, GNM, BSC) will be determined based on the candidate's experience and the state in which they are employed (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh, Maharashtra).

2\. Education & Experience-based Salary Structure:

2.1. Freshers:

- For GDA: Rs. 3000 (in all locations)
- For ANM: Rs. 7000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 8000 (Maharashtra)
- For GNM: Rs. 7000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 7000-8000 (Maharashtra)
- For BSC: Rs. 8000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 8000-9000 (Maharashtra)

2.2. 1 Year Experience:

- For GDA: Rs. 3000-5000 (in all locations)
- For ANM: Rs. 7000-8000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 8000-9000 (Maharashtra)
- For GNM: Rs. 7000-9000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 8000-10000 (Maharashtra)
- For BSC: Rs. 8000-12000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 9000-13000 (Maharashtra)

2.3. 2 - 3 Years Experience:

- For GDA: Rs. 5000-6000 (in all locations)
- For ANM: Rs. 8000-9500 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 9000-10500 (Maharashtra)
- For GNM: Rs. 9000-12000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 10000-13000 (Maharashtra)
- For BSC: Rs. 12000-15000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 13000-16000 (Maharashtra)

2.4. 3 - 5 Years Experience:

- For GDA: Rs. 6000-7000 (in all locations)
- For ANM: Rs. 9500-11500 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 10000-12000 (Maharashtra)
- For GNM: Rs. 12000-14000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 13000-15000 (Maharashtra)
- For BSC: Rs. 15000-18000 (Balaghat, Madhya Pradesh) / Rs. 16000-19000 (Maharashtra)

3\. Go Green Performance Criteria: In addition to education and experience, nurses will be evaluated based on their overall performance, which includes the following factors:

- Attendance: Regular and punctual attendance is expected of all nurses.
- Punctuality: Nurses should consistently be on time for their shifts and duties.
- Behaviour: Professional behaviour, respect, and empathy towards patients, colleagues, and hospital staff are essential.
- Patient Feedback: Patient feedback will be considered to assess the nurse's quality of care and communication.
- Feedback from Colleagues: Feedback from colleagues will be taken into account to evaluate teamwork and cooperation.

4\. Performance Evaluation Process:

- Performance evaluations will be conducted periodically, preferably annually, or more frequently if needed.
- Department heads and supervisors will be responsible for evaluating nurses' performance.
- Evaluations will be documented, and feedback will be provided to nurses to help them improve.

5\. Salary Increment and Bonuses:

- Nurses who consistently demonstrate excellent performance (Go Green) may be eligible for salary increments or bonuses as a recognition of their dedication and commitment.
- Salary increments and bonuses will be subject to the hospital's financial performance and policies.

6\. Communication:

- This SOP will be communicated to all nurses during the hiring process and orientation.
- Any updates or changes to the salary criteria will be communicated to all relevant staff.

7\. Review and Amendments:

- This SOP will be reviewed periodically to ensure its effectiveness and relevance.
- Amendments to this SOP can be made as per the hospital's requirements, but any significant changes will be communicated to all relevant parties.

By implementing this SOP, Hope & Ayushman Hospital aims to maintain a motivated and skilled nursing workforce while ensuring that salary criteria are transparent and fair for all nurses based on their education, experience, and overall performance.

1\. Never give it for more than 15 days.

2\. See Patient again after 15 days and re issue.

3\. Even in repeat case's, make sure that he or she is the patient , identify the pt. By photo I. D. Card , and then issue. Not to the attendants.

3\. Avoid issuing certificates for diseases which you are not treating / or trained to treat. (Other Disciplines)

4\. Describe the disability at best as you can even if you don't know how to grade it.

5\. MOST IMPORTANT

It is a legal document

Even if you print otherwise, it is admissible in court & you can't say , " that it was not intended for legal purposes"

6\. Certificates must address a particular person...."like Principal of the school, employer etc.

Don't write whomsoever it may concern.

7\. Never give from back date

8\. Never give without your OPD days.

9\. Never give fitness on advanced date or back date.

10\. Never give fitness, if Rest is given by somebody else.

11\. Give if you can justify the disease or ailment and duration also for that particular disease.

12\. If there is no disease, then always ask purpose why are you want to take medical, then only give 2- 3 days If someone's family member in severe life threatening to attending him on humanity ground, pl verify it before giving, because opinion  can differ person to person.

13\.  Physical presence is a must because pt. May be abroad or heavenly abode. So never write down PNB (Patient NOT Brought)

14\. You are a responsible class one gazetted officer verifying the physical presence and attendance.
