### 4.13 RMO: Immediate consultant visit-

Informed again on 23rd march 2025

As the CMD of Hope Hospital and Ayushman Hospital, I would like to address a growing concern regarding patient care. We have noticed that some good-paying patients have recently been leaving the hospital before their treatment has even begun. This is unacceptable and must be addressed immediately.

It has always been a rule that all patients must be seen within half an hour of admission or OPD registration. Additionally, surgeons must operate on patients within 2-3 hours, even if they are elective cases. This rule has been put in place to ensure that our patients receive prompt and efficient treatment, and to prevent the loss of revenue for the hospital.

I expect all surgeons and physicians to follow this rule and make every effort to see patients promptly. This is not only important for our financial success, but more importantly, it is essential for the well-being of our patients. I thank you for your attention to this matter and for your continued commitment to providing exceptional patient care.

As the owner of Hope Hospital, it has come to my attention that there are certain job responsibilities that are not being followed. Therefore, I am issuing this SOP (Standard Operating Procedure) to ensure that patient care is provided in a timely and efficient manner. Please read and follow the below SOP carefully:

Within half an hour of admission, the consulting doctor must visit the patient. This is crucial to determine the course of treatment and to address any immediate concerns or questions the patient may have.

In case the patient requests surgery, the consulting doctor must perform the surgery within 2 hours of the request. This is important to alleviate the patient's pain and discomfort and to prevent any delay in treatment.

Before handing over the discharge summary to the patient, the consulting doctor must send it to the concerned consultant for correction. This is necessary to ensure that the patient's treatment plan is accurate and complete.

On discharge, the consulting doctor must inform the concerned consultant that their patient is being discharged. The discharge notes must be written by the consultant and should contain the diagnosis, surgeries performed, and the treatment on discharge.

It is essential that all resident doctors follow these SOPs to provide efficient and timely care to our patients. Failure to comply with these SOPs may result in disciplinary action.

### 4.15 Housekeeping Staff : JD

Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for Hospital Housekeeping Supervision

- Purpose: The purpose of this SOP is to ensure that the hospital environment is maintained in a clean, sanitary, and appealing condition. This procedure will help prevent nosocomial infections and ensure patient safety, comfort, and satisfaction.
- Scope: This SOP is applicable to all the housekeeping staff and supervisors at Hope Hospital and Ayushman Nagpur Hospital.
- Responsibilities:

- Housekeeping Supervisors: Supervise the housekeeping staff, ensure adherence to the SOP, conduct regular inspections, provide training, and handle grievances.
- Housekeeping Staff: Adhere to the SOP, ensure cleanliness and hygiene, report any irregularities to the supervisor.
- Management Committee: To ensure implementation and adherence to the SOP, conduct audits and reviews.

- Procedure:

- Daily Cleanliness: Housekeeping staff should perform cleaning duties as per the assigned schedule, which should include sweeping, mopping, dusting, waste disposal, and restroom cleaning. They should ensure that the common areas, patient rooms, OTs, ICUs, and other areas are well-maintained.videos of all toilets and storage areas have to be shared in the whatsapp group.
- Deep Cleaning: Periodic deep cleaning schedules must be set for all areas, especially operation theatres, ICUs, and other critical areas. Deep cleaning should involve thorough cleaning and disinfection.
- Infection Control: Infection control protocols should be strictly followed. Staff should use appropriate personal protective equipment (PPE), and use approved disinfectants while cleaning.
- Waste Management: Staff should segregate waste as per the hospital's biomedical waste management guidelines. They should handle, transport, and dispose of waste in designated areas only.
- Training: Housekeeping staff should be trained on the SOP, hygiene and sanitation practices, infection control, waste management, handling of cleaning chemicals, and safety procedures.
- Inspections: Housekeeping supervisors should perform daily inspections to ensure adherence to the SOP and cleanliness standards. Any deviations or issues should be recorded and addressed promptly.
- Reporting and Communication: Housekeeping staff should report any issues or irregularities to the supervisor. The housekeeping department should communicate with other departments to ensure coordinated efforts for maintaining cleanliness and hygiene.
- Water seepages have to be stopped in 6 hours of reporting

- Review: This SOP should be reviewed periodically, or whenever there are changes in procedures, equipment, or cleaning chemicals.

- Non-compliance: Any non-compliance to this SOP should be addressed immediately. Actions should be taken as per the hospital's disciplinary policy.

This SOP aims to ensure a clean, hygienic, and safe environment for patients, staff, and visitors in our hospitals. The hospitals are committed to maintaining the highest standards of cleanliness and hygiene.

### 14.6  Bell Boy/ Hospital porter to be presently done by junior front office staff

In a hospital setting, a Bell Boy, often referred to as a Hospital Porter, plays a vital role in maintaining the smooth operation of the facility. While the exact responsibilities can vary depending on the size and structure of the hospital, a few general duties are often common. Here are some of the primary roles and responsibilities:

- Patient Assistance: Bell Boys assist patients by transporting them to and from different areas within the hospital. This can include moving patients from their rooms to various departments such as radiology, pathology, operation theaters, physiotherapy, etc. They might use wheelchairs or stretchers for patients who cannot move on their own.
- Material Transportation: They may be responsible for moving medical equipment, supplies, specimens, documents, and other items around the hospital. This may include delivering fresh linen to rooms, taking laundry away, or transporting medical equipment.
- Room Preparation: After a patient is discharged, Bell Boys may assist the housekeeping staff in preparing the room for the next patient. This may involve removing used linens, cleaning the room, or moving furniture.
- Guest Services: They may also help visitors by providing directions or escorting them to the correct department or patient room. In some settings, they might also assist with luggage or other belongings.
- Emergency Assistance: In emergency situations, Bell Boys play a crucial role by quickly transporting patients, equipment, or medical staff where they are needed.
- Maintenance Assistance: They can also assist the maintenance department by reporting any noticeable issues, like a malfunctioning elevator or a burned-out light bulb.

The role of a Bell Boy or Hospital Porter is often physically demanding, and it requires excellent interpersonal skills due to the high level of interaction with patients, their families, and hospital staff. They are an integral part of the hospital team, contributing significantly to the efficient and patient-friendly operation of the facility.

Dhiraj's patient was admitted with 2 days of intimation. Dismal sanitation and very unclean toilet. She is mother-in-law of Dhiraj's sister. Admitted at 10 PM. No housekeeping and bell boy in Absolutely, Dr. Murali B K. This incident indeed indicates a gap in service quality at our hospital, which we strive to maintain at the highest level. This situation highlights several areas for improvement. Here is an outline of how we can enhance our services and prevent such occurrences in the future:

- Advance Notification System: We can better utilize our advance notification system. When Dhiraj's mother-in-law was scheduled for admission with a 2-day notice, there should have been ample time to prepare her room, including thoroughly cleaning the restroom. To improve this, we need to enhance our communication protocols between the admission department, housekeeping, and patient service assistants.
- Night Shift Housekeeping & Patient Service Assistants: Our services should not be limited to specific hours of the day. The absence of housekeeping staff and patient service assistants during night hours is an oversight. We should ensure there is sufficient staff around the clock to maintain the cleanliness and patient service standards we have set for Hope Hospital. This would involve hiring additional staff or shifting current staff schedules to ensure 24/7 coverage.
- Staff Training: We should provide ongoing staff training to reinforce the importance of cleanliness and service quality in all patient areas. They should understand that their responsibilities directly impact patient satisfaction and safety. A module on empathy and soft skills training would also be beneficial, ensuring staff understand how their actions or inactions affect patients and their families.
- Prompt Response to Feedback: We must ensure an effective feedback system for immediate action when patients or their families have complaints. In Dhiraj's mother-in-law's case, immediate attention to the unclean toilet could have mitigated her dissatisfaction.
- Quality Assurance: We need a more robust quality assurance system, particularly for the sanitation department. Regular checks and surprise audits can help identify and rectify issues before they reach the patient.
- Improving Interdepartmental Communication: Effective communication between different departments can ensure that all necessary preparations have been completed prior to the patient's arrival.

This incident serves as a reminder that our ultimate aim is to provide quality service to our patients, regardless of the time of day. It's an opportunity for us to strengthen our systems, improve staff training, and ultimately provide the level of service our patients expect and deserve. We appreciate this being brought to our attention and will make the necessary improvements.

### 5.3 Yellow Fever Vaccine Administration

[International Certification of Yellow fever vaccination or Prophylaxis consent 2020](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/13EyZeSNF2g4FFQGw8dkJyKJViVRWCX07odzuXSMdRMU/edit&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089181932271&usg=AOvVaw3GDSfqXecrF6gS-tUR_SAq)

Cost of yellow fever is 4000 rupees

Purpose: The purpose of this SOP is to outline the procedures for the safe and effective administration of the Yellow Fever vaccine while adhering to the best medical practices and regulatory guidelines.

- Scope: This SOP applies to all healthcare professionals involved in the administration of vaccines at Hope Hospital.
- Responsibilities:

- Healthcare Professionals: Administer the vaccine, adhere to the SOP, provide patient education, and document vaccination records.
- Management Committee: Ensure SOP implementation and adherence, provide necessary resources, conduct audits, and manage vaccine inventory.
- Reception Desk: Schedule vaccination appointments and manage patient records.

- Procedure:

- Vaccine Storage: Store the vaccine as per manufacturer’s guidelines, typically between 2°C to 8°C. Regularly monitor and record the storage temperature.
- Patient Screening: Screen patients for contraindications. This includes asking whether the patient is immunocompromised. The vaccine should not be given to infants under 9 months, pregnant women, immunocompromised individuals, or those allergic to any component of the vaccine. Obtain informed consent.
- Preparation: Reconstitute the vaccine using the diluent provided by the manufacturer just before administration. Do not use if the vaccine has changed colour or contains particles.
- Administration: Administer 0.5 mL of the vaccine subcutaneously, preferably in the upper arm. Follow standard hygiene practices, including hand hygiene and use of clean gloves.
- Post-Vaccination Monitoring: Monitor the patient for at least 15 minutes post-vaccination for any adverse reactions. Provide necessary medical intervention if required.
- Patient Education: Educate the patient about possible side effects and when to seek medical help. Remind them to carry their Yellow Fever Vaccination Certificate when travelling to areas where the vaccine is mandatory.
- Documentation: Record the vaccination in the patient’s medical records and provide the patient with a vaccination card. Maintain a vaccine administration log.

- Emergency Handling: Healthcare staff should be trained to manage any immediate adverse reactions, including anaphylaxis. An emergency kit including epinephrine should be readily available.
- Review: This SOP should be reviewed periodically and updated as necessary, based on new findings or changes in guidelines related to the Yellow Fever vaccine.
- Documentation: All vaccinations, patient reactions, temperature logs, and other related data should be documented for future audits and quality control.
- Non-compliance: Any non-compliance to this SOP should be addressed promptly and may lead to disciplinary action as per hospital policy.

The SOP aims to ensure the safe and effective administration of the Yellow Fever vaccine, thereby contributing to public health and the prevention of yellow fever.

### 5.4 Biomedical Engineers: Hospital Equipment and Machine Maintenance

Purpose

The purpose of this SOP is to guide the biomedical engineers, Ishin and Atul, in the daily, weekly, and monthly maintenance tasks for all hospital machines and equipment. This will ensure the equipment is kept in optimal condition, reducing downtime and improving patient care.

Scope

This SOP applies to all hospital machines and equipment, including but not limited to the generator, AHU, and OT equipment.

Roles and Responsibilities

- Biomedical Engineers, Ishin and Atul: Carry out maintenance, weekly training, servicing, and adherence to do's and don'ts, ensuring all machines are NABH ready.

Procedures

1\. Daily Procedures

- Inspection of all hospital machines and equipment, noting any visible wear and tear or malfunction.
- Perform routine servicing as required by the manufacturer's guidelines.

2\. Weekly Procedures

- Conduct weekly training sessions for relevant hospital staff on the correct usage of machines and equipment.
- Carry out comprehensive maintenance and servicing of all machines and equipment.

3\. Monthly Procedures

- Prepare and submit a monthly report detailing the status of all machines and equipment, any issues encountered, and their resolution.
- Conduct a thorough check to ensure all machines and equipment are NABH compliant.

Do's and Don'ts

- Do follow all manufacturer guidelines for the use and maintenance of all machines and equipment.
- Do keep a log of all maintenance activities.
- Do not attempt to repair any machine or equipment without the necessary training or guidance.
- Do not ignore any signs of malfunction or damage.

Documentation

- All maintenance activities, issues, and their resolution must be documented and maintained for future reference and audits.

### 5.5 Policy on Pathology Lab Tests

- Correct Reports: All lab reports must be accurate, clear, and concise. Any discrepancy or error should be corrected immediately, and the revised report should be disseminated promptly.
- Report Turn Around Time: The standard turnaround time for reports will be 3 hours from the time the sample is received, unless otherwise specified. If there is a delay, the requesting physician will be notified immediately.
- Use of Reagents: Only approved and validated reagents will be used for lab tests. The expiration dates and storage conditions must be strictly followed to maintain reagent efficacy.
- Purchase of Reagents: The lab manager is responsible for ensuring the procurement and supply of all reagents. This includes verifying the quality and quantity of the reagents and confirming their appropriate storage conditions.
- Cross-Checking: All lab results will undergo a secondary review by another qualified laboratory technician to ensure accuracy.
- Register: All incoming samples and their respective test results will be logged into a secure database. This includes details about the type of test, date of test, test result, and the technician who conducted the test.
- Outsourced Tests: The number of outsourced tests should be minimized, and all outsourcing should be done through pre-approved vendors only. The lab manager will keep a record of all outsourced tests.
- Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for Histopathology and Cytopathology:

- Samples will be processed following established protocols for histopathology and cytopathology.
- All samples will be handled with utmost care to prevent cross-contamination.
- Quality control measures will be implemented at every step of the procedure to ensure accuracy.

- Outsourced Testing: If tests are outsourced, they should be sent to a reliable, certified lab that has agreed to abide by our turnaround times and reporting standards. The lab manager will maintain a list of such labs.
- Rates: The rates for lab tests will be competitive and transparent. All charges will be clearly itemized on the invoice provided to the patient.
- Report Turn Around Time for Outsourced Tests: The standard turnaround time for reports of outsourced tests may vary based on the external lab's policies. This should be communicated to the requesting physician or patient as soon as possible.

5.7 Standard Operating Procedure (SOP) for Patient Management under Yojana Scheme at Hope & Ayushman Institutions

Upon the arrival of a patient at "Hope" under the Yojana scheme, they are to be promptly directed to "Ayushman" for comprehensive diagnosis and necessary investigations. It's imperative that no fees be charged to Yojana-approved patients; any deviation is considered fraud and will result in the immediate termination of the responsible employee. All diagnostic and investigative requisitions are to be electronically recorded via our designated software, ensuring accurate tracking and accountability. Handwritten requisitions are strictly prohibited. Dr. Shiraz will oversee and validate all patient referrals, and a dedicated register will document these interactions. Daily reporting of patient activities is mandatory. Following the completion of the Yojana treatment package at "Hope," patients must be immediately transitioned to "Ayushman" for further consultation. Sachin is responsible for strict adherence to this SOP.

Undertaking/ Memorandum of Understanding (MoU)BetweenHope Group of HospitalsAnd its employees

Employee Name: \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

Purpose: This Memorandum of Understanding (MoU) establishes the terms and conditions under which the employees of Hope Group of Hospitals will adhere to ethical practices and avoid any fraudulent activities while performing their duties. This agreement specifically addresses the recent incident involving Mr. Irfan, who was found collecting cash in his UPI account by displaying his QR code instead of the Hospital’s QR code, leading to a police complaint and FIR.

Scope: This MoU applies to all employees working in various units of Hope Group of Hospitals, including but not limited to Pharmacy, Canteen, Pathology, Billing Desk, and Reception.

Terms and Conditions:

1. Ethical Conduct:

- Employees must conduct themselves ethically and with integrity while performing their duties.
- Employees are prohibited from engaging in any form of fraudulent activities.

2. Prohibition of Personal Financial Transactions:

- Employees are strictly prohibited from collecting cash or any form of payment in their personal accounts while on duty.
- All financial transactions must be conducted through the official channels and QR codes of Hope Group of Hospitals.

3. Hospital Property:

- All units within the hospital, including Pharmacy, Canteen, Pathology, Billing Desk, and Reception, are the property of Hope Group of Hospitals.
- Employees have no right to claim ownership or personal control over any of these units.

4. Prohibition of Misrepresentation:

- Employees must not misrepresent themselves as owners or operators of any hospital units.
- Any employee found asking patients for money under false pretenses will be subject to severe disciplinary action.

5. Reporting and Disciplinary Actions:

- Any employee found engaging in fraudulent activities will be reported to the police and a formal complaint will be filed.
- Such activities will be considered fraud, and the employee will be handed over to the police for legal action.

6. Compliance:

- Employees must comply with all the policies and regulations set forth by Hope Group of Hospitals.
- Any breach of these terms will result in immediate disciplinary action, up to and including termination of employment.

Acknowledgment: By signing this MoU, the employee acknowledges understanding and agreement to adhere to the above terms and conditions. The employee also acknowledges that failure to comply with these terms will result in severe disciplinary action and potential legal consequences.

समझौता ज्ञापन (एमओयू)के बीचहोप ग्रुप ऑफ हॉस्पिटल्सऔर

\[कर्मचारी का नाम\]

उद्देश्य: यह समझौता ज्ञापन (एमओयू) होप ग्रुप ऑफ हॉस्पिटल्स के कर्मचारियों द्वारा उनके कर्तव्यों का पालन करते समय नैतिक प्रथाओं का पालन करने और किसी भी प्रकार की धोखाधड़ी गतिविधियों से बचने की शर्तों और शर्तों को स्थापित करता है। यह समझौता विशेष रूप से श्री इरफान के हालिया मामले को संबोधित करता है, जो अपने क्यूआर कोड के बजाय अस्पताल के क्यूआर कोड को प्रदर्शित करके अपने यूपीआई खाते में नकद एकत्र करते पाए गए थे, जिससे पुलिस शिकायत और एफआईआर दर्ज की गई थी।

दायरा: यह एमओयू होप ग्रुप ऑफ हॉस्पिटल्स के विभिन्न इकाइयों में कार्यरत सभी कर्मचारियों पर लागू होता है, जिसमें फार्मेसी, कैंटीन, पैथोलॉजी, बिलिंग डेस्क और रिसेप्शन शामिल हैं लेकिन इन्हीं तक सीमित नहीं है।

शर्तें और नियम:

1. नैतिक आचरण:

- कर्मचारियों को अपने कर्तव्यों का पालन करते समय नैतिकता और ईमानदारी के साथ व्यवहार करना चाहिए।
- कर्मचारियों को किसी भी प्रकार की धोखाधड़ी गतिविधियों में संलिप्त होने से मना किया जाता है।

2. व्यक्तिगत वित्तीय लेन-देन की मनाही:

- कर्मचारियों को ड्यूटी पर रहते हुए अपने व्यक्तिगत खातों में नकद या किसी भी प्रकार का भुगतान प्राप्त करने से मना किया जाता है।
- सभी वित्तीय लेन-देन होप ग्रुप ऑफ हॉस्पिटल्स के आधिकारिक चैनलों और क्यूआर कोड के माध्यम से ही किए जाने चाहिए।

3. अस्पताल की संपत्ति:

- अस्पताल के भीतर की सभी इकाइयाँ, जिनमें फार्मेसी, कैंटीन, पैथोलॉजी, बिलिंग डेस्क और रिसेप्शन शामिल हैं, होप ग्रुप ऑफ हॉस्पिटल्स की संपत्ति हैं।
- कर्मचारियों को इनमें से किसी भी इकाई पर स्वामित्व या व्यक्तिगत नियंत्रण का दावा करने का अधिकार नहीं है।

4. गलत प्रस्तुति की मनाही:

- कर्मचारियों को किसी भी अस्पताल इकाई के मालिक या ऑपरेटर के रूप में अपने को प्रस्तुत करने की मनाही है।
- किसी भी कर्मचारी को गलत बहाने से मरीजों से पैसे मांगते पाए जाने पर सख्त अनुशासनात्मक कार्रवाई की जाएगी।

5. रिपोर्टिंग और अनुशासनात्मक कार्रवाई:

- किसी भी कर्मचारी को धोखाधड़ी गतिविधियों में संलिप्त पाया जाएगा तो उसे पुलिस को रिपोर्ट किया जाएगा और औपचारिक शिकायत दर्ज की जाएगी।
- ऐसी गतिविधियों को धोखाधड़ी माना जाएगा, और कर्मचारी को कानूनी कार्रवाई के लिए पुलिस के हवाले किया जाएगा।

6. अनुपालन:

- कर्मचारियों को होप ग्रुप ऑफ हॉस्पिटल्स द्वारा निर्धारित सभी नीतियों और विनियमों का पालन करना होगा।
- इन शर्तों का कोई भी उल्लंघन तत्काल अनुशासनात्मक कार्रवाई, जिसमें रोजगार समाप्ति भी शामिल है, के परिणामस्वरूप होगा।

स्वीकृति: इस एमओयू पर हस्ताक्षर करके, कर्मचारी उपरोक्त शर्तों और शर्तों को समझने और पालन करने के लिए अपनी सहमति व्यक्त करता है। कर्मचारी यह भी स्वीकार करता है कि इन शर्तों का पालन करने में विफलता सख्त अनुशासनात्मक कार्रवाई और संभावित कानूनी परिणामों का कारण बनेगी।

### "Risk Management and Insurance in Healthcare at Hope and Ayushman Hospitals, Nagpur"

\[Slide 1: Opening Slide - Risk Management and Insurance at Hope and Ayushman Hospitals\]

Ishita: Good morning, esteemed colleagues of Hope and Ayushman Hospitals in Nagpur. Today's discussion is focused on navigating the intricacies of risk management and insurance, tailored specifically for our operations and the local challenges we face in Nagpur's healthcare environment.

Risk management in a hospital encompasses the processes and strategies used to identify, assess, mitigate, and monitor potential risks that could harm the organization, its patients, employees, and stakeholders. It involves a proactive approach to preventing adverse events, ensuring compliance with regulations, and maintaining financial stability. Key components include patient safety, staff training, legal compliance, disaster preparedness, and financial risk management, among others.

Here’s why it's crucial for the leadership team to be well-versed in risk management:

1\. \*\*Patient Safety and Quality of Care\*\*: At its core, risk management aims to protect patients from harm and ensure the highest quality of care. Leaders must prioritize patient safety to foster trust and satisfaction among patients and their families, reduce the incidence of medical errors, and improve clinical outcomes.

2\. \*\*Regulatory Compliance\*\*: Healthcare facilities operate under strict regulatory standards. Leadership needs to understand these requirements to ensure compliance with health laws, privacy regulations, and accreditation standards. Non-compliance can result in legal penalties, financial losses, and damage to the hospital's reputation.

3\. \*\*Financial Stability\*\*: Effective risk management strategies help protect the hospital’s financial resources. By identifying financial risks early, such as potential lawsuits or equipment failures, and by ensuring adequate insurance coverage, leaders can safeguard against unexpected expenses that could impact the hospital's budget and financial health.

4\. \*\*Operational Efficiency\*\*: Leadership teams need to ensure that hospital operations are resilient to disruptions, whether from natural disasters, supply chain issues, or technological failures. Understanding risk management enables leaders to develop contingency plans, ensuring continuity of care and minimizing operational disruptions.

5\. \*\*Reputation and Trust\*\*: The hospital’s reputation is closely tied to how well it manages risks. Effective risk management strategies demonstrate a commitment to excellence and responsibility, which can enhance public trust and confidence in the institution.

6\. \*\*Strategic Decision Making\*\*: Leaders equipped with risk management knowledge can make more informed strategic decisions. They can assess the potential risks and benefits of new services, technologies, or expansion plans, ensuring that growth opportunities do not expose the hospital to undue risk.

7\. \*\*Workforce Safety and Satisfaction\*\*: Protecting hospital staff from workplace hazards and ensuring a safe working environment is a crucial aspect of risk management. A safe and supportive workplace enhances employee satisfaction, retention, and recruitment, directly impacting the quality of patient care.

In essence, risk management is indispensable in the complex and high-stakes environment of healthcare. It requires the leadership team to be proactive, knowledgeable, and committed to implementing effective strategies that safeguard the hospital's patients, staff, resources, and reputation against potential risks.

\[Slide 2: Identifying Risks at Hope and Ayushman Hospitals\]

Ishita: In our hospitals, risk encompasses clinical, operational, financial, and strategic dimensions. Clinical risks may involve patient safety incidents specific to our patient demographics, while operational risks could include local supply chain vulnerabilities. Financial risks might stem from regional billing practices, and strategic risks could arise from local healthcare reforms or changes in patient population needs.

"In our hospitals, managing risk is a multifaceted challenge, deeply influenced by our local environment in Nagpur. Let me provide you with specific examples to illustrate this:

- Clinical Risks: Given Nagpur's demographic, with a significant portion of the population suffering from cardiovascular diseases and diabetes, a major clinical risk could involve managing chronic conditions and preventing hospital-acquired infections among this vulnerable patient group.
- Operational Risks: For the talk on "Risk Management and Insurance in Healthcare" at Hope and Ayushman Hospitals, Nagpur, the following real-life scenarios from the hospitals can serve as compelling examples to illustrate the challenges and actions taken in risk management and insurance strategies:

1\. Storm situation, \*\*Supply Chain Disruptions Due to Seasonal Monsoons\*\*: Nagpur's geographic location subjects it to seasonal monsoons, which can cause supply chain disruptions, affecting the delivery of essential medical supplies. An example of this was when delayed shipments of critical medications occurred last monsoon season. Swift action was taken to source alternatives locally, ensuring there was no impact on patient care. This highlights the importance of having robust supply chain risk management strategies and insurance to cover losses or delays.

2\. \*\*Impact of Natural Disasters on Hospital Operations\*\*: The Ayushman Hospital experienced flooding during the monsoon season, leading to the generator and lift being submerged. This disrupted patient transport to the 3rd floor, showcasing the necessity for preparedness against natural disasters, including insurance coverage for property damage and operational disruptions.

3\. \*\*Shortages of Essential Medical Supplies\*\*: Hope Hospital faced a shortage of Vasofix in the wards and pharmacy, critical for emergency patient admissions. This scenario underlines the need for maintaining adequate stock levels and insurance that can assist in quick replenishment in case of shortages.

4\. \*\*Equipment Malfunction and Mismanagement\*\*: An incident occurred where an ECG machine was either not working or malfunctioned at a critical time when a patient was brought in deceased. The device was also mislabeled, leading to confusion and distress among the patient's relatives, resulting in a ruckus at the hospital. This example emphasizes the importance of regular equipment maintenance, proper management, and having insurance to cover malpractice or equipment failure claims.

- 5\. Cybersecurity Breach Incident: Imagine a scenario where the hospital’s reception smartphone was hacked. The patients who were to pay online were paying to the hackers account for the days it was hacked. The patient data system is hacked, leading to the theft of sensitive patient information. This breach not only risks patient confidentiality but also exposes the hospital to potential legal actions and damages its reputation. The example could explore how cyber insurance and proactive cybersecurity risk management strategies can mitigate these risks.
- 6\. Critical HIMS Software issues: A dead patient was billed to ECHS stating that the patient was treated by us even after death. This was because of a software issue of not closing the admission even after the patient was discharged! The present software accounting module does not show outstanding payable if the patient does not pay any amount!
- 7\. Medical Equipment and manpower Failure during Critical Surgery: A high-tech surgery is underway when suddenly a critical piece of medical equipment like an image intensifier or arthroscopy fails, jeopardizing the patient's life and leading to a complex surgery being delayed. The scenario could discuss the importance of equipment breakdown insurance and regular maintenance checks to prevent such incidents.CPR training and Mock drill should be recorded
- 8\. Mass casualty, Pandemic Outbreak Response: Covid outbreak puts the hospital under immense pressure, leading to a shortage of beds and resources. The situation explores how business interruption insurance and contingency planning are crucial for healthcare facilities to manage such unprecedented health crises.Similar situation was faced in mass casualty situation in LIC Hope when a bus carrying WCL personnel met with an accident.
- 9\. Legal Action from a Wrongful Death Claim: A family files a wrongful death lawsuit against the hospital, claiming negligence after a patient dies due to what they allege is a misdiagnosis. This example could be used to highlight the role of professional liability insurance and the importance of thorough documentation and communication as preventive measures.
- 10\. Damage to Hospital Property by a mob: A  scenario where a fire in one of the hospital wings causes significant damage to the infrastructure and medical equipment, leading to temporary closure of that section. This would emphasize the importance of property insurance and disaster recovery planning in ensuring quick restoration and minimizing operational disruptions. Emergency Police numbers and whom to contact should be clearly identified. To prevent such incidents we need to have video counseling regarding all billing counseling and critical patient counseling. Fire response training  and mock drill to be given regularly.
- 11\. Pharmaceutical Liability Scenario: The hospital pharmacy accidentally dispenses the wrong medication to multiple patients, leading to adverse reactions. This situation could illustrate the necessity of pharmaceutical liability insurance and the implementation of stringent pharmaceutical risk management procedures.
- 12\. Yearly yellow fever vaccine shortage - Who will order and what is the minimum stock that should be available in both hospitals?
- 13\. Staff absent or late coming, leaving early issues:  3 minute meeting to be taken by Ruby, Shrikant, Suraj. If all 3 are absent then the president has to take a meeting by 10 am and report to Dr Murali by calling him! If a muslim festival is approaching, then replacements are decided 3 days in advance and informed in attendance -  whatsapp group and individually. Such irregularities  can be life threatening. And memos should be immediately issued within 24 hours of indiscipline.
- 14. Pilferages in OT and ward leading to loss of revenue and non availability of emergency drugs and disposables. Proper storage of OT stock by LT
- 15\. Overcharging of corporate patients during replacements and not returning drugs on discharge of corporate and insurance patients. Revenue loss
- 16. Implant commission being taken by surgeons leading to loss in revenue.
- 17. Theft of patient belongings
- 18\. Food contamination served to patients
- 19.Wrong medication, Unqualified staff
- 20.Accusation as a fraud hospital - ECHS accused Hope hospital of billing after patient had expired during covid.
- 21.Scarcity of Emergency commodities like vasofix etc.
- 22 Elevator, .Lift failure
- 23\. Anticipating a Mob, Mob in hospital, Unruly patient

- 24\. Sickness,.Injury death of employee
- 25.Surprise Raid, survey, audit by a corporate or government agency
- 26\. Fraud by Dr Sachin Jain. He was an RMO in Hope hospital. He made fake bills to show his father was admitted in hospital and claimed from insurance company. Was caught.
- 27\. Alleged Fraud by MD India patient stating that wrongly billed as ICU stay when the patient stayed in a room. MD india deempanneled Hope hospital for 5 years

- 32, Irfan running the canteen had taken payment by showing the QR code in his mobile. It was a case of fraud which was caught.

Mechanism to collect above information \- 3 minute meeting and rounding “Round” of hospitals.3 minute meeting to be taken by Ruby, Shrikant, Suraj. If all 3 are absent then the president has to take a meeting by 10 am and report to Dr Murali by calling him! The agenda is Manpower and machine status and patient feedback! Snap reporting and formless.ai ( Nurses incharge and coordinators) reporting to mandatory. 5 point reporting once a month is also mandatory. HT should always discuss if insurances are still valid and if any are expiring in the next 3 months.

These examples vividly demonstrate the various operational risks that healthcare institutions like Hope and Ayushman Hospitals face. They underscore the critical need for effective risk management strategies and comprehensive insurance solutions to mitigate these risks, ensuring continuous, quality patient care amidst uncertainties.

Financial Risks: Our billing practices must adapt to the diverse insurance landscape and government healthcare schemes popular in Maharashtra, such as the Mahatma Jyotiba Phule Jan Arogya Yojana. Misalignment with these schemes' billing requirements poses a financial risk, potentially leading to reimbursement delays.

Strategic Risks: Local healthcare reforms, such as the recent government initiative to increase public access to primary care in rural areas around Nagpur, impact our patient demographics. A strategic risk here involves anticipating and adapting to these shifts, ensuring our services remain aligned with community needs, especially in attracting and retaining patients who now have more healthcare options.

\[Slide 3: Conducting Risk Assessments\]

Ishita: Effective risk management starts with detailed assessments. Given our local context in Nagpur, this means understanding the unique health risks our patient population faces, assessing the stability of local suppliers, and staying abreast of regional healthcare policies. Our goal is to prioritize risks that could most impact our patient care and operational efficiency.

Ishita: "Effective risk management begins with comprehensive and methodical risk assessments. For Hope and Ayushman Hospitals, situated in the heart of Nagpur, this process is crucial and needs to be customized to our setting. Let's discuss specific methods we use to conduct these assessments:

- Health Risk Assessments (HRAs): We conduct HRAs to identify the most prevalent health conditions in our patient demographics, such as cardiovascular diseases and diabetes, which are common in Nagpur. This involves analyzing patient records, local health surveys, and collaborating with community health centers to gather data on regional health trends.
- Supplier Risk Evaluations: Given the logistical challenges, including those posed by Nagpur's monsoon season, we evaluate our suppliers on various criteria such as delivery reliability, quality of supplies, and financial stability. This is done through supplier audits, performance reviews, and setting up alternative supply chains as backups.
- Regulatory Compliance Tracking: To stay abreast of regional healthcare policies and ensure compliance, we utilize a combination of legal advisories and partnerships with healthcare associations like the Indian Medical Association’s Nagpur chapter. This helps us monitor and adapt to changes in healthcare laws and regulations affecting our operations.
- SWOT Analysis for Strategic Risks: To understand and plan for strategic risks, we conduct a SWOT (Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, Threats) analysis, focusing on how local healthcare reforms or shifts in patient population needs could impact us. This involves gathering insights from healthcare think tanks, patient feedback, and analyzing regional healthcare trends.
- Patient Feedback Systems: Implementing robust systems for collecting and analyzing patient feedback helps us identify clinical and operational risks from the patient’s perspective, enabling us to make patient-centered improvements.

\[Slide 4: Implementing Risk Management Strategies\]

Ishita: Addressing these risks requires tailored strategies. For clinical risks, we might focus on specialized training for staff on prevalent local health issues. To mitigate operational risks, diversifying our supplier base within Maharashtra could be key. These strategies are designed to minimize the impact on our operations and ensure continuous, high-quality patient care.

\[Slide 5: Insurance as a Risk Transfer Tool\]

Ishita: Insurance plays a crucial role in our risk management framework, serving as a financial safety net. In the context of Nagpur, we need to consider insurance solutions that cover local challenges, such as malpractice insurance that addresses the specific legal environment in India, and property insurance that considers the local climate and infrastructure conditions.

Ishita: "In the nuanced healthcare landscape of Nagpur, insurance isn't just a requirement—it's a strategic shield against the multifaceted risks we encounter. Let's break down how specific insurance solutions are tailored to address the unique challenges we face:

- Malpractice Insurance Customized for India's Legal Environment: Recognizing the rising incidences of medical litigation in India, we've tailored our malpractice insurance to offer comprehensive coverage that aligns with India's legal statutes and court precedents. This includes provisions for legal defense and potential settlements, ensuring that our healthcare professionals can focus on patient care without the looming fear of legal repercussions.
- Property Insurance with Emphasis on Local Climate Risks: Nagpur's climate, marked by hot summers and a significant monsoon season, poses unique risks to our hospital infrastructure. Our property insurance is designed to cover damages from natural events such as floods, which are crucial given our geographical vulnerability. This ensures financial stability and rapid recovery from any infrastructure damages caused by climate-related events.
- Supply Chain Interruption Insurance: Given our operational risks related to monsoon-induced supply chain disruptions, we've invested in supply chain interruption insurance. This policy is specifically structured to cover losses from delays or failures in receiving critical medical supplies, allowing us to maintain uninterrupted patient care even during adverse weather conditions.
- Cyber Liability Insurance: With the increasing reliance on digital health records and telemedicine platforms, cyber liability insurance has become indispensable. This coverage protects us from potential breaches of patient data, covering the costs associated with data recovery, legal fees, and any financial losses due to cyber-attacks. Considering the growing cyber threats in India, this insurance is crucial for safeguarding our patient data and maintaining trust.
- Business Interruption Insurance: This policy is particularly important for us, as it covers the loss of income that occurs when day-to-day operations are halted due to an insured event. It ensures that we can continue to meet our financial obligations, such as staff salaries and utility payments, even when our operations are temporarily disrupted.

Each of these insurance policies is a key part of our comprehensive risk management strategy, tailored to mitigate the specific risks associated with delivering healthcare in Nagpur. By carefully selecting and customizing these insurance solutions, we not only protect our financial assets but also ensure the sustainability of high-quality patient care amidst the myriad of risks we face."

* * *

\[Slide 6: Developing a Localized Insurance Strategy\]

Ishita: Our insurance strategy must reflect our specific needs and the unique risks of operating in Nagpur. This means choosing policies that offer the best protection for the common health issues we treat and ensuring coverage for risks posed by local weather patterns or infrastructure challenges. Regularly reviewing and adjusting this strategy is vital as our hospitals grow and the external environment changes.

\[Enhanced Slide 6: Crafting a Localized Insurance Strategy\]

Ishita: "Crafting a localized insurance strategy for our hospitals in Nagpur is more than just a regulatory requirement; it's a proactive measure to safeguard our mission of delivering exceptional healthcare. Let’s delve deeper into how we tailor our insurance strategy to meet the unique demands of our environment:

- Assessment of Local Health Risks: Given Nagpur’s health profile, with notable prevalence of cardiovascular diseases and diabetes, we prioritize health insurance products that cover treatments and procedures most in demand. This involves analyzing patient data to understand health trends and ensuring our insurance coverage reflects the services most needed by our community.
- Weather-Related Insurance Coverage: Nagpur's weather, particularly the monsoon season, presents specific risks to our operations. Our strategy includes comprehensive property and casualty insurance that specifically covers flood damage and other monsoon-related impacts. Additionally, we explore coverage options for indirect weather impacts, such as power outages that could affect our medical equipment and refrigeration of medications.
- Infrastructure and Technology Risks: Recognizing the challenges posed by infrastructure and technology in a rapidly growing city like Nagpur, our insurance strategy encompasses policies that protect against these risks. This includes coverage for equipment failure, which is crucial for our diagnostic and treatment technologies, and insurance against construction risks as we expand and upgrade our facilities.
- Regular Strategy Reviews: The healthcare landscape and local environment are constantly evolving. To ensure our insurance strategy remains aligned with our current needs and the external environment, we conduct semi-annual reviews. These reviews consider changes in local healthcare regulations, shifts in patient demographics, and any modifications in the regional risk landscape. We also stay in close communication with insurance providers to adjust our coverages as needed, ensuring optimal protection against emerging risks.
- Employee Health and Safety Coverage: Our employees are our most valuable asset. We extend our localized strategy to include comprehensive health insurance for our staff, taking into account the common health issues they face. Moreover, we ensure our policies provide robust coverage for workplace injuries, an essential factor in maintaining a healthy and motivated workforce.

By meticulously aligning our insurance strategy with the specific needs and risks of operating in Nagpur, we not only protect our physical and financial assets but also reinforce our commitment to providing uninterrupted, high-quality healthcare services. This localized approach ensures that both Hope and Ayushman Hospitals remain pillars of stability and care in the community, even in the face of unforeseen challenges."

\[Slide 7: Case Study: Risk Management in Action\]

Ishita: Let’s examine a case where Hope or Ayushman Hospital successfully mitigated a significant risk through proactive management and insurance. This real-life example will highlight the importance of understanding local risks and customizing our approach to insurance and risk management.

\[Enhanced Slide 7: Case Study - Risk Management in Action\]

Ishita: "Today, I want to share a compelling case study from our own backyard—how Ayushman Hospital successfully navigated a significant challenge through strategic risk management and insurance planning. This story not only demonstrates our resilience but also underscores the critical importance of a localized approach to risk management.

The Challenge:

In the summer of 2020, Ayushman Hospital faced an unprecedented risk when the early onset of the monsoon season threatened to flood the hospital premises. This was not just a potential infrastructure disaster but also posed a severe risk to the continuity of patient care, especially critical given the concurrent COVID-19 pandemic.

Proactive Risk Management:

Understanding the monsoon’s potential impact, the hospital had previously conducted a comprehensive risk assessment focusing on seasonal weather patterns. This assessment was part of our localized risk management strategy, recognizing Nagpur’s susceptibility to sudden and severe monsoon floods.

Customized Insurance Solution:

Leveraging insights from the risk assessment, Ayushman Hospital had secured a tailored property insurance policy covering flood damage, including not just the physical damages but also the operational disruptions. This policy was specifically designed with Nagpur’s monsoon patterns in mind, ensuring extensive coverage.

The Mitigation Strategy:

As the monsoon approached, Ayushman Hospital activated its emergency response plan, developed from the risk assessment findings. This plan included preemptive measures such as reinforcing flood defenses, securing critical medical supplies, and setting up emergency communication channels for patients and staff. Additionally, the hospital's administration engaged with the insurance provider to prepare for a potential claim process, ensuring all necessary documentation and procedures were in place.

Outcome:

The hospital’s premises experienced minor flooding, but thanks to the robust preparation and the swift activation of the emergency plan, patient care services were maintained without significant disruption. The insurance coverage facilitated a quick recovery, covering repair costs and operational losses during the recovery period.

Lessons Learned:

This experience reinforced the value of our localized risk management approach. By understanding the specific risks posed by our environment in Nagpur and customizing our insurance solutions accordingly, Ayushman Hospital not only protected its physical and financial assets but, most importantly, ensured the continuity of care for our community during a critical time.

Closing Thoughts:

This case study exemplifies how anticipation, preparation, and the right insurance strategy can turn potential crises into manageable situations. It’s a testament to our commitment to safeguarding our hospitals against local risks, ensuring that we continue to serve as beacons of health and safety in Nagpur."

* * *

\[Slide 8: Best Practices for Hope and Ayushman Hospitals\]

Ishita: To ensure the safety of our patients and the stability of our hospitals, here are some best practices:

- Regular, localized risk assessments.
- Creating a culture that prioritizes safety and encourages reporting of potential risks.
- Selecting insurance policies with our specific Nagpur context in mind.
- Continuous learning from local and global healthcare risk management trends.

\[Enhanced Slide 8: Best Practices in Risk Management and Insurance\]

Ishita: "In our quest to uphold the highest standards of patient care and maintain the operational integrity of Hope and Ayushman Hospitals, we have identified a set of core practices. These are not just guidelines but the foundation of our risk management strategy, especially crafted for the unique challenges and opportunities in Nagpur:

- Regular, Localized Risk Assessments: Understanding that the health and environmental landscape in Nagpur is ever-changing, we commit to conducting bi-annual risk assessments. These assessments are meticulously designed to identify new risks or changes in existing risks specific to our locale, such as seasonal health trends or monsoon-related infrastructural threats. Utilizing data analytics and insights from local health authorities, these assessments enable us to stay proactive and prepared.
- Fostering a Culture of Safety: We believe that a safe hospital is built on a culture of safety. This involves training our staff not only to adhere to the highest standards of patient care but also to be vigilant observers of their environment. We encourage open reporting of any potential risks, no matter how small they may seem, through an anonymous reporting system. Regular safety drills and workshops keep our team sharp and responsive to emergencies.
- Insurance Policies Tailored to Nagpur’s Context: Selecting the right insurance policies goes beyond the basics. For us, it means working closely with insurance providers to develop packages that address the specific risks associated with operating in Nagpur, from coverage for monsoon-related damages to cyber insurance that protects against digital threats prevalent in our region. This localized approach ensures that our coverage is both comprehensive and relevant.
- Continuous Learning and Adaptation: The field of healthcare risk management is dynamic, influenced by both local developments and global trends. We have instituted a continuous learning program for our risk management team, which includes attending international webinars, participating in workshops hosted by healthcare associations, and collaborating with global health institutions. This commitment to learning keeps us at the forefront of risk management practices, allowing us to integrate innovative solutions into our strategies.
- Community Engagement and Preparedness: Recognizing that our hospitals are part of a larger community, we engage in public health education and disaster preparedness initiatives within Nagpur. By hosting free workshops on health risk prevention and first aid, we not only contribute to a healthier community but also mitigate potential healthcare burdens following natural disasters or public health emergencies.

Implementing these best practices is not just about adhering to standards; it’s about actively creating a safer, more resilient healthcare environment for the people of Nagpur. By regularly assessing our risks, fostering a culture of safety, customizing our insurance solutions, and engaging in continuous learning, we ensure that Hope and Ayushman Hospitals are prepared to face both current and future challenges."

Thank you for your commitment to excellence and patient safety.

# Ayushman Specific rules:

Addressing Hygiene and Maintenance Concerns

1. Toilet Allocation and Cleanliness:

- Toilets should not be labeled exclusively as staff toilets. Ensure adequate facilities are available for all classes of patients, including educated professionals.
- Common toilets must be kept clean, and dedicated facilities should meet hygiene standards.

2. Improper Storage:

- Brooms and mops must not be stored inside the toilets. Allocate a proper storage area for cleaning equipment.

3. Storage Area Maintenance:

- The storage area must be cleaned and maintained regularly to prevent complaints.

Patient Care and Communication

4. Doctor Availability:

- Patients should be informed about the doctors responsible for their care. Any complaints about unavailability or delays in consultations must be addressed immediately.

5. Billing Updates:

- Bills for private and corporate patients must be updated promptly. This is a critical requirement to maintain trust and ensure smooth operations.

We are pleased to inform you that you have been appointed as a Billing Executive at Hope Hospital, effective from 21st feb 2025. You will be reporting to the Billing Manager and will be responsible for handling all billing and financial documentation related to patient services.

Your employment will be governed by the hospital’s standard policies and procedures, including those outlined in the Hope Hospital SOP & Induction Manual.

1. Designation: Billing Executive
2. Department: Financial and Billing Operations
3. Reporting To: Billing Manager / Hospital Administrator

* * *

### Job Description: Billing Executive

#### Department: Financial & Billing Operations

#### Location: Hope Hospital, Nagpur

#### Reports To: Billing Manager / Finance Director

#### Job Responsibilities:

1. Patient Billing & Documentation:

- Generate and process invoices for OPD, IPD, and emergency services.
- Verify patient details and treatment records before billing.
- Ensure correct inclusion of surgeon and physician visit charges.
- Update billing activities daily in the hospital software.

2. Cashless & TPA Billing:

- Process claims for cashless insurance (Ayushman Yojana, CGHS, ECHS, corporate empanelment).
- Coordinate with the TPA desk for approval and documentation.
- Follow-up on outstanding payments from insurance and corporate partners.

3. Billing Accuracy & Compliance:

- Verify hospital tariff for procedures, investigations, and consultation charges.
- Ensure accurate billing of medical implants and high-value consumables.
- Address patient inquiries regarding billing discrepancies and payment plans.

4. Coordination with Departments:

- Work closely with reception, accounts, RMOs, and consultants for seamless billing.
- Ensure all patient information is updated in the hospital software.
- Cross-check discharge summaries with final billing.

5. Financial Transactions & Record-Keeping:

- Maintain cash transactions, bank transfers, and online payment logs.
- Ensure proper handling of patient deposits, refunds, and payment receipts.
- Keep records of OPD and IPD billing for internal audits.

6. Software & Technology Use:

- Utilize hospital management software for billing and reporting.
- Update software issues or bugs to the IT team.
- Generate daily, weekly, and monthly billing reports.

7. Reporting & Compliance:

- Prepare daily reports on outstanding and pending patient bills.
- Send reminder mails and messages to recover outstanding from corporates
- Ensure billing compliance with NABH and hospital policies.
- Attend mandatory training sessions for billing accuracy and fraud prevention.

#### Key Skills Required:

- Technical Knowledge: Experience with hospital billing software.
- Accuracy & Detail-Oriented: Ensure zero billing errors.
- Communication: Interact with patients, doctors, and insurance providers professionally.
- Time Management: Prioritize tasks to ensure timely bill processing.
- Problem-Solving: Address billing discrepancies and patient grievances effectively.

#### Salary & Growth Opportunities:

- Salary as per hospital standards.
- Annual performance-based increments.
- Promotion opportunities in financial operations.

1 leader - 1 task

* * *

What is Elon Musk's 1 hour rule?

AI Overview

Elon Musk's "1-Hour Rule" is a strategy for deep, focused work: dedicate one hour daily - 10 to 11 am to tackle your most crucial, often postponed, task without distractions, fostering clear thinking, problem-solving, and intentional progress, moving from reactive chaos to proactive control. It involves creating a distraction-free environment, setting boundaries, and focusing on one thing that truly matters, like designing solutions or improving a core process, rather than just being busy.

How it Works

- Identify the Core Task: Determine the single most important thing you keep putting off (e.g., fixing a business process, strategic planning, deep learning).
- Create Boundaries: Declare this hour non-negotiable and tell others not to disturb you.
- Clear the Environment: Have only your main mission and necessary tools in front of you, eliminating all other stimuli.
- Focus Deeply: Use this hour for uninterrupted, high-level thinking and action on that one task, moving from reacting to designing.

Why It's Effective

- Shifts from Busy to Effective: It's not about working more, but about making hours better through deep focus.
- Builds Agency: It shifts your identity from reactive to deliberate, giving you control over your direction.
- Solves Big Problems: It creates space to think clearly and make tough decisions, rather than getting lost in minor tasks.

This technique is a cornerstone for managing intense workloads and achieving strategic breakthroughs by prioritizing deep work over constant busyness, a method applicable to anyone, not just tech titans.

कार्यालय सूचना: लीडरशिप टीम को दिए गए अधिकार

# कार्यालय सूचना: लीडरशिप टीम को दिए गए अधिकार

# तारीख: 24 सितंबर 2025   प्रेषित: सभी कंसल्टेंट्स, RMO, नर्सिंग, बिलिंग, फ्रंट ऑफिस, टेक्नीशियन, हाउसकीपिंग एवं सिक्योरिटी   प्रेषक: चेयरमैन एवं मैनेजिंग डायरेक्टर

## उद्देश्य

# लीडरशिप टीम को सशक्त बनाना ताकि हम 75 इन-पेशेंट के तात्कालिक ऑक्युपेंसी लक्ष्य को प्राप्त कर सकें, साथ ही सभी स्तरों पर पेशेवर आचरण और सम्मान सुनिश्चित हो।

## प्रदत्त अधिकार (तुरंत प्रभाव से)

1. # स्टाफिंग (नियुक्ति, तैनाती, हटाना)


- # लीडरशिप टीम (President, VP, ST, LGH, तथा MCom कोऑर्डिनेटर्स) को अधिकार है कि वे:


- # स्क्रीनिंग/इंटरव्यू करें, जॉइनिंग निर्देश जारी करें, तथा दैनिक ऑक्युपेंसी आवश्यकताओं के अनुसार शिफ्ट/यूनिट में तैनाती/पुनर्तैनाती करें।

- # नॉन-रिपोर्टिंग/अनुपस्थित कर्मियों को ड्यूटी रोस्टर से हटाएँ और HR नियमों के अनुरूप अनुशासनात्मक कार्रवाई प्रारम्भ करें (जैसे 3 दिन नो-शो → रोस्टर से हटाना), तथा आवश्यकता होने पर HR/CMD को टर्मिनेशन की सिफारिश करें।

- # जहाँ सेवाओं की कमी से एडमिशन/डिस्चार्ज फ्लो प्रभावित हो, वहाँ तत्काल प्रतिस्थापन/अतिरिक्त स्टाफ की सिफारिश करें।


2. # प्रदर्शन-आधारित कार्रवाई (ऑक्युपेंसी हेतु)


- # जब कोई कर्मचारी/टीम ऑक्युपेंसी लक्ष्य को सपोर्ट नहीं कर रही हो (जैसे एडमिशन/डिस्चार्ज में देरी, अधूरी डॉक्यूमेंटेशन, OPD→IPD कन्वर्ज़न में सहयोग की कमी), तो लीडरशिप टीम सुधारात्मक कदम उठाएगी।

- # ऑक्युपेंसी एक घोषित मैनेजमेंट KPI है; दैनिक/साप्ताहिक ट्रैकिंग और बेड-उपयोग संबंधी कार्रवाइयाँ अनिवार्य हैं।

- # संगठन का रणनीतिक बेंचमार्क 75% ऑक्युपेंसी लक्ष्य ही रहेगा।


3. # वित्तीय अधिकार: दैनिक संचालन निधि


- # लीडरशिप टीम को ₹5,000 प्रतिदिन (प्रति अस्पताल) की कंटिजेंसी निधि प्रदान की जाती है, जिसे ऑक्युपेंसी से सीधे जुड़ी आवश्यकताओं पर खर्च किया जाएगा (जैसे छोटे-मोटे रिपेयर, लिनेन, मरीज सुविधाएँ, रेफरल लॉजिस्टिक्स, प्रिंटिंग, छोटे विक्रेता खर्च)।

- # सभी बिल/वाउचर संलग्न करते हुए दैनिक लॉग बनाएँ; मासिक समेकन हेतु जमा करें। CMD द्वारा पश्च-स्वीकृति (ratification) लागू होगी।


## संचालन अनुशासन

- # सुबह/शिफ्ट हडल्स और 3-मिनट रिपोर्टिंग सभी इंचार्ज और लीडरशिप रिपोर्टिंग लाइन्स के लिए अनिवार्य हैं।

- # वित्तीय एवं संचालन रिपोर्टिंग मरीज-वार रिकन्सिलिएशन और इंटीग्रेटेड लेजर प्रथाओं के अनुसार होगी।


## सम्मान एवं आचरण (नॉन-नेगोशिएबल)

- # सभी कर्मचारी लीडरशिप टीम के निर्देशों के साथ पूर्ण सहयोग करें और सम्मानजनक व्यवहार रखें। लीडरशिप के प्रति अपमान, तंज, या सार्वजनिक आलोचना स्वीकार्य नहीं है।

- # यही सम्मानजनक संस्कृति मरीजों व परिजनों के साथ भी हर समय बनी रहनी चाहिए।


## पर्यवेक्षण

- # ये अधिकार CMD द्वारा प्रत्यायोजित हैं; HR की विधि-प्रक्रिया एवं अस्पताल नीतियाँ यथावत लागू रहेंगी। नियुक्ति और टर्मिनेशन पर अंतिम अधिकार निदेशकों/CMD का रहेगा, जो किसी भी निर्णय की समीक्षा कर सकते हैं।


# आइए, तात्कालिकता, एकजुटता और शिष्टाचार के साथ आज की ऑक्युपेंसी प्राप्त करें और प्रतिदिन उत्कृष्टता बनाए रखें।

# Office Note: Delegated Powers to the Hospital Leadership Team

Date: 24 September 2025

To: All Consultants, RMOs, Nursing, Billing, Front Office, Technicians, Housekeeping & Security

From: Chairman & Managing Director

## Purpose

To empower the Leadership Team to deliver our immediate occupancy target of 75 in-patients, while ensuring professional conduct and respect at all times.

## Delegated Powers (with immediate effect)

1. Staffing (Appointment, Deployment, Removal)


- The Leadership Team (President, VP, ST, LGH, with MCom coordinators) is empowered to:


- Conduct screenings and interviews, issue joining instructions, and deploy/redeploy staff across shifts/units to meet daily occupancy needs, in line with the existing practice that departmental interviews are led by the in-charge and overseen by CMD.

- Remove non-reporting/absent staff from the duty roster and initiate disciplinary action per HR norms (e.g., 3 days no-show → removal from roster), and recommend termination to HR/CMD where required.

- Recommend additions/replacements where service gaps affect admissions and discharge flow.


2. Performance Action for Occupancy


- The Leadership Team will take corrective action when any staff member/team is not supporting the occupancy goal (e.g., delayed admissions/discharges, incomplete documentation, poor OPD→IPD conversion support).

- Occupancy is a stated management KPI; daily/weekly tracking and bed-utilization actions are mandatory.

- Our strategic benchmark remains the organization’s occupancy targets framework (ref. “Goal Setting for Achieving 75% Occupancy”).


3. Financial Authority: Daily Operational Fund


- A contingency fund of ₹5,000 per day per hospital is entrusted to the Leadership Team for immediate, occupancy-linked needs (e.g., small repairs, linens, patient amenities, referral logistics, printing, minor vendor items). This aligns with the President’s approval limit of ₹5,000, subject to subsequent CMD ratification. Maintain bills/vouchers and a daily log for monthly consolidation.


## Operating Discipline

- Morning/shift huddles and 3-minute reporting continue to be compulsory for in-charges and leadership reporting lines.

- Financial & operational reporting must follow the existing patient-wise reconciliation and integrated-ledger practices.


## Respect & Conduct (Non-Negotiable)

- All staff must cooperate with and respect Leadership Team directives. No insults, sarcasm, or public criticism toward leadership will be tolerated. Our culture requires professional, patient-centric teamwork and positive communication in meetings and WhatsApp groups.

- This respectful culture extends to patients and visitors at all times.


## Oversight

- These powers are delegated by the CMD; HR due process and hospital policies remain applicable. The Directors/CMD retain final authority on appointments and terminations and may review any decision.


Let us act with urgency, unity, and courtesy to achieve today’s occupancy and sustain excellence daily.

escalation

# Escalation - Channel for Issues & Feedback (No Direct Approach to Directors)

Date: 25 September 2025

To: All Consultants, RMOs, Nursing, Billing, Front Office, Technicians, Housekeeping & Security – Hope Hospital & Ayushman Nagpur Hospital

From: Chairman & Managing Director

## Policy (Effective Immediately)

1. No direct approach to Directors:

    Staff must not approach the CMD/Directors directly for operational issues, requests, or feedback.

2. Mandatory channel – Leadership Team:

    All matters must go first to the Hospital Leadership Team (LT): President → Vice President → Secretary-Treasurer → LGH/In-charges.

3. Reporting Pathway (Who to contact first):


- Unit/Department staff → Respective In-Charge

- If unresolved in a shift/day → LGH / VP

- If still unresolved within 48 hours → President

- President consolidates and escalates to Group President/CMD as needed.


4. WhatsApp & Logs:


- Use designated official WhatsApp groups to post issues and updates (no personal DMs to Directors).

- Each issue must include: Unit, brief description, time, action taken, and current status.

- Maintain a simple Issue Log (Date \| Unit \| Issue \| Owner \| ETA \| Status \| Escalation level).


5. Turnaround Expectations:


- Minor issues: within 24–48 hours

- Critical patient-safety/clinical risk: immediately to In-Charge → President (with parallel entry in Issue Log).


6. Respect & Conduct:


- All communication with LT must be professional and respectful.

- Public arguments, sarcasm, or bypassing the channel will invite disciplinary action.


7. Exceptions (Permitted Direct Escalation):


- Whistle-blowing (fraud, harassment, severe misconduct).

- Life-threatening emergencies where delay risks patient safety.

   In these rare cases, inform the President simultaneously and document in the Issue Log.


8. Consequences for Bypassing:


- First instance: Written advisory.

- Repeat: Disciplinary action per HR policy.


## Leadership Team Contacts

## President: Aman Brother

- Vice President:Kashish
- Secretary-Treasurer: Abhishek
- LGH: Anas


Please align all communications to this channel. This ensures swift resolution, accountability, and uninterrupted progress toward our 75 in-patient occupancy goal.

— Chairman & Managing Director

1. डायरेक्टर्स से सीधे संपर्क वर्जित है।

2. सभी विषय पहले लीडरशिप टीम (President → VP → ST → LGH/इंचार्ज) को भेजे जाएँ।

3. रिपोर्टिंग क्रम: स्टाफ → इंचार्ज → (48 घंटे में न सुलझे) LGH/VP → (फिर) President → (आवश्यकतानुसार) Group President/CMD।

4. व्हाट्सएप/लॉग: केवल आधिकारिक ग्रुप में मुद्दे पोस्ट करें; Issue Log में तारीख, विभाग, समस्या, उत्तरदायी, ETA, स्थिति, एस्कलेशन दर्ज करें।

5. TAT: सामान्य मुद्दे 24–48 घंटे; मरीज-सुरक्षा जोखिम तुरंत इंचार्ज/President को।

7. अपवाद: व्हिसलब्लोइंग/गंभीर आपात स्थिति—President को साथ-साथ अवगत कराएँ और लॉग भरें।


— चेयरमैन एवं प्रबंध निदेशक

### Standard Operating Procedures: RMO Induction & Hospital Protocols

#### 1\. RMO Induction

All new Resident Medical Officers (RMOs) and staff members must be provided with a comprehensive contact list upon joining. This list must include:

- Contact details for all OT (Operation Theater) Staff. \- Hope In charge - Apeksha 8605104628, Pankaj 9604347371
- Contact details for commonly visiting Surgeons and anaesthetists - . Dr Pranam Sadawarte 7276771181, etc..

#### 2\. Handover Protocols[New RMO handover format hope](https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1QxOOz7fxscYBE9sK26CrvZTMwB-vEwSKfU6uK2_1w5I/edit?gid%3D0%23gid%3D0&sa=D&source=editors&ust=1779089182138532&usg=AOvVaw1h3XcE0ekxM8qknIMcjC6_)

- Mandatory Written Record: Verbal handovers are strictly insufficient. To ensure patient safety and continuity of care, all RMO handovers must be documented in writing using the proper hospital format.

#### 3\. Operation Theater (OT) Coordination

- Posting Schedule: The OT schedule must be posted at least 24 hours prior to the procedure.
- RMO Responsibilities: Once the schedule is posted, the RMO is responsible for calling the Surgeon and OT staff 2 hours before the surgery to coordinate the final plan.
- Sterilization Check: The RMO and nursing staff must confirm that all necessary equipment, instruments, and implants are autoclaved (sterilized) and ready for the procedure.

#### 4\. Admission & Treatment Rules

- Consultant Visit: Upon a patient's admission, the Consultant is required to visit the patient within 30 minutes to ensure the treatment plan is initiated immediately.

#### 5\. Diagnostic Reporting (Labs & Imaging)

- Processing: As soon as MRI, CT scans, or Pathology reports are received by the hospital, they must be processed immediately.
- Communication Protocol: The RMO is required to share these findings with the Consultant and the patient's relatives within 30 minutes of receiving the reports.

Here is the revised Referral Policy document we need to discuss

Referral Policy: Private Patients

1\. Deductions Before calculating the referral amount, the following charges must be deducted from the total bill:

Consultation: Deduct 100% of charges.

Laboratory: Deduct 75% of charges of billed amount

Radiology: Deduct 75% of chargesof billed amount.

Outsource Services (Surgeon & Anesthetist): Deduct 100% of actual charges as per the bill.

Implants: Deduct 100% of actual implant charges as per the bill.

Medicine: Deduct 100% of medicine charges.

2\. Referral Calculation Rules Referral amounts are calculated on the net amount remaining after the deductions listed above:

Standard Rate: The referral is calculated at 20% of the net amount (after deductions).

Bills Below ₹1,25,000: The referral amount is strictly 20% of the net amount.

Bills Above ₹1,25,000: The referral amount is capped at a maximum of ₹25,000.

Payment Cap: The total approved payment cannot exceed ₹2,00,000.

Referral Policy: Yojna (Scheme) Patients

1\. General Guidelines

This policy applies only to approved Yojna patients.

Standard Referral: Generally calculated at 10%, but subject to the fixed amounts below.

2\. Fixed Amounts

Maximum Payout: ₹5,000.

Minimum Payout: ₹2,000

. Special Categories

Conservative Medical Management: Requires an approval amount of ₹25,000 for calculating referral.

Package Amount Exceptions: If the package amount is high and the requested referral exceeds ₹5,000, the case must be discussed with Dr. M.

Major Surgeries: For major surgeries (e.g., Angioplasty, Jejunostomy, THR, large package spine or Ortho) involving significant outsource costs (Surgeon, Stent, Medicine), the maximum referral paid is ₹5,000.
